<!-- section 1 (id=3577, raw_sort=1): عقل اور توحید -->
## Intellect and Tawḥīd

A distinction must be drawn between intellect (ʿaql) and reasoning. The intellect is the name of an infinite faculty that can transcend this mortal world, ascend to the spiritual realm, and grasp the realities found there. Reasoning, by contrast, is a finite force that moves from one subject to another by logic and operates only within the domain of mental conception. By the light of intellect a human being apprehends absolute realities; through reasoning those same realities can be approached only in part. Reasoning is the servant of the intellect — an instrument that the intellect deploys as need requires.

Absolute reality is that which simply *is* — the Qurʾān, for example.

### Intentions and Actions

At the moment when the Battle of the Camel was about to begin, a Bedouin came forward to the Commander of the Faithful and asked, "O ʿAlī, do you say that God is one?" The bystanders tried to silence him, insisting that the battlefield was no place for such a question. Mawlānā ʿAlī (peace be upon him) instructed them to let the man speak: "This man wishes to know — and it is precisely for this knowledge that we fight, so that people may know." With this single utterance he established the priority of intention over outward act and taught that the knowledge of Absolute Truth and its oneness is the purpose of every action, irrespective of its outward form, whether worship, the recitations of *tasbīḥ*, or war itself. The fact is that ⟪ar:توحید رب العزت،⟫ the tawḥīd (divine oneness) of the Lord of Glory was the intention behind every outward act of ʿAlī (peace be upon him). His phrase "so that people may know" reveals that the real motive behind every intention, thought, and movement — whether on a battlefield or in a mosque — is ⟪ar:علم⟫ knowledge. The question of God's oneness is therefore permissible at every time and in every place. In ʿAlī's lifetime the three battles — ⟪ar:جمل⟫ (Jamal), ⟪ar:نحروان⟫ (Nahrawān), and ⟪ar:صفین⟫ (Ṣiffīn) — were fought in response to this very question. As the Messenger of God (peace be upon him and his family) had said, "O ʿAlī, you will fight for the taʾwīl (esoteric exegesis) of the Qurʾān as I have fought for its revelation."[^cite-1]

### The Unity of al-Ḥaqq

On the same battlefield ʿAlī delivered a remarkable sermon on the divine oneness. He explained to the Bedouin that it is not permissible to call God "one" in the sense of number and enumeration, for that which has no parallel cannot be drawn into any tally. He has no equal — He is ⟪ar:لا ثانی⟫ ("without a second") — and not merely that He has no partner, but that there can be nothing resembling Him at all.

He is ⟪ar:’الحق المبین‘⟫ "the Manifest Truth": beyond all that is in the universe, yet manifest to all things; at once inaccessible and unavoidable. By this teaching ʿAlī made plain to those of insight that He is not "one God" set against many gods, but ⟪ar:الحق⟫ al-Ḥaqq alone is the only reality, and all else is mere semblance and deception.

> **Notes ·**
> In Arabic, the word *āya* means *sign*. Each sign points to the one who made the mark. Hoofprints in the sand are an āya of the horse's existence and its presence in that place; smoke is an āya of fire.

Everything that exists is fashioned as ⟪ar:’آیت‘⟫ "a sign" of the existence of ⟪ar:’ھو‘⟫ "He" — a token and a proof that points back to His presence. This is precisely the meaning of ⟪ar:تاویل⟫ taʾwīl: "that which returns a thing to its origin." He is the First and the Last, the Outward and the Inward; every outward multiplicity returns to His ⟪ar:’وحدانیت‘⟫ "oneness" and to His ⟪ar:’أحدیت‘⟫ "uniqueness," as God Most High says:

> ⟪quran 41:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ ‎⟫
> *&nbsp;We will show them Our Signs in the universe, and in their ownselves, until it becomes manifest to them that this (the Quran) is the truth. Is it not sufficient in regard to your Lord that He is a Witness over all things?*
> We will show them Our signs in the world and in their own souls until it becomes clear to them that it is the truth. Is it not sufficient that their Lord is a witness over all things?
> — **Quran 41:53 (inline widget)**

In this verse God uses the plurals "Our Signs" and "their souls," but for the Truth He employs the singular together with the definite article ⟪ar:ال⟫ — indicating that the multiplicity of all the signs of cosmos and soul return to one Truth which is One.[^cite-2]

Within the human being there is a restlessness, a movement, that draws us toward the bliss of oneness — the necessity of striving always for that bliss.

Jung

### Qurʾān and Interpretation

For this reason the Qurʾān is one, but each verse admits multiple interpretations.

> **Interpretation ·**
> Likewise, ʿAlī is one, and the Imāms among his descendants — who have become "signs" of him — are many.

⟪ar:امام جعفر الصادق علیہ السلام⟫ once said to one of his companions, "If I wished, I could give you seventy interpretations of every verse of the Qurʾān." God taught ⟪ar:محمد مصطفی صلی اللہ علیہ و آلہ و سلم⟫ the taʾwīl of the Qurʾān, the Prophet in turn taught it to ʿAlī, and then he declared, ⟪ar-quote:علی مع القرآن و القرآن مع العلی⟫ — "ʿAlī is with the Qurʾān and the Qurʾān is with ʿAlī." ʿAlī himself said to ʿAbbās that were he to disclose the taʾwīl of ⟪ar:سورۃ الفاتحۃ⟫ alone, seventy camels would be required to bear the volumes. ʿAlī is the true interpreter of the Qurʾān.[^cite-3]

> **Interpretation ·**
> The Qurʾān is a book written between two covers. These two covers are Muḥammad and ʿAlī, and all the pages in between refer to the Imāms (peace be upon them) who are their descendants.

### Reason, Revelation, and Spirit

The revelation of God — the Book of the Qurʾān — is ⟪ar:’صامت‘⟫ "silent" and does not speak in its own tongue. It requires an interpreter to disclose its meaning: ⟪ar:لا بُدَّ لَہُ مِن تَرجُماَن⟫ — "It must have a translator." So too, in order to understand the divine messages of ⟪ar:وحی⟫ (revelation), an interpreter or envoy is required: this is ⟪ar:عقل⟫ (intellect). The bond between them is made plain by the Prophet's saying, ⟪ar-quote:رسول الرجل ترجمان عقلہ⟫ — "A man's messenger is the interpreter of his intellect." The messenger is sent by the intellect itself.

This is why every word of Mawlānā ʿAlī mirrors the Qurʾān. Each of his utterances passes from the words of the Qurʾān to its revelation, from the revelation to its spirit, and from the spirit to the One who reveals it. His statements return the words of the Qurʾān, through all these stages, to their origin and source — ⟪ar:عقل اول⟫ al-ʿAql al-Awwal (the First Intellect). The One who revealed this word — ⟪ar:’الہ‘⟫ "the God" — is therefore at once hidden within ʿAlī's utterances (in their meaning) and made manifest through their words. He is ⟪ar:’حق‘⟫ the Real. He cannot be grasped or described; only through the impressions of His creations can His existence and self-disclosure be acknowledged.

*power hierarchies — giving children power over parents; power imbalance*

| The Revelation | Discount | Interpretation |
| --- | --- | --- |
| First Mind | Mohammed | Ali |
| The Revelation of the Qur'an | Words of the Qur'an | The Meaning of the Qur'an |
| Allah | Revelation | Mind |

Revelation and intellect appear, on the surface, to be two distinct realities, which scholars divide into two opposed categories:

| Revelation | Mind |
| --- | --- |
| Convention Tradition | Nature |
| Imitation Imitation | Research Verification |
| Piety | Get Inquiry |

In reality, however, the two are intimate to one another. There is complementarity between them; each completes the other. These two distinct realities together compose a single object — and that single object is the very purpose of ⟪ar:توحید⟫ (tawḥīd), since ⟪ar:’توحید‘⟫ literally means "to make one." A parallel may be drawn with the emergence of a truth through the conjunction of negation and affirmation: if it is true that Aḥmad has one goat, the truth is secured only by also denying that he has two.

The combination of intellect and revelation — that to which the "one" reality points — is the ⟪ar:’روح‘⟫ (spirit) that stands between them. The intellect, by itself and without the spirit, is limited in its scope and cannot stand against revelation. But the spirit, which is the driver of this intellect, is unlimited in its scope. Only the spirit can receive the messages of revelation, become conscious of them, and test their elevated quality. The spirit receives revelation and conveys it to the intellect, and the intellect then processes and refines it. Were this not so, revelation would have been reduced to a name for innumerable rules and regulations imposed upon the human will, rather than a creative inspiration for the intellect.

> — *Image text (from image 001; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at .. /images/001.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Revelation, which is multidimensional, cannot be confined to a single dimension of words. The Messenger of God (peace be upon him and his family) clothed the revelation of God in words so that spirituality could take on a corporeal nature and the human being could see, hear, and read it with the five senses. Here the bond between revelation and intellect is forged: rather than confining meaning within words, the intellect frees meaning from the confinement of words. Through it, the outward face of words yields countless streams of inner meaning — as in the story of Moses, who struck the stone with his staff (the intellect) and twelve springs of meaning gushed forth.

> ⟪quran 2:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَإِذِ ٱسْتَسْقَىٰ مُوسَىٰ لِقَوْمِهِۦ فَقُلْنَا ٱضْرِب بِّعَصَاكَ ٱلْحَجَرَ ۖ فَٱنفَجَرَتْ مِنْهُ ٱثْنَتَا عَشْرَةَ عَيْنًۭا ۖ قَدْ عَلِمَ كُلُّ أُنَاسٍۢ مَّشْرَبَهُمْ ۖ كُلُوا۟ وَٱشْرَبُوا۟ مِن رِّزْقِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا تَعْثَوْا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ مُفْسِدِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when Musa (Moses) asked for water for his people, We said: "Strike the stone with your stick." Then gushed forth therefrom twelve springs. Each (group of) people knew its own place for water. "Eat and drink of that which Allah has provided and do not act corruptly, making mischief on the earth." *
> When Moses prayed for water for his people, We said, 'Strike the rock with your staff.' Thereupon twelve springs gushed forth from it, and each tribe knew its drinking-place. Eat and drink of God's provision, and do not act corruptly on the earth, making mischief.
> — **Quran 2:60 (inline widget)**

The greater the talent and refinement of the spirit, the more it can grasp the content of revelation and the more pearls of high meaning it draws from this single shell. The intellect is the inner messenger — the inner consciousness — through which a person can empirically affirm and verify the divine messages of revelation. Were this not so, the human soul would be forced to receive revelation only by dogmatic submission.

For this reason the Commander of the Faithful told Kumayl that one of the reasons for the sending of God's prophets was to disclose the hidden treasures of the intellect.[^cite-4] The intellect is enlivened and awakened by revelation. Revelation, in truth, is a voice that reaches into the spiritual depths of the intellect, awakening the seeds of consciousness that God sowed in it on the eternal day, and bringing those seeds to flower. Revelation cannot be obtained from anything other than the intellect, and the treasures hidden beneath the soil of the intellect cannot be revealed except by revelation. From this perspective there is an eternal bond between intellect and revelation, such that the two may be described as analogous — or at least the intellect may be said to be a form of revelation.

> — *Image text (from image 002; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at .. /images/002.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Mawlānā ʿAlī's teaching — in which he names the disclosure of the intellect's hidden treasures as the reason for the sending of the prophets — proves that the spiritual intellect of any human being cannot be ignorant of the message of revelation but rather recognizes it, because God's message accords with the very essence of intellect. Since the two share a common origin, the intellect recognizes the source and origin of revelation as the ⟪ar:’الہ الحقیقی‘⟫ "True God." The divine messages of the prophets awaken the intellect, and so these messages cannot be regarded as separate from the intellect; rather they are its real purpose and end. The ⟪ar:’روح‘⟫ (spirit) is meant to receive these divine messages through the intellect and assimilate them into itself in such a way that the two become one. When that happens, the heart becomes able to "see" God. God cannot be seen with the eyes, only through the heart — and this is what the Commander of the Faithful called ⟪ar:’حق الیقین‘⟫ ḥaqq al-yaqīn (the truth of certainty).

<!-- section 2 (id=3599, raw_sort=2): عقل اور استدلال کا فرق -->

## The Distinction between Intellect and Reasoning

Between the faculty of intellect and the faculty of inference (istidlāl, reasoning) there obtains a kind of continuity, and yet, in another sense, the two stand quite apart. The continuity lies in the fact that every thought and every idea begins from a meaningful concept, and the power of inference yields ideas that are logical and grounded in reality. It proceeds by way of ⟪ar:مفارقۃ⟫ (mufāraqa, distinction or separation), ⟪ar:تناقض⟫ (tanāqud, antinomy), ⟪ar:نفی⟫ (nafy, negation), and ⟪ar:اثبات⟫ (ithbāt, affirmation), and through these instruments it draws out the treasures latent in the intellect. There is, however, a horizon beyond which this thinking cannot pass. Its boundaries are tethered to physical matters, and it cannot enter the spiritual realm. To cross into that realm the intellect needs an external guide — revelation (⟪ar:’وحی‘⟫, waḥy) — and an internal messenger, which is the intellect itself (⟪ar:’عقل‘⟫, ʿaql, intellect). Through this companionship the intellect steps into the precinct of the spiritual.

Therefore, when Mawlānā ʿAlī refuses the concepts attached to the word "god" (⟪ar:’الہ‘⟫, ilāh), he refuses them on account of the poverty and weakness of inferential power. The denial of those concepts is the very threshold at which the consciousness latent in the intellect — a consciousness beyond the reach of unaided reason — begins to stir and to be drawn forth. The negation of every finite human image becomes, in this way, the very basis for the confession of an infinite divinity. It is a negation that lifts upward, not one that drags down. This dialectic of negation and affirmation appears in his praise of God preserved in ⟪ar:نہج البلاغۃ⟫ (Nahj al-Balāgha), where he says:

| {{IMG_URL:.. /images/quote_open.gif}} Praise be to Allah, whose praise is not attained by those who say, and whose blessings are not counted, and whose diligent people do not perform His duty, who does not realize it after determination, and who does not attain the diving of understanding, whose attribute has no limit, no adjective, no limited time, and no extended time. He created the creatures by His power, and He spread the winds by His mercy, and He swallowed the field of IMG_URL His land with rocks. /images/quote_closed.gif}} |
| --- |

In this saying of the Commander of the Faithful — and in many others like it — the paradox is plain. God is the One praised, yet He cannot be adequately praised. His blessings are present, yet they cannot be counted, though all else can be enumerated. The fulfilment of His right is incumbent upon us, yet that right cannot be fulfilled. Such paradoxical obligations recur throughout his discourses.

The divine attributes admit of no bound — ⟪ar:لیس لصفاتہ حد محدود⟫ — and yet they cannot be left undescribed, for they truly are. The Qurʾān itself describes God as Generous (⟪ar:’کریم‘⟫, karīm), Mighty (⟪ar:’عزیز‘⟫, ʿazīz), and Merciful (⟪ar:’رحیم‘⟫, raḥīm); yet Mawlānā ʿAlī insists that none of these attributes can be circumscribed. God is generous — but by what measure? Whose generosity sets the standard: mine, yours, his, theirs?

He says: "Sincerity (⟪ar:أخلاص⟫, ikhlāṣ) is the negation of every attribute from God." On the one hand we must acknowledge the divine attributes; on the other we must deny them. The difficulty is precisely this: the human mind, in order to think of God at all, leans upon these attributive words; but ʿAlī sweeps away those very supports and leaves us no easy purchase upon the divine concept. If the attributes are the only conceptual handles we have, and yet we must negate them, what is a person to do? Out of this contradiction of affirmation and negation a new and deeper register of knowledge emerges. The hidden treasures of the intellect are awakened, and the human being is compelled to recognise that the knowledge of God exceeds every faculty of thought, conception, reasoning, and inference — something only the soul can sense, though the intellect alone cannot grasp it. "My Lord," he says, "cannot be confined within dimensions, motion, time, or place; He is subtle, but not in the manner of subtle bodies; magnificent, but not in the manner of magnitude; great, but not in the manner of stature."

Here once again he both affirms the attributes and denies them. God is the owner of these attributes, but He cannot be imprisoned in them, nor reduced to our imaginings. The attributes furnish the intellect with a measure of concept, but the concept they yield is weak and partial; and so, to acknowledge the perfection of those attributes, one must negate them, since every concept carries the defect of finitude. It is from the conjunction of the dimensions of negation and the dimensions of affirmation that the depth of true knowledge is created. Yet that depth cannot stand unless we acknowledge that neither dimension — neither the negative nor the positive — is in itself adequate to reflect the picture accurately. To deny every attribute is in truth to confess the infinity of His essence, which is the genuine import of the testimony of sincerity (⟪ar:کلمۃ اخلاص، لا الہ الا اللہ⟫).[^cite-5] For any concept to be established in the human mind, a closed definition is required; and where there is definition, there are limits and exclusions. But the definition of the divine attributes is free of every such limitation, for they are the infinite attributes of an infinite essence. In one sense, then, we may place every attribute in the position of negation within the kalimat al-ikhlāṣ and recite: ⟪ar:⟪ar:’لا رحمن الا اللہ‘⟫ (lā raḥmān illā Allāh), ⟪ar:’لا عظیم الا اللہ‘⟫ (lā ʿaẓīm illā Allāh), ⟪ar:’لا کریم الا اللہ‘⟫ (lā karīm illā Allāh), and so on. In this way the apparent negation of every attribute becomes the very affirmation of its true identity. These attributes are not extrinsic adjuncts fastened upon His essence; they are constitutive of that essence, and can be distinguished only through the conceptual operation that belongs to ⟪ar:’علم الوجود‘⟫ (ʿilm al-wujūd, the science of being).[^cite-6] For just this reason God Himself says:

> ⟪quran 23:91⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَا ٱتَّخَذَ ٱللَّهُ مِن وَلَدٍۢ وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُۥ مِنْ إِلَهٍ ۚ إِذًۭا لَّذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهٍۭ بِمَا خَلَقَ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَىٰ بَعْضٍۢ ۚ سُبْحَنَ ٱللَّهِ عَمَّا يَصِفُونَ ‎⟫
> *No son (or offspring or children) did Allah beget, nor is there any ilah (god) along with Him; (if there had been many gods), behold, each god would have taken away what he had created, and some would have tried to overcome others! Glorified be Allah above all that they attribute to Him!*
> Allah has not begotten a son, nor is there any god besides Him; if there were, each god would have taken away what he had created, and some of them would have risen above others. Glory be to Allah, that which they describe.
> — **Quran 23:91 (inline widget)**

The infinity of God deserves to be freed from every imagined constraint, but the heart is not incapable of knowing Him. With its own organ of vision the heart can see Him. The heart has always been the seat of rational thought and wisdom, and the intellect has always required it for its own refinement. The remembrance of God (⟪ar:’ذکر اللہ‘⟫, dhikr Allāh) is in truth the very source of the intellect's purity, and it is for this reason that ʿAlī says, "The remembrance of God is the most excellent form of worship." Yet here too a paradox confronts us: the reality of remembrance (⟪ar:ذکر⟫, dhikr) is not attained unless the worshipper "loses" himself within it. To be lost here is not the cessation of intellect but the dissolution of the soul in the remembrance of God — what is called annihilation in God (⟪ar:’فنا بااللہ‘⟫, fanāʾ bi-Allāh).

The intellect is the name of a spiritual capacity; the soul is its origin and the very cause of its life. Without the intellect the soul becomes an unconscious thing; without the true soul the intellect inclines toward inanimate thought. God says:

> ⟪quran 32:7-9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِىٓ أَحْسَنَ كُلَّ شَىْءٍ خَلَقَهُۥ ۖ وَبَدَأَ خَلْقَ ٱلْإِنسَنِ مِن طِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ جَعَلَ نَسْلَهُۥ مِن سُلَلَةٍۢ مِّن مَّآءٍۢ مَّهِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةَ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Who made everything He has created good, and He began the creation of man from clay. Then He made his offspring from semen of worthless water (male and female sexual discharge). Then He fashioned him in due proportion, and breathed into him the soul (created by Allah for that person), and He gave you hearing (ears), sight (eyes) and hearts. Little is the thanks you give!*
> Who created all that He created, and He originated man from clay, then He made his progeny from an abject fluid, then He fashioned his fragments, and breathed into him of His spirit, and made for you hearing, and sight, and hearts. Little thanks do you give!
> — **Quran 32:7-9 (inline widget)**

The breathing of the spirit (⟪ar:’نفخ الروح‘⟫, nafkh al-rūḥ) is what brings life and consciousness into being. If the spirit is not granted its due, such a life is itself a kind of death. It is through this spirit that static things are animated, and through it that unconscious objects are roused into awareness. Through this divine spirit a person comes to know not only the realities about him but his own self as well. From the conjunction of this "being" and this "knowing" every spiritual concept is established. When this spirit is joined to the body, the body lives, and knowledge revives it, as God says:

> ⟪quran 8:24⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱسْتَجِيبُوا۟ لِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ إِذَا دَعَاكُمْ لِمَا يُحْيِيكُمْ ۖ وَٱعْلَمُوٓا۟ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يَحُولُ بَيْنَ ٱلْمَرْءِ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَأَنَّهُۥٓ إِلَيْهِ تُحْشَرُونَ ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Answer Allah (by obeying Him) and (His) Messenger when he (PBUH) calls you to that which will give you life, and know that Allah comes in between a person and his heart (i.e. He prevents an evil person to decide anything). And verily to Him you shall (all) be gathered.*
> O you who believe! Obey Allah and the Messenger when He calls you to that matter in which you live, and know that Allah stands as a barrier between a man and his heart, and that to Him you will be gathered.
> — **Quran 8:24 (inline widget)**

ʿAlī has already declared that the divine summons in whose embrace human beings live is the revelation (⟪ar:’وحی‘⟫) that awakens the latent treasures of the intellect. The intellect, the very expression of the soul, is no mere name for a mental power; it is grounded in life itself. Mawlānā ʿAlī says that the truly rational person (⟪ar:’عاقل‘⟫, ʿāqil) is one whose knowledge is sound, whose action is sound, and whose effort is always directed toward the Absolute Truth. Another of his definitions of the ʿāqil is "one who places every thing in its rightful station" — that is, the just (⟪ar:’عادل‘⟫, ʿādil). This shows that only the rational can be just, since only one who sees things according to their reality can set them in their rightful place. Right thinking, blameless virtue, and authentic being are all of them qualities bound up with the intellect.

[^cite-5]: This articulation — that the very negation of an attribute must itself be negated, lest "negation" be made into a name of the divine essence — is the doctrine of double tanzīh worked out most rigorously by Abū Yaʿqūb al-Sijistānī, who teaches that the Originator (Mubdiʿ Taʿālā, the Originator, Most High) is not to be described either by an attribute or by its negation, since both belong to the order of created things.
[^cite-6]: Al-Sijistānī treats the divine attributes as identical with the essence, distinguished from one another only through the operation of the conceiving mind: they are not adjuncts adhering to a substrate but the essence itself viewed under different aspects.

<!-- section 3 (id=3578, raw_sort=3): علی کا کمیل ابن زیاد کو خطاب -->

## ʿAlī's Address to Kumayl ibn Ziyād

Kumayl ibn Ziyād al-Nakhaʿī relates that the Commander of the Faithful — peace be upon him — took hold of his hand and led him out to the cemetery. When they had passed through the burial ground and the city lay behind them, he drew a deep sigh and said:

⟪ar-quote:قال كُمَيْل بن زياد- أخذ بيدي أميرالمؤمنين علي بن أبي طالب عليه السلام ، فأخرجني إلى الجبّان فلمّا أصحر تنفّس الصّعَدَاء ثمّ قال⟫

"O Kumayl, these hearts are vessels, and the best of them is that which best preserves what it holds. So preserve what I say to you."

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْل بْن زِيَادٍ، إِنَّ هذهِ الْقُلُوبَ أَوْعِيَةٌ فَخَيْرُهَا أَوْعَاهَا فَاحْفَظْ عَنِّي مَا أَقُولُ لَكَ⟫

"People are of three sorts. There is the divinely instructed scholar (ʿālim rabbānī); there is the seeker of knowledge upon the path of deliverance; and there is the common rabble who trail behind every caller, swaying with every passing wind. They draw no light from the radiance of knowledge, nor do they take refuge in any firm support."

⟪ar-quote:النَّاسُ ثَلاَثَةٌ- فَعَالِمٌ رَبَّانِيٌّ وَمُتَعَلِّمٌ عَلَى سَبِيلِ نَجَاةٍ، وَهَمَجٌ رَعَاعٌ أَتْبَاعُ كُلِّ نَاعِقٍ يَمِيلُونَ مَعَ كُلِّ رِيحٍ، لَمْ يَسْتَضِيئُوا بِنُورِ الْعِلْمِ، وَلَمْ يَلْجَؤُوا إِلَى رُكْنٍ وَثِيقٍ⟫

"O Kumayl, knowledge is better than wealth. Knowledge guards you, while you must guard wealth. Wealth diminishes as it is spent; knowledge multiplies as it is given, and what wealth produces perishes with the perishing of wealth itself."

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلُ، الْعِلْمُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ الْمَالِ- الْعِلْمُ يَحْرُسُكَ وَأَنْتَ تَحْرُسُ المَالَ، وَالْمَالُ تَنْقُصُهُ النَّفَقَةُ، وَالْعِلْمُ يَزْكُوعَلَى الاْنْفَاقِ، وَصَنِيعُ الْمَالِ يَزُولُ بِزَوَالِهِ⟫

"O Kumayl son of Ziyād, the true recognition of knowledge is a religion to be practised. By it, a person earns obedience in his lifetime and a fair remembrance after his death. Knowledge is the ruler, and wealth is what is ruled."

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلَ بْنَ زِيَادٍ مَعْرِفَةُ الْعِلْمِ دِينٌ يُدَانُ بِهِ . بِهِ يَكْسِبُ الْإِنْسَانُ الطَّاعَةَ فِى حَيَاتِهِ وَ جَمِيلَ الْأُحْدُوثَةِ بَعْدَ وَفَاتِهِ وَ الْعِلْمُ حَاكِمٌ وَ الْمَالُ مَحْكُومٌ عَلَيْهِ⟫

"O Kumayl, those who hoard wealth are dead even while they live, but the knowers will endure for as long as the world endures. Their bodies are absent, yet their likenesses live on within the hearts. Here — and he pointed to his breast — here is an abundance of knowledge, if only I could find someone fit to bear it. Yes, I did find some; but one was quick of apprehension yet not to be trusted: he would put the instrument of religion to the service of the world, and use God's favours upon him as a means of dominion over His servants, and God's proofs as a means of mastery over His friends. Another was obedient to the bearers of truth, yet had no insight in his breast: at the first appearance of doubt his heart would be set aflame with misgiving."[^cite-7]

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلُ هَلَكَ خُزَّانُ الْأَمْوَالِ وَ هُمْ أَحْيَاءٌ وَ الْعُلَمَاءُ بَاقُونَ مَا بَقِيَ الدَّهْرُ أَعْيَانُهُمْ مَفْقُودَةٌ وَ أَمْثَالُهُمْ فِى الْقُلُوبِ مَوْجُودَةٌ هَا إِنَّ هَاهُنَا لَعِلْماً جَمّاً وَ أَشَارَ بِيَدِهِ إِلَى صَدْرِهِ لَوْ أَصَبْتُ لَهُ حَمَلَةً بَلَى أَصَبْتُ لَقِناً غَيْرَ مَأْمُونٍ عَلَيْهِ مُسْتَعْمِلًا آلَةَ الدِّينِ لِلدُّنْيَا وَ مُسْتَظْهِراً بِنِعَمِ اللَّهِ عَلَى عِبَادِهِ وَ بِحُجَجِهِ عَلَى أَوْلِيَائِهِ أَوْ مُنْقَاداً لِحَمَلَةِ الْحَقِّ لَا بَصِيرَةَ لَهُ فِى أَحْنَائِهِ يَنْقَدِحُ الشَّكُّ فِى قَلْبِهِ لِأَوَّلِ عَارِضٍ مِنْ شُبْهَةٍ⟫

"Neither this man nor that man will do. Or there is the one famished for pleasures, easily led by his passions, or the one consumed with collecting and hoarding wealth: neither of them counts among the shepherds of religion in any respect. The nearest likeness to them is loose grazing cattle. Thus does knowledge die with the death of those who bear it."

⟪ar-quote:أَلَا لَا ذَا وَ لَا ذَاكَ أَوْ مَنْهُوماً بِاللَّذَّةِ سَلِسَ الْقِيَادِ لِلشَّهْوَةِ أَوْ مُغْرَماً بِالْجَمْعِ وَ الِادِّخَارِ لَيْسَا مِنْ رُعَاةِ الدِّينِ فِى شَيْ‏ءٍ أَقْرَبُ شَيْ‏ءٍ شَبَهاً بِهِمَا الْأَنْعَامُ السَّائِمَةُ كَذَلِكَ يَمُوتُ الْعِلْمُ بِمَوْتِ حَامِلِيهِ⟫

"O my God — and yet! The earth is never left without one who upholds the proof of God, whether openly and known by all, or in fear and hidden from view, lest the proofs of God and His clear signs be brought to nothing. How few they are, and where are they to be found? By God, they are the fewest in number and the greatest in standing before God. Through them God preserves His proofs and His evidences, until they entrust them to others of their like, and sow them in the hearts of those who resemble them."[^cite-8]

⟪ar-quote:اللَّهُمَّ بَلَى! لاَ تَخْلُو الاْرْضُ مِنْ قَائِمٍ لله بِحُجَّةٍ، إِمَّا ظَاهِراً مَشْهُوراً، أوْ خَائِفاً مَغْمُوراً لِئَلاَّ تَبْطُلَ حُجَجُ اللهِ وَبَيِّنَاتُهُ. وَكَمْ ذَا وَأَيْنَا أُولئِكَ؟ أُولئِكَ ـ وَاللَّهِ ـ الاْقَلُّونَ عَدَداً، وَالاْعْظَمُونَ قَدْراً، يَحْفَظُ اللهُ بِهِمْ حُجَجَهُ وَبَيِّنَاتِهِ، حَتَّى يُودِعُوهَا نُظَرَاءَهُمْ، وَيَزْرَعُوهَا فِي قُلُوبِ أَشْبَاهِهِمْ⟫

"Knowledge has carried them through to the reality of insight; they have laid hold of the spirit of certainty; what the pampered find harsh, they have found easy, and what the ignorant find strange, they have come to find familiar. They keep company with this world in their bodies, while their spirits remain fastened to the highest station. These are the vicegerents of God upon His earth and the summoners (duʿāt, the Summoners) unto His religion. Ah, ah — how I yearn to behold them! Go now, O Kumayl, whither you will."

⟪ar-quote:هَجَمَ بِهِمُ الْعِلْمُ عَلَى حَقِيقَةِ الْبَصِيرَةِ، وَبَاشَرُوا رُوحَ الْيَقِينِ، وَاسْتَلاَنُوامَا اسْتَوْعَرَهُ الْمُتْرَفُونَ وَأَنِسُوا بِمَا اسْتَوْحَشَ مِنْهُ الْجَاهِلُونَ، وَصَحِبُوا الدُّنْيَا بِأَبْدَانٍ أَرْوَاحُهَا مُعَلَّقَةٌ بِالْـمَحَلِّ الاْعْلَى، أُولئِكَ خُلَفَاءُ اللهِ فِي أَرْضِهِ، وَالدُّعَاةُ إِلَى دِينِهِ، آهِ آهِ شَوْقاً إِلَى رُؤْيَتِهِمْ! انْصَرِفْ إذَا شِئْتَ!⟫

[^cite-7]: The Imam's lament that he could find no fit bearer for the knowledge in his breast is taken up in Fatimid daʿwa (the summons / the invitation) literature as a charter for the carefully graded transmission of taʾwīl (esoteric exegesis), pledged from one trustworthy dāʿī to another rather than scattered indiscriminately. Qāḍī al-Nuʿmān reflects this discipline in his treatment of the imamate.
[^cite-8]: The doctrine that the earth is never devoid of a qāʾim bi-ḥujjat Allāh — one who upholds God's proof in every age, whether manifest or concealed — is the bedrock of Fatimid imamology. Qāḍī al-Nuʿmān cites this saying as a foundational warrant for the doctrine of the perpetual imamate.

<!-- section 4 (id=3579, raw_sort=4): علم اور بصیرت -->
## Knowledge and Insight

In this sermon, the Imam speaks of the blessed servants of God — the Imams themselves — and declares them to be the very life of God's religion. The "Divine Religion" here is the religion that issues from the Almighty: it is the essence of faith, complete and immutable. Religion, the Imam says, stands erect only through the knowledge of the true scholars; were it not for these scholars — the Imams of truth — every trace of religion would long since have been effaced. He then continues with the celebrated phrase, ⟪ar-quote:هَجَمَ بِهِمُ الْعِلْمُ عَلَى حَقِيقَةِ الْبَصِيرَةِ⟫ ("Through them, knowledge has stormed the very reality of insight").[^cite-9] As has been observed, although knowledge has always lain concealed within the substance of the intellect, it must still be quickened into life. The Imam's choice of the verb "to storm" (⟪ar:’ھَجَمَ‘⟫) testifies that this knowledge lies hidden in meanings buried beneath the surface of words — deeper meanings subordinate to the apparent ones. The saying thus points to graded degrees of knowledge. Indicating his own breast, he then said, ⟪ar-quote:هَاهُنَا لَعِلْماً جَمّاً⟫ ("Here, indeed, lies a vast knowledge"). The breast, plainly, conceals the heart within it; yet to reach the heart through the breast, one must penetrate deep into the breast itself. Words can point to hidden realities, but they cannot encompass them.

> — *Image text (from image 003; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at .. /images/003.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

In Arabic, the word ⟪ar:’ھَجَمَ‘⟫ means "to attack" or "to charge." The aim of an army's charge is to drive into the heart of the enemy formation, which lies at its centre. The verb ⟪ar:ھجم⟫ therefore summons us to a kind of intellectual assault — to break through the outward face of words and to reach the depths of the realities concealed within them. Once those depths of insight have been embedded, the gates of contemplation open before the intellect, and the seeker comes to know the truth of this knowledge, as the Imam himself observed: ⟪ar-quote:من فَھِم عَلِمَ گوہر العلم⟫ ("Whoever has been granted understanding has reached the very essence of knowledge"). The descent into such depths demands struggle, as in his other dictum: ⟪ar-quote:بالتَّعَلُّم یَناَلُ العلم⟫ ("Knowledge is attained only through learning"). The aim of every such effort is that one should so deeply absorb external knowledge into one's own self, through the intellect, that the two become indistinguishable. It is the power of the spirit (⟪ar:’روح‘⟫) that forges this unification (⟪ar:’توحید‘⟫, tawḥīd) of knowledge with essence.

### Jihad al-Nafs

This unification is possible only when the self has been emptied of egocentricity (⟪ar:أنانیت⟫). The Lord of the Faithful teaches that the wise are those who wage perpetual war against the baser tendencies, appetites, and desires of the soul — for each of these transgresses against the authority of knowledge. The vices of the soul are like clouds: when they crowd the sky of the intellect, vision is dimmed and reality is no longer plainly seen. The Qur'an names these vices "rust":

> ⟪quran 83:14⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّا ۖ بَلْۜ رَانَ عَلَىٰ قُلُوبِهِم مَّا كَانُوا۟ يَكْسِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *Nay! But on their hearts is the Ran (covering of sins and evil deeds) which they used to earn .*
> by no means, but their hearts are rusted by what they used to do.
> — **Quran 83:14 (inline widget)**

Though vices are morally repugnant, viewed spiritually they stand as the antithesis of the realities God has created. To follow them is to obscure sight and to blind the eye of the heart — that organ by which God is perceived. The wise person is therefore in constant struggle against the appetites and cleaves to noble character. The root of every immorality is ignorance, and to be rid of ignorance one must wage a great war against one's own self — the war that the Prophet (peace be upon him) named the "greater jihad" (⟪ar:’جہاد اکبر‘⟫). Concerning this jihad of the self (⟪ar:جہاد النفس⟫), the Lord of the Faithful says:[^cite-10]

| The wise man fights against his self through knowledge.
| --- |
| The most powerful is the one who stands against his own self.
| Indeed, those who fight against their souls in the cause of Allah, their status in the sight of Allah is that of those who are martyred.
| The ultimate battle is man's war with his own self.
| He who knows his self fights with it.
| No Jihad is Greater Than Jihad of the Self |

He says that although this war appears to be against the self, in truth it is for the self's own good. The intellect (⟪ar:العقل⟫) is the commander of the army of the Merciful (⟪ar:رحمن⟫), while caprice (⟪ar:الھوی⟫) is the commander of the army of Satan. The self is caught between them, drawn one way and then the other (⟪ar:متجاذبہ بینھُما⟫), and whichever of them prevails recruits the self into its forces. To enter the army of the Merciful (⟪ar:’رحمن‘⟫), then, the self must be wholly subdued. The goal is not the abolition of the self but the abolition of caprice (⟪ar:’ھوی‘⟫) within it. The Qur'an testifies that the Messenger did not speak from caprice (⟪ar:ھوی⟫):

> ⟪quran 53:3-4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْىٌۭ يُوحَىٰ ‎⟫
> *Nor does he speak of (his own) desire. It is only an Inspiration that is inspired.*
> Nor does he say anything of his own accord. It is naught but a revelation that comes to him.
> — **Quran 53:3-4 (inline widget)**

The intellect is the spokesman of the army of the Merciful and the foe of the army of Satan. The word caprice (⟪ar:الھوی⟫) appears elsewhere in the Qur'an in a still more arresting form:

> ⟪quran 25:43⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ أَفَأَنتَ تَكُونُ عَلَيْهِ وَكِيلًا ‎⟫
> *Have you (O Muhammad PBUH) seen him who has taken as his ilah (god) his own desire? Would you then be a Wakîl (a disposer of his affairs or a watcher) over him?*
> Have you seen him who has taken his God for his own desires? Will you then be a guardian over him?
> — **Quran 25:43 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 45:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who takes his own lust (vain desires) as his ilah (god), and Allah knowing (him as such), left him astray, and sealed his hearing and his heart, and put a cover on his sight. Who then will guide him after Allah? Will you not then remember?*
> have you seen him who has become a slave of his own desire, and Allah has led him astray despite his knowledge, and set a seal upon his hearing and his heart, and put a covering on his sight? Who will guide him after Allah? Will you not then understand?
> — **Quran 45:23 (inline widget)**

The Messenger of God said of this hidden polytheism (⟪ar:’شرک خفی‘⟫) of caprice (⟪ar:ھوی⟫): ⟪ar-quote:الشرك فيكم أخفی من دبيب النمل⟫ ("Shirk among you is more hidden than the crawl of an ant"). To shatter the idols of the egoic self (⟪ar:أنانیت⟫), an external force is required — one not derived from the self's own caprice (⟪ar:ھوی⟫). That force is the "divine sciences," issuing from intellect and faith. God declares:

> ⟪quran 79:40-41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَى ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎ ‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫
> *But as for him who feared standing before his Lord, and restrained himself from impure evil desires, and lusts. Verily, Paradise will be his abode.*
> But as for him who fears to stand before his Lord, and restrain himself from lust, his abode is Paradise.
> — **Quran 79:40-41 (inline widget)**

The core energy of the soul cannot be extinguished, but it can be turned away from the manifold satanic appetites and redirected towards what is beneficent. Tawḥīd means "to make one," to integrate. God is not only the unique (⟪ar:’أحد‘⟫) in Himself but the source from which the unique (⟪ar:أحد⟫) creature also derives. In this sense, tawḥīd is not merely an acknowledgement of divine oneness (⟪ar:أحدیت⟫) but a declaration of oneself as one (⟪ar:أحد⟫), so that the true Unique (⟪ar:أحد حقیقی⟫) may be properly reflected. To know God is to be bound to Him. One of the meanings of "intellect" is "to bind," for the intellect grasps and contains meaning. Distinct from the intellect is the "heart" — the seat of the intellect (⟪ar:الحام⟫) and the organ that broadcasts spiritual realities. Put another way: the intellect apprehends; the heart radiates. The intellect is the power that binds together the disparate elements of the soul and unifies them. For this reason, the Lord of the Faithful says:

⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ اللہ تَوَحَّدُ⟫ (He who knows Allah becomes one with Him)*
⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ⟫ Abstraction ⟫ * (He who knows his own self is separated from it)*
⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ⟫ People are different⟫ * (He who knows the people is separated from them)*
⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ⟫ Al-Dunya Tazhd ⟫ * (He who knows the world restrains himself from it)*

### Sincerity

Elsewhere, the Lord of the Faithful gives the name "sincerity" (ikhlāṣ) to this total ordering of the self according to divine reality. The verb ⟪ar:خَلُصَ⟫ means to be wholly purified, to descend into the unmixed essence, to be free of every admixture. In this spirit he says: ⟪ar-quote:أخلص لی اللہ العلم و العمل والحب و العداوۃ، والقبض و المغادرۃ، والنطق و الصمت⟫ ("Purify for the sake of God your knowledge and your works, your love and your enmity, your taking and your relinquishing, your speech and your silence"). To be sincere is to purify the self for God in such a way that no stain remains within it. The stain here means everything other than God (⟪ar:’غیر اللہ‘⟫): the purgation of every devotion, action, intention, and passion that is not for God's sake is what we call sincerity. The deepest of these stains is egocentricity (⟪ar:أنانیت⟫). Sincerity demands that every act, every thought, and the very existence of the person be without self-interest, undertaken solely for God. The Imam's phrase "the ultimate battle" was meant precisely to underscore this. Whoever attains such sincerity is, in the sight of God, a martyr — for he has slain his own self in God's path, and now lives by the light of intellect and is sustained by revelation, as God says:

> ⟪quran 3:169⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ ٱلَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا۟ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ أَمْوَتًۢا ۚ بَلْ أَحْيَآءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ ‎⟫
> *Think not of those who are killed in the Way of Allah as dead. Nay, they are alive, with their Lord, and they have provision.*
> Think not of those who are slain in the way of Allah as dead.
> — **Quran 3:169 (inline widget)**

The word "martyr" (⟪ar:شہید⟫) also bears the sense of "witness." That is, by sacrificing his own soul the sincere one bears witness that he stands with God and against everything that is not God. The centre of such a person is no longer his own self; the centre of all things has become God. Sincerity, then, is existence for the sake of God and replete with God, as God says:

> ⟪quran 6:162⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِنَّ صَلَاتِى وَنُسُكِى وَمَحْيَاىَ وَمَمَاتِى لِلَّهِ رَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH): "Verily, my Salat (prayer), my sacrifice, my living, and my dying are for Allah, the Lord of the 'Alamîn (mankind, jinns and all that exists).*
Say> Surely my prayer and my sacrifice and my life and my death are all for Allah, the Lord of all the worlds.
> — **Quran 6:162 (inline widget)**

### Sincerity and Prayer

Prayer is integral to sincerity. The food of the human soul is worship, and no sustenance is more nourishing than prayer. It is for this reason that, in the verse just cited and in many others, God names prayer first. The one who does not pray has starved his soul of its proper sustenance and failed to discharge what is due to it; and the one who cannot fulfil the right of his own soul will never fulfil the rights of others. Whoever sets right what is between himself and God, God in turn sets right what is between him and God's servants. The Qur'an again attests:

> ⟪quran 15:99⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱعْبُدْ رَبَّكَ حَتَّىٰ يَأْتِيَكَ ٱلْيَقِينُ ‎⟫
> *And worship your Lord until there comes unto you the certainty (i.e. death).*
> and worship your Lord until there comes to you certainty.
> — **Quran 15:99 (inline widget)**

If the hidden treasures of the intellect are to be awakened, then knowledge must be pursued with constancy and total devotion. Such devotion in turn demands an unbroken focus on divine realities and a depth of worship in which no veil interposes between the worshipper and the Worshipped — worship in which the servant forgets all others, and forgets even himself. Without this inward forgetting, mechanical worship has no value. The Lord of the Faithful says that a person who prays without the strenuous effort of ijtihād is like one who looses an arrow without a bow. So too with knowledge: it depends upon action; absent a balanced practice, it dissolves. The heart cannot digest knowledge acquired without seriousness; it can therefore neither attain insight nor see God.

The Lord of the Universe says, "Acquire knowledge, and life will acquire you." At the outset, a person is unaware of life's realities. He seeks knowledge, which awakens consciousness in him. But when this seeking is pursued with sincerity over a sustained period — that is, when knowledge is steadily transmuted into action — there comes a moment when it is no longer the seeker who is integrating knowledge into himself, but life itself that is absorbing the knowledge into him. The process he once carried out with utmost effort and ijtihād becomes the settled rhythm of his life, in which the same dedication is exercised without conscious labour. Habit, in short, ripens into instinct.

Let us return to the saying of the Lord of the Universe that knowledge has stormed the realities of insight. The scholar (⟪ar:’عالم‘⟫) is not merely immersed in insights; he is the one to whom these divine insights now come, and the world itself becomes a vehicle for him — because he has at last integrated himself into the very knowledge (⟪ar:’علم‘⟫) he sought.

<!-- section 5 (id=3580, raw_sort=5):  یقین کی روح -->
## The Spirit of Certainty

Then you say, "⟪ar-quote:وبشِّرُ روح الیقین⟫ (They rejoice because they are joined to the Spirit of Certainty)." Among human beings, the term ⟪ar:’مباشرت‘⟫ derives from the sense of close contact or direct relation with something; but the same root also conveys extreme delight. When a person genuinely touches the spirit of certainty (yaqīn), the joy he receives lies beyond expression. That happiness, the Imām suggests, surpasses every other blessing promised in Paradise, of which Allāh says:

> ⟪quran 9:72⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَٱلْمُؤْمِنَتِ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ خَلِدِينَ فِيهَا وَمَسَكِنَ طَيِّبَةًۭ فِى جَنَّتِ عَدْنٍۢ ۚ وَرِضْوَنٌۭ مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُوَ ٱلْفَوْزُ ٱلْعَظِيمُ ‎⟫
> *Allah has promised to the believers -men and women, - Gardens under which rivers flow to dwell therein forever, and beautiful mansions in Gardens of 'Adn (Eden Paradise). But the greatest bliss is the Good Pleasure of Allah. That is the supreme success.*
> Allah has promised the believers, men and women, Gardens beneath which rivers flow, wherein they will abide for ever, and noble dwellings and Gardens of Eden. And the greatest of all, the pleasure of Allah; that is the great attainment.
> — **Quran 9:72 (inline widget)**

Mawlānā ʿAlī teaches that the acquisition of knowledge, joined with sustained contemplation, is itself a sign of divine favour upon the scholar. Allāh is One, and each of His creatures is likewise singular: every human being occupies a station in which no other shares him, and his standing within that circle cannot be divided. The truest knowledge a person can pursue is therefore the knowledge of his own self — a knowledge he can never wholly compass. For this reason the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: ⟪ar-quote:من عرف نفسہ فقد عرف ربہ⟫ "Whoever knows his own soul has thereby known his Lord." In its early stages, the joy of learning resembles the relief of one who has returned from the exile of ignorance to the calm of his own house. The most knowing among us is the most living, and the most living is the one nearest to Allāh; and life itself, on this measure, is joy. Such happiness differs in kind from the pleasures men gather along the way. Mawlānā ʿAlī further teaches that a true ⟪ar:’فقیہ‘⟫ (faqīh, jurist of insight) is one who never causes the people to despair of Allāh's mercy: immersed himself in the light of that mercy, he is confident that, whatever Allāh decrees, mercy will be folded within it.[^cite-11] Allāh says:

> ⟪quran 15:56⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قَالَ وَمَن يَقْنَطُ مِن رَّحْمَةِ رَبِّهِۦٓ إِلَّا ٱلضَّآلُّونَ ‎⟫
> *[Ibrahim (Abraham)] said: "And who despairs of the Mercy of his Lord except those who are astray?" *
> said, Only those who despair of the mercy of their Lord are those who have gone astray.
> — **Quran 15:56 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *When those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.) come to you, say: "Salamun 'Alaikum" (peace be on you); your Lord has written Mercy for Himself, so that, if any of you does evil in ignorance, and thereafter repents and does righteous good deeds (by obeying Allah), then surely, He is Oft&shy;Forgiving, Most Merciful.*
> And those who believe in Our verses, when they come to you, say, Peace be upon you. Your Lord has made mercy incumbent upon Himself. So whoever among you does evil in ignorance, then repents thereafter and does good, then indeed He is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful.
> — **Quran 6:54 (inline widget)**

The joy proper to Allāh's mercy is, in truth, the inward shape of beauty itself. This is not the beauty of mere aesthetic surface but a deeper beauty: the image cast by the intellect when it contemplates its Lord. The Arabic word ⟪ar:’أحسان‘⟫ (iḥsān) is most often rendered as virtue or excellence, yet it carries also the sense of ⟪ar:حُسن⟫ (ḥusn, beauty) — that is, of concepts which render the soul itself beautiful. Mawlānā ʿAlī has said that the excellence of the intellect lies in its ability ⟪ar:ینظر جمال الظاہر والباطن⟫ to perceive the beauty of things both outward and inward. The beauty of forms and acts is completed by their interior beauty, just as the beauty of deeds proceeds from the virtue of the soul that performs them. It is in this sense that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, "Allāh is beautiful and loves beautiful things."

By cultivating beautiful character within himself, a person becomes capable of loving Allāh — for Allāh loves what is beautiful. It is precisely this beauty of character that made ⟪ar:محمد مصطفی صلی اللہ علیہ و آلہ و سلم⟫ the most beloved of Allāh's servants, and by which he summoned his Umma to the same nobility:

> ⟪quran 3:31⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ ٱللَّهَ فَٱتَّبِعُونِى يُحْبِبْكُمُ ٱللَّهُ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ ذُنُوبَكُمْ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH to mankind): "If you (really) love Allah then follow me (i.e. accept Islamic Monotheism, follow the Quran and the Sunnah), Allah will love you and forgive you of your sins. And Allah is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful." *
Say, > if you love God, then follow me, and God will love you and forgive you your sins. God is Forgiving and Merciful.
> — **Quran 3:31 (inline widget)**

In commenting on this principle, the Imām declares: ⟪ar-quote:اول العقل التَوَدُّد⟫ "The first principle of intellect is loving-kindness." That is, one must first inculcate the principle of love within the soul, and only then express that love through outward action, until inward warmth and outward grace become a single radiance. To follow the Messenger of Allāh is, in substance, to take on the morals of the Messenger of Allāh; for in him alone the perfection of those morals has been actualised. From this it follows that the connection of the intellect with Truth is established only through the noblest virtues — gentleness, contentment, gratitude, generosity, modesty, wisdom, forbearance — which are beautiful in themselves and which generate love both within and without. A true intellect is the very embodiment of these qualities, since without them no intellect attains completion. Through such virtues a person works depth into his habitual actions and brings forth the hidden treasures of intellect.[^cite-12] To pour all these dispositions into the single mould of the soul, until they become unified there, is in a real sense an act of monotheism. Truth, of course, acts upon the soul of its own accord; yet morality must become the leaven of intellect so that the latter may pass from potency ⟪ar:بالقوۃ⟫ to actuality ⟪ar:بالفعل⟫ through the dispositions of right action. In this light, every immorality is not merely vice but a cause of intellectual debility. The heart sickens, and the eye is darkened, until it can no longer recognise reality. As the Qurʾān says:

> ⟪quran 2:10⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فِى قُلُوبِهِم مَّرَضٌۭ فَزَادَهُمُ ٱللَّهُ مَرَضًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا كَانُوا۟ يَكْذِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *In their hearts is a disease (of doubt and hypocrisy) and Allah has increased their disease. A painful torment is theirs because they used to tell lies.*
> is a sickness in their hearts, so Allah has increased their sickness, and there awaits them a painful punishment, for they used to lie.
> — **Quran 2:10 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 22:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَلَمْ يَسِيرُوا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ فَتَكُونَ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ يَعْقِلُونَ بِهَآ أَوْ آذَانٌۭ يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَا ۖ فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَعْمَى ٱلْأَبْصَرُ وَلَكِن تَعْمَى ٱلْقُلُوبُ ٱلَّتِى فِى ٱلصُّدُورِ ‎⟫
> *Have they not travelled through the land, and have they hearts wherewith to understand and ears wherewith to hear? Verily, it is not the eyes that grow blind, but it is the hearts which are in the breasts that grow blind.*
> have they not travelled in the land, so that they have hearts wherewith to understand, or ears wherewith to hear? Verily it is not the eyes that are blinded, but it is the hearts in the breasts that are blinded.
> — **Quran 22:46 (inline widget)**

Mawlānā ʿAlī teaches that the one who masters his passions prospers, and that through such well-being a person can come to taste the happiness which only certainty yields. The spirit of this certainty arises from the union of right intention with sincerity (ikhlāṣ), observed within the bounds of Sharīʿa. Where the works of Sharīʿa lack sincerity they collapse into hypocrisy, and hypocrisy, the Imām warns, is itself a form of associating with Allāh: "Know that even the slightest hypocrisy is shirk." Allāh makes this plain in His sūra:

> ⟪quran 107:1-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ ٱلَّذِى يُكَذِّبُ بِٱلدِّينِ ‎ ‏فَذَلِكَ ٱلَّذِى يَدُعُّ ٱلْيَتِيمَ ‎ ‏وَلَا يَحُضُّ عَلَىٰ طَعَامِ ٱلْمِسْكِينِ ‎ ‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎ ‏وَيَمْنَعُونَ ٱلْمَاعُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who denies the Recompense? That is he who repulses the orphan (harshly), And urges not the feeding of AlMiskîn (the poor), So woe unto those performers of Salat (prayers) (hypocrites), Who delay their Salat (prayer) from their stated fixed times, Those who do good deeds only to be seen (of men), And refuse Al-Ma'un (small kindnesses e.g. salt, sugar, water,  etc.). *
> Hast thou seen him who denies the Day of Judgment, and is he who pusheth away the orphan and does not urge the feeding of the needy? Woe to the worshippers who are heedless of their prayers and restrict them from their prayers.
> — **Quran 107:1-7 (inline widget)**

The sūra makes clear that outward worship retains no value unless it is fused with sincerity and a morally serious life. Religion without that depth is empty. An act carried by pure intention is true action; without it, the outward deed is dust and never rises in the sight of Allāh.[^cite-13]

> ⟪quran 22:37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏لَن يَنَالَ ٱللَّهَ لُحُومُهَا وَلَا دِمَآؤُهَا وَلَكِن يَنَالُهُ ٱلتَّقْوَىٰ مِنكُمْ ۚ كَذَلِكَ سَخَّرَهَا لَكُمْ لِتُكَبِّرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عَلَىٰ مَا هَدَىٰكُمْ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلْمُحْسِنِينَ ‎⟫
> *It is neither their meat nor their blood that reaches Allah, but it is piety from you that reaches Him. Thus have We made them subject to you that you may magnify Allah for His Guidance to you. And give glad tidings (O Muhammad PBUH) to the Muhsinun (doers of good).*
> It is not their flesh nor their blood that reaches Allah, but piety from you reaches Him. Thus have He subjected them to you, that you may magnify Allah for that He has guided you, and give good tidings to the doers of good.
> — **Quran 22:37 (inline widget)**

Mawlānā ʿAlī says that he who has no intellect has no religion, and that the sleep of certainty is finer than the wakefulness of doubt. Such ones remain spiritually awake even while their bodies sleep, in the manner the Prophet (peace be upon him) described: "My eyes sleep, but my heart remains awake." The wise know that, while the outward acts of worship are necessary in their own right, the blessings of Allāh cannot be earned by these alone. What is required, in addition, is awareness of what one is doing — and why one is doing it. This consciousness, joined to interior beauty of character, draws down Allāh's acceptance. As Mawlānā ʿAlī declares: "The best knowledge for you is that which renders your deeds acceptable to Allāh."

*Verses referenced in this topic (curated linkage from KAHSKOLE. TopicAyats — 5 of 5 not already cited above):*

> ⟪quran 2:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous good deeds, that for them will be Gardens under which rivers flow (Paradise). Every time they will be provided with a fruit therefrom, they will say: "This is what we were provided with before," and they will be given things in resemblance (i.e. in the same form but different in taste) and they shall have therein Azwajun Mutahharatun (purified mates or wives), (having no menses, stools, urine, etc.) and they will abide therein forever.*
> And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds, that for them are Gardens beneath which rivers flow; whenever they are provided with a fruit from it, they will say, This is what we were provided with before. And they will be given fruits like the same, and they will have therein purified spouses, and they will abide in it forever.
> — **Quran 2:25 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 38:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We did choose them by granting them (a good thing, i.e.) the remembrance of the home [in the Hereafter and they used to make the people remember it, and also they used to invite the people to obey Allah and to do good deeds for the Hereafter].*
> assuredly We preferred unto them a distinct distinction, the remembrance of the Hereafter.
> — **Quran 38:46 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 55:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫
> *Is there any reward for good other than good?*
> recompense for goodness other than goodness?
> — **Quran 55:60 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 87:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَبْقَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Although the Hereafter is better and more lasting.*
> whereas the Hereafter is better and more enduring.
> — **Quran 87:17 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 89:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫
> *(It will be said to the pious): "O (you) the one in (complete) rest and satisfaction!*
> O soul of contentment,
> — **Quran 89:27 (TopicAyats)**

<!-- section 6 (id=3600, raw_sort=6): دنیا میں رہتے ہوئے آخرت کی زندگی -->
## Living the Life of the Hereafter While Dwelling in This World

The Imām then says that, though such people are joined to this world by their bodies, their souls are connected to the Hereafter. The thought can be illumined by another of his sayings, in which he declares that he belongs to a company whose spiritual rank is this: their hearts dwell in Paradise even as their bodies labour in this world. That the hearts are "settled" in Paradise tells us that, while still living here, they have arrived there spiritually, conceptually, and actually. The saying confirms also a teaching of the Prophet (peace be upon him), that Allāh keeps His servants in the state they themselves desire. Those who live in the upper world draw the foundation of their being from the Hereafter; those who live in this world, by contrast, draw all their thought and longing from it. Their reflections, fancies, and aims are imprisoned in this lower realm, and every act of theirs bears its seal. The wise, however, weigh each act against the recompense it earns in the Hereafter — for they grasp the truth that every deed is dust except that which Allāh, by His acceptance, raises up.[^cite-14]

Mawlānā ʿAlī often speaks in his sermons of the blessings of Paradise and the torments of Hell. Has he thus given a transactional cast to the commandments of Allāh? Not at all. To know about Paradise and Hell is one thing; to derive meaning from that knowledge is quite another. The Imām's aim is to plant within the Umma a feeling by which moral character itself may be set alight. From a merely transactional view, the object of a trade loses its purpose once the trade is concluded; would, then, the virtues of piety, refinement, and restraint become superfluous once Paradise has been entered? Certainly not. The atmosphere of Paradise will itself be made of these very virtues. The reason the Imām speaks of Paradise is precisely so that one may prepare himself, while still in this world, for the climate of the world to come. In one such sermon he says:

> If you turn your heart to the descriptions of Paradise, your soul will recoil from the wonders, desires, pleasures, and charming sceneries of this world. It will become absorbed instead in the scene of Paradise — with streams swaying along the banks of the canals, with their roots set in dunes of fragrant musk, and with glittering pearls hanging from the branches.

The highest grade of certainty — ⟪ar:’روحانیت‘⟫ (rūḥāniyya, spirituality) — lies above both the desire for Paradise and the dread of Hell. When that level is reached, the soul becomes "heavenly" even while still in this world. The condition of Paradise, properly understood, is one in which the soul is satisfied only with the august presence of its Lord and craves nothing besides. The Imām calls this state by the Qurʾān's own name: ⟪ar:’نفس المطمئنۃ‘⟫ (al-nafs al-muṭmaʾinna, the tranquil soul):

> ⟪quran 89:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫
> *(It will be said to the pious): "O (you) the one in (complete) rest and satisfaction!*
> O soul of contentment,
> — **Quran 89:27 (inline widget)**

The tranquillity of this soul flows directly from the completeness of its faith. Another verse echoes throughout Mawlānā ʿAlī's sermons:

> ⟪quran 87:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَبْقَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Although the Hereafter is better and more lasting.*
> whereas the Hereafter is better and more enduring.
> — **Quran 87:17 (inline widget)**

The Hereafter is not merely a "time" when the divine promises and glad tidings will be fulfilled; it is also a "house" in which all the noblest attributes — earthly and divine — find their full appearance, the faintest reflection of which we may glimpse in this world. In this capacity, the very mention and conception of Paradise works to purify the intellect and to draw it away from the appetites and pleasures of this world, as Allāh says:

> ⟪quran 38:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We did choose them by granting them (a good thing, i.e.) the remembrance of the home [in the Hereafter and they used to make the people remember it, and also they used to invite the people to obey Allah and to do good deeds for the Hereafter].*
> assuredly We preferred unto them a distinct distinction, the remembrance of the Hereafter.
> — **Quran 38:46 (inline widget)**

That is to say, pure knowledge of the Hereafter generates the very conception by which Paradise becomes present in this world, enabling a person to perform the deeds and bear the virtues that properly belong to the Hereafter — so that he attains felicity here as well as there.[^cite-15] It is in this way demonstrated that such moral perfections can arise only in one from whose vision the veil of this world has been lifted, who can sense and perceive the life of the Hereafter while still inhabiting this transient one. Good deeds, in this register, are not performed in order to earn a recompense in the Hereafter; rather, the good deed itself partakes already of that recompense. Allāh says:

> ⟪quran 55:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫
> *Is there any reward for good other than good?*
> recompense for goodness other than goodness?
> — **Quran 55:60 (inline widget)**

Mawlānā ʿAlī teaches that the fruit of every good action resembles its root — meaning that the end of an act lies already in its beginning, in the intention from which it sprang. Here this verse of the Qurʾān is wholly apposite:

> ⟪quran 2:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous good deeds, that for them will be Gardens under which rivers flow (Paradise). Every time they will be provided with a fruit therefrom, they will say: "This is what we were provided with before," and they will be given things in resemblance (i.e. in the same form but different in taste) and they shall have therein Azwajun Mutahharatun (purified mates or wives), (having no menses, stools, urine, etc.) and they will abide therein forever.*
> And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds, that for them are Gardens beneath which rivers flow; whenever they are provided with a fruit from it, they will say, This is what we were provided with before. And they will be given fruits like the same, and they will have therein purified spouses, and they will abide in it forever.
> — **Quran 2:25 (inline widget)**

The fruits of the Hereafter are tasted within this world as goodness, beauty, truth, and every joy that arises from these. Each such taste is a foretaste of the true nourishment of Paradise. In the order of morality, good deeds — and the inward sense that good deeds are needful (iḥsān, doing the beautiful) — are required not only for the salvation of the Hereafter but for liberation within this world: liberation, outwardly, from the bondage of sin, and inwardly, from the bondage of ego. This consciousness has been the focus and end of all the Imām's teaching.

<!-- section 7 (id=3581, raw_sort=7): وہ چیز جو آسان بھی ہے اور مشکل بھی -->

## That Which Is Both Easy and Difficult

He said: "Those things are easy for them which are difficult for the extravagant; and they love that from which the ignorant recoil." This saying of yours describes a quality that perpetually rests upon the hearts of the saints of God (awliyāʾ Allāh). They remain ever mindful of death and of their encounter with their Lord, and through His help they relinquish all attachment to the world. What strikes the ignorant as alien is precisely the manifest difficulty, suffering, and deprivation of this lower abode. The Qurʾān speaks of such trials in unmistakable terms:

> ⟪quran 2:155-157⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَنَبْلُوَنَّكُم بِشَىْءٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْخَوْفِ وَٱلْجُوعِ وَنَقْصٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْأَمْوَلِ وَٱلْأَنفُسِ وَٱلثَّمَرَتِ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلصَّبِرِينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَآ أَصَبَتْهُم مُّصِيبَةٌۭ قَالُوٓا۟ إِنَّا لِلَّهِ وَإِنَّآ إِلَيْهِ رَجِعُونَ ‎ ‏أُو۟لَٓئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَتٌۭ مِّن رَّبِّهِمْ وَرَحْمَةٌۭ ۖ وَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْمُهْتَدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And certainly, We shall test you with something of fear, hunger, loss of wealth, lives and fruits, but give glad tidings to As-Sabirin (the patient ones, etc.). Who, when afflicted with calamity, say: "Truly! To Allah we belong and truly, to Him we shall return." They are those on whom are the Salawat (i.e. blessings, etc.) (i.e. who are blessed and will be forgiven) from their Lord, and (they are those who) receive His Mercy, and it is they who are the guided-ones.*
> And We will surely test you with something of fear and hunger and loss of wealth and lives and fruits; and give glad tidings to those who patiently bear them, who, when afflicted with calamity, say: We belong to Allah, and to Him we shall return; these are the ones upon whom there is mercy from their Lord, and mercy, and they are the guided. are
> — **Quran 2:155-157 (inline widget)**

These guided ones — ⟪ar:مھتدون⟫ — are patient in the face of adversity, and through the certainty born of true knowledge they perceive and taste the blessings that issue from such forbearance:

> ⟪quran 103:1-3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْعَصْرِ ‎ ‏إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَفِى خُسْرٍ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلصَّبْرِ ‎⟫
> *By Al-'Asr (the time). Verily! Man is in loss, Except those who believe (in Islamic Monotheism) and do righteous good deeds, and recommend one another to the truth (i.e. order one another to perform all kinds of good deeds (Al-Ma'which Allah has ordained, and abstain from all kinds of sins and evil deeds (Al-Munkar which Allah has forbidden), and recommend one another to patience (for the sufferings,  harms, and injuries which one may encounter in Allah's Cause during preaching His religion of Islamic Monotheism or Jihad, etc.). *
By > time, man is in loss, except those who believe, and do righteous deeds, and enjoin one another to the truth and to be patient.
> — **Quran 103:1-3 (inline widget)**

These are the believers who remain firm amid trial, who know whence they came and whither they go, and who hold fast to the Qurʾānic refrain, "to Him we shall return." For this reason the difficulties of the world fall light upon them. The extravagant, by contrast, perceive only the bitterness and pain of these sufferings. The ease that hides within them is veiled by his ignorance, yet stands plain before the wise:

> ⟪quran 94:5-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَإِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًۭا ‎⟫
> *So verily, with the hardship, there is relief, Verily, with the hardship, there is relief (i.e. there is one hardship with two reliefs, so one hardship cannot overcome two reliefs).*
> Surely, with every hardship is ease, and with every hardship is ease.
> — **Quran 94:5-6 (inline widget)**

These wise ones do not merely behold with inward sight the fruit of ease that follows hardship; they taste it. They take suffering and trial for their companions, while the ignorant flee from them. For this reason he said: "Death is dearer to me than a mother's breast is to a suckling child."[^cite-16] One speaks of love for death while yet alive, as though seeing with one's own eyes the reality of death and the blessings that come after it. He said also: "I am the death of death!" — for life in this world is itself a kind of dying, a constraint and a compulsion. As God says:

> ⟪quran 29:64⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا هَذِهِ ٱلْحَيَوٰةُ ٱلدُّنْيَآ إِلَّا لَهْوٌۭ وَلَعِبٌۭ ۚ وَإِنَّ ٱلدَّارَ ٱلْآخِرَةَ لَهِىَ ٱلْحَيَوَانُ ۚ لَوْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And this life of the world is only amusement and play! Verily, the home of the Hereafter, that is the life indeed (i.e. the eternal life that will never end), if they but knew*
> And the life of this world is naught but a sport and a pastime; and the life of the Hereafter, if they but knew.
> — **Quran 29:64 (inline widget)**

### Asceticism

It is important to grasp here that the aim of such sayings is not the renunciation of this physical world as such, but the renunciation of its "world-being": that is, the severance of the bond between the worldly ⟪ar:’أنا‘⟫ (the worldly "I") and the things to which it clings. In ⟪ar:نہج البلاغۃ⟫ (Nahj al-Balāgha), he describes this state of ⟪ar:’زہد‘⟫ (zuhd, ascetic detachment) in the following terms:

This world is a place for which ruin has been ordained, and ruin has been decreed for its people. It is sweet and alluring. He who comes seeking it finds it rushing toward him; he who turns his gaze upon it allows it to settle in his heart. Gather, then, the best of provision (tawshah) from this place and depart, and ask nothing beyond what is most essential.

This is the best provision indeed. Elsewhere he says that this best provision is ⟪ar:’زہد‘⟫ and ⟪ar:’تقوی‘⟫ (taqwā, God-consciousness). For the life to come, this provision is acquired in the measure that one becomes indifferent to the perishing things of this world:

> ⟪quran 17:18⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَّن كَانَ يُرِيدُ ٱلْعَاجِلَةَ عَجَّلْنَا لَهُۥ فِيهَا مَا نَشَآءُ لِمَن نُّرِيدُ ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَا لَهُۥ جَهَنَّمَ يَصْلَىٰهَا مَذْمُومًۭا مَّدْحُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *Whoever wishes for the quick-passing (transitory enjoyment of this world), We readily grant him what We will for whom We like. Then, afterwards, We have appointed for him Hell, he will burn therein disgraced and rejected, ( far away from Allah's Mercy).*
> whosoever desires this fleeting life, We hasten to give him therein whatsoever We will; then We have prepared for him Gehenna wherein he shall dwell, disgraced and disgraced.
> — **Quran 17:18 (inline widget)**

The following sayings of Mawlānā ʿAlī give full voice to this contempt for the world:

By God! In my eyes, this world of yours is more despicable than a pig's bone chewed in the hand of a leper.
The likeness of the world is that of a serpent — soft to the touch, yet filled with deadly venom.
For me this world is no better than the mucus that flows from a goat's nose.

The greatness of God renders the world contemptible and base. When this world is viewed in the light of the absolutely Real, all its pleasures appear transient and trifling, and the lowliness of His servants before the majesty of God becomes manifest. Mawlānā ʿAlī praised one believer with the words: ⟪ar-quote:کان یعظمہ فی عینی، صغار الدنیا فی عینہ⟫ "In my eyes he was great because, in his eyes, the world was small." The world was not contemptible to the gnostics of God because it was of no use; rather, the greatness of God, of the Hereafter, and of the absolute realities present to their inward vision made it so. As the Qurʾān declares:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*
> And do not invoke any other god along with Allah; there is no God except Him; all things will perish except His Face; His is the command, and it is to Him that you will be returned.
> — **Quran 28:88 (inline widget)**

The worth of this world rests in this: that it holds the creatures of God who, morning and evening, declare His praise and acknowledge His greatness:

> ⟪quran 17:44⟫
> ⟪ar:‏تُسَبِّحُ لَهُ ٱلسَّمَوَتُ ٱلسَّبْعُ وَٱلْأَرْضُ وَمَن فِيهِنَّ ۚ وَإِن مِّن شَىْءٍ إِلَّا يُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِهِۦ وَلَكِن لَّا تَفْقَهُونَ تَسْبِيحَهُمْ ۗ إِنَّهُۥ كَانَ حَلِيمًا غَفُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *The seven heavens and the earth and all that is therein, glorify Him and there is not a thing but glorifies His Praise. But you understand not their glorification. Truly, He is Ever Forbearing, Oft-Forgiving.*
> seven heavens and the earth glorify Him and all that is between them. There is not a thing that does not glorify Him with His praise, but you do not understand their glorification. Indeed, He is all-forbearing, all-forgiving.
> — **Quran 17:44 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 24:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ عَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *See you not (O Muhammad PBUH) that Allah, He it is Whom glorify whosoever is in the heavens and the earth, and the birds with wings out-spread (in their flight). Of each one He (Allah) knows indeed his Salat (prayer) and his glorification, [or everyone knows his Salat (prayer) and his glorification], and Allah is All-Aware of what they do.*
> do you not see that all those who are in the heavens and the earth, and the birds with outspread wings, glorify Allah? Each one knows its prayer and its glorification, and Allah knows what they do.
> — **Quran 24:41 (inline widget)**

A double aspect of this world thus emerges: in one sense it is "an evil place," in another a "goodly place" in which all provisions for the Hereafter may be prepared. In his sermons he praises God for the artistry of nature — for peacocks and birds, even for ants, dragonflies, and elephants. In another sermon he uses the blessings of this world to illustrate the blessings of the Hereafter, saying that when the eye beholds the scenes of Paradise, even the most splendid of earthly visions and the most delicate of earthly pleasures grow despised in the sight of man. By the same measure, all the difficulties of this world become not only light but a wellspring of joy. The ascetics — ⟪ar:زاہدین،⟫ — endure every hardship through these spiritual resources, gained through faith. Their knowledge yields a certainty so firm and complete that they say: ⟪ar-quote:لو کشف الغطاء ما الزدت یقینا⟫ "Were the veil to be lifted, my certainty would not increase."[^cite-17]

Speaking of the sincerity of his own witness, he says: "I bear witness that there is no god but God! The sincerity of this witness of mine has been tested, and its essence is mingled — ⟪ar:مُعتقدٌ مصاصُہُ⟫ — with conviction." In Arabic the word ⟪ar:’مصاص‘⟫ means to suck, and the subtle pith of any object is that which holds its essence — just as the origin of a fruit is its juice, drawn out by sucking. The sincerity of ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ that has been thus tested is the spiritual substance of the soul itself, not a notion arising from the utterance of the formula or its outward meaning. The words of the testimony are only an echo of a spiritual substance fixed within the heart at the level of concept (mafhūm).

You return then to the saying: those things are easy for them which are difficult for the extravagant, and they love that which is alien to the ignorant. In one sense this concerns "suffering"; in another it concerns "death" itself. For the ignorant, death is a terrible disintegration in which one is parted from the body.
