For him it is the end of life rather than its beginning — the severance from that on which he has fixed all his attention his whole life long. For the wise, by contrast, death is the name of salvation from suffering and of the encounter with God; for him it is the completion of monotheism (tawḥīd), in which he is taken up into His transcendent realm and becomes "one" with Him. Only one who plunges into this sea can taste the sweetness of its waters. The heat of this whole consumes every part to ashes. Those who remain slaves to their ego stay entangled in the outward and inward aspects of the parts. The wise man, however, remains fixed upon the remembrance of the absolute Morrow, and the joy that issues from it dislodges his ego and shatters all his illusions.

<!-- section 8 (id=3583, raw_sort=8): عدل کا فلسفہ  -->

## The Philosophy of Justice

The finest expression of the Commander of the Faithful's — ⟪ar:أمیر المومنین⟫ — philosophy of ⟪ar:’عدل‘⟫ (ʿadl, justice) is found in the letter he addressed to ⟪ar:’مالک اشتر بن الحارث النخئی‘⟫ (Mālik al-Ashtar al-Nakhaʿī), the captain of his army, when he appointed him governor of Egypt.[^cite-18] In his view, the orientation of moral law toward justice is not bound to the outward world alone; it extends to the spiritual world as well. The principles of justice he sets forth transcend the constraints of any single process. In his sayings, thought and act appear as close-knit complements, mirroring the message of ⟪ar:’توحید‘⟫ (tawḥīd, divine unity — the calling to be one). The lives of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and ʿAlī (upon him be peace) are the living embodiment of these principles.

The first point is this: the Commander of the Faithful — ⟪ar:امیر المونین⟫ — was himself the perfect embodiment of justice. The second is that within the foundations of his justice we find profound spiritual lessons — how a life passed in love of God naturally yields a life of beauty. A life that resembles ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ (al-Ḥaqq, the Real) within itself. If we look at the ethics of ⟪ar:’أحسان‘⟫ (iḥsān, beautiful action) within the broader compass of morals, we find that the conjunction of moral and spiritual dimensions opens a depth that gives both their proper ground. The common question of right and wrong is thereby reshaped into the deeper question: "What is reality?"

ʿAlī's spiritual vision of monotheism is not only that there is no peer to God, but that nothing stands against Him. For this reason every good deed — ⟪ar:حَسَنَ⟫ — that is a sign of God is not the antithesis of a moral evil. ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ is a singular and individual existence in its own right; over against it, if anything stands at all, it is only ⟪ar:’عدم‘⟫ (ʿadam, non-being). If goodness, then, is on the positive side of ⟪ar:الحق⟫, evil is the "capacity" or "intention" to negate it. In other words, goodness is an attribute of the Creator, while evil is an attribute of the creature He has formed. As God says:

> ⟪quran 113:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ ‎⟫
> *"From the evil of what He has created;*
> from the evil of His creatures.
> — **Quran 113:2 (inline widget)**

This verse is often mistranslated as "the evil that God has created" — a rendering false both in religion and in language. By saying ⟪ar:‏مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ،⟫ God plainly states that the "evil" came from "what He created"; that is, He created free creatures endowed with good qualities, and the creatures themselves brought "evil" into being by negating those qualities. It cannot therefore be said that God created evil. He created only the conditions in which His creatures, of their own choosing, took part in evil — even though they could have chosen the truth. This proves that evil is in reality nothing other than the negation of good, and possesses no existence of its own. The verse may also be read in the sense: I take refuge in the "truth" from the "untruth." Evil appears only as a negation of the truth, and the eye of the heart perceives it as an "illusion." Just as every illusion can be dispelled by reason, so truth and goodness possess the power to overcome every evil. The more a soul becomes an advocate before its Lord, the more it overcomes evil through the firmness of its will. This maturity passes from the intellect into the heart, persuading it that good is more truly ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ than evil, strengthened by its own knowledge. Since evil has no existence, and is only a thing that has slipped from its proper place, what is needed is to overcome it and restore it to the truth. For this reason, in the eyes of the Commander of the Faithful, the discharge of obligations and of rights toward all — toward God, toward oneself, and toward the whole of creation — is the very definition of justice. Pointing to this, he says: "Justice is the placing of things in their proper stations."[^cite-19] The more a man's actions accord with their proper place, the more just he becomes; and this essence of justice will be present in him in the measure that he is bound to ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫. First a man must be "good"; only then will he be able to do "good"; and to be ⟪ar:الحق⟫ is to become "one" — ⟪ar:توحید⟫ — for He alone is ⟪ar:الحق⟫.

An analysis of the letter he wrote to ⟪ar:مالک اشتر⟫ shows that justice is not the name of any one of the virtues, but the name of their sum — and most especially of the three virtues of temperance, courage, and wisdom. When these three stand in their proper places, only then can the self be called just.[^cite-20]

Ethics and spirituality are inseparably interwoven. This is confirmed by the tradition that once, while the Messenger of God was seated among his companions, Gabriel came to him in the form of a man and said: ⟪ar:یا محمد (ﷺ)!⟫ "Tell me of ⟪ar:’اسلام‘⟫." He replied: ⟪ar:الأسلام⟫ "It is to bear witness that there is no god but God and that Muḥammad is His Messenger, to perform the prayer, to give the alms, to fast in Ramaḍān, and to make pilgrimage to the House of God." Gabriel said: "You have spoken truly!" Then he asked: "Tell me of ⟪ar:’ایمان‘⟫." He replied: "It is to believe in God, in His angels, in His books, in His messengers, and in the reward and punishment of the Hereafter." Gabriel said: "You have spoken truly!" Then he asked: "Tell me of ⟪ar:’أحسان‘⟫." He replied: "It is to worship God as though you see Him; for though you do not see Him, He nonetheless sees you."

*Note:* The literal meaning of iḥsān is "to do beautifully," for the word iḥsān is derived from ḥasana, which means to be beautiful. Goodness is called ḥasan in Arabic and evil qabīḥ — literally, beauty and ugliness.

The constant presence of God and the awareness of standing beneath His gaze runs as a thread through all these grand stations, as the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "Worship God as though He were visible." Hence the concept of beneficence is rooted in Islam. ʿAlī, on the one hand, says in his sermons: "Know that every action you perform depends on your prayer — that is, on how you regard 'goodness'." On the other hand, he says that ostentation, pride, and self-praise are the most powerful traps of Satan, by which he destroys those who would be ⟪ar:محسنین⟫ and ruins their ⟪ar:احسان⟫. The whole purpose of worship is the dissolution of one's selfhood, of egoism — ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫ — and of "I-ness" — ⟪ar:أنائیت⟫ — in the sight of God. The first of your quotations calls for justice, which places all things, oneself included, in their rightful stations; the second explains the cause of every injustice as ⟪ar:کبر⟫ (kibr, arrogance), ⟪ar:حرس⟫ (ḥirṣ, avarice), and ⟪ar:حسد⟫ (ḥasad, envy) — these being what are called ⟪ar:’أمہات معاصی‘⟫ (the mothers of all sins).

[^cite-16]: Cited in the JSONL block below.
[^cite-17]: Cited in the JSONL block below.
[^cite-18]: Cited in the JSONL block below.
[^cite-19]: Cited in the JSONL block below.
[^cite-20]: Cited in the JSONL block below.

<!-- section 9 (id=3582, raw_sort=9): مالک اشتر کے نام خط -->
## Letter to Mālik al-Ashtar

This is what the servant of God, ʿAlī, Amīr al-Muʾminīn, ordered Mālik ibn al-Ḥārith al-Ashtar in his instrument of appointment (ʿahd, the covenant of investiture) when he made him governor of Egypt — charged with the collection of its revenues, the prosecution of war against its enemies, the welfare of its people, and the prospering of its towns.[^cite-21]

⟪ar-quote:هذَا مَا أَمَرَ بِهِ عَبْدُ اللهِ عَلِيٌ أَميِرُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، مَالِكَ بْنَ الْحَارِثِ الاْشْتَرَ فِي عَهْدِهِ إِلَيْهِ، حِينَ وَلاَّهُ مِصْرَ- جِبْوةَ خَرَاجِهَا، وَجِهَادَ عَدُوِّهَا، وَاسْتِصْلاَحَ أَهْلِهَا، وَعِمَارَةَ بِلاَدِهَا⟫

He commanded him to fear God, to prefer obedience to Him above all else, and to follow what He has enjoined in His Book — both its obligations and its recommended observances — for none attains felicity save through following them, and none falls into misery save by denying and neglecting them. He further commanded him to aid God, glorified is He, with his heart, his hand, and his tongue, for He whose name is sublime has pledged to assist whoever assists Him and to honour whoever honours Him. He bade him also to break the self at the rising of its passions and to restrain it when it bolts, for the soul is ever inciting to evil except where God has shown mercy.

⟪ar-quote:أَمَرَهُ بِتَقْوَى اللهِ، وَإِيثَارِ طَاعَتِهِ، وَاتِّبَاعِ مَا أَمَرَ بِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ- مِنْ فَرَائِضِهِ وَسُنَنِهِ، الَّتِي لاَ يَسْعَدُ أَحَدٌ إِلاَّ بِاتِّبَاعِهَا، وَلاَ يَشْقَى إِلاَّ مَعَ جُحُودِهَا وَإِضَاعَتِهَا، وَأَنْ يَنْصُرَ اللهَ سُبْحَانَهُ بَيَدِهِ وَقَلْبِهِ وَلِسَانِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ، جَلَّ اسْمُهُ، قَدْ تَكَفَّلَ بِنَصْرِ مَنْ نَصَرَهُ، وَإِعْزَازِ مَنْ أَعَزَّهُ. وَأَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَكْسِرَ نَفْسَهُ عِنْدَ الشَّهَوَاتِ، وَيَزَعَهَا عِنْدَ الْجَمَحَاتِ، فَإِنَّ النَّفْسَ أَمَّارَةٌ بِالسُّوءِ، إِلاَّ مَا رَحِمَ اللهُ⟫

### The Qualifications of a Governor and His Responsibilities

Know then, O Mālik, that I have dispatched you to a land over which governments have passed before you — some just, some tyrannical. The people will now scrutinize your conduct as you once scrutinized the conduct of the rulers before you, and they will speak of you as you once spoke of them. The righteous are known only through what God circulates of their reputation upon the tongues of His servants. Let the dearest of all treasures to you, therefore, be the treasury of good deeds. Master your passions, and be miserly with your soul against what is not lawful for you — for true miserliness with the soul is its dispensing of justice in what it loves and what it loathes.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْلَمْ يَا مَالكُ، أَنِّي قدْ وَجَّهْتُكَ إِلَى بِلاَد قَدْ جَرَتْ عَلَيْهَا دُوَلٌ قَبْلَكَ، مِنْ عَدْل وَجَوْر، وَأَنَّ النَّاسَ يَنْظُرُونَ مِنْ أُمُورِكَ فِى مِثْلِ مَا كُنْتَ تَنْظُرُ فِيهِ مِنْ أُمُورِ الْوُلاَةِ قَبْلَكَ، وَيَقُولُونَ فِيكَ مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِيهِمْ،إِنَّمَا يُسْتَدَلُّ عَلَى الصَّالِحِينَ بِمَا يُجْرِي اللهُ لَهُمْ عَلَى أَلْسُنِ عِبَادِهِ. فَلْيَكُنْ أَحَبَّ الذَّخَائِرِ إِلَيْكَ ذَخِيرَةُ الْعَمَلِ الصَّالِحِ، فَامْلِكْ هَوَاكَ، وَشُحَّ بِنَفْسِكَ عَمَّا لاَ يَحِلُّ لَكَ، فَإِنَّ الشُّحَّ بِالنَّفْسِ الاْنْصَافُ مِنْهَا فَيَما أَحْبَبْتَ وَكَرِهْتَ⟫

Habituate your heart to mercy for the subjects (raʿiyya), to love for them and kindness towards them. Never carry yourself among them as a ravening beast that counts their devouring its prize, for they are of two kinds: a brother to you in religion or a fellow to you in creation. Slips will issue from them and defects will overtake them; wrong will be done at their hands, whether intentionally or by error. Extend to them, then, the same pardon and forbearance that you would wish God to extend to you, for you stand above them, and the commander of the affair (the Imām) stands above you, and God stands above the one who appointed you. He has charged you with the management of their affairs and tested you through them.[^cite-22]

⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْعِرْ قَلْبَكَ الرَّحْمَةَ لِلرَّعِيَّةِ، وَالْـمَحَبَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَاللُّطْفَ بِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَكُونَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ سَبُعاً ضَارِياً تَغْتَنِمُ أَكْلَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهُمْ صِنْفَانِ- إِمَّا أَخٌ لَكَ فِي الدِّينِ، وَإمّا نَظِيرٌ لَكَ فِي الْخَلْقِ، يَفْرُطُ مِنْهُمُ الزَّلَلُ، وَتَعْرِضُ لَهُمُ الْعِلَلُ،يُؤْتَى عَلَى أَيْدِيهِمْ فِي الَعَمْدِ وَالْخَطَاَ، فَأَعْطِهِمْ مِنْ عَفْوِكَ وَصَفْحِكَ مِثْلَ الَّذِي تُحِبُّ أَنْ يُعْطِيَكَ اللهُ مِنْ عَفْوِهِ وَصَفْحِهِ، فَإِنَّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ، وَ وَالِي الاْمْرِ عَلَيْكَ فَوْقَكَ، وَاللهُ فَوْقَ مَنْ وَلاَّكَ! وَقَدِ اسْتَكْفَاكَ أَمْرَهُمْ، وَابْتَلاَكَ بِهِمْ⟫

Do not set yourself up for battle against God, for you have no power against His retribution and no exemption from your need of His pardon and mercy. Never regret a pardon granted; never exult over a punishment carried out. Do not yield in haste to an impulse from which a way of avoidance is open. And do not say, "I have been given command; I order and am obeyed." Such speech sows corruption in the heart, weakens the religion, and brings ruin near. If the office in which you sit ever stirs in you pride or self-conceit, lift your gaze to the immensity of the dominion of God above you and to His power over what you possess no power over even in yourself. Such reflection lowers the soaring of your ambition, blunts the edge of your temper, and restores to you the reason that had slipped away.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْصِبَنَّ نَفْسَكَ لِحَرْبِ اللهِ، فَإِنَّهْ لاَيَدَيْ لَكَ بِنِقْمَتِهِ، وَلاَ غِنَى بِكَ عَنْ عَفْوِهِ وَرَحْمَتِهِ. وَلاَ تَنْدَمَنَّ عَلَى عَفْو، وَلاَ تَبْجَحَنَّ بِعُقُوبَة، وَلاَ تُسْرِعَنَّ إِلَى بَادِرَة وَجَدْتَ مِنْهَا مَنْدُوحَةً، وَلاَ تَقُولَنَّ- إِنِّي مُؤَمَّرٌ آمُرُ فَأُطَاعُ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ إِدْغَالٌ فِي الْقَلْبِ، وَمَنْهَكَةٌ لِلدِّينِ، وَتَقَرُّبٌ مِنَ الْغِيَرِ. وَإِذَا أَحْدَثَ لَكَ مَا أَنْتَ فِيهِ مِنْ سُلْطَانِكَ أُبَّهَةً أَوْ مَخِيلَةً، فَانْظُرْ إِلَى عِظَمِ مُلْكِ اللهِ فَوْقَكَ، وَقُدْرَتِهِ مَنْكَ عَلَى مَا لاَ تَقْدرِ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ يُطَامِنُ إِلَيْكَ مِنْ طِمَاحِكَ، وَيَكُفُّ عَنْكَ مِنْ غَرْبِكَ،يَفِيءُ إِلَيْكَ بِمَا عَزَبَ عَنْكَ مِنْ عَقْلِكَ⟫

Beware of vying with God in His greatness or likening yourself to Him in His omnipotence — for God abases every tyrant and disgraces every man given to pride.

⟪ar-quote:إِيَّاكَ وَمُسَامَاةَ اللهِ فِي عَظَمَتِهِ، وَالتَّشَبُّهَ بِهِ فِي جَبَرُوتِهِ، فَإِنَّ اللهَ يُذِلُّ كُلَّ جَبَّار، وَيُهِينُ كُلَّ مُخْتَال⟫

Render justice towards God, and render justice towards the people from yourself, from those closest to you among your family, and from any of your subjects whom you favour. For if you do not, you will be a tyrant; and whoever wrongs the servants of God has, in place of His servants, God Himself as his adversary. Whenever God becomes the adversary of a man, He demolishes his plea, and that man remains in a state of war with God until he desists and repents. Nothing is more apt to overturn the bounty of God or to hasten His vengeance than persistence in oppression — for God hears the cry of the oppressed and lies in wait for the oppressors.

⟪ar-quote:أَنْصِفِ اللهَ وَأَنْصِفِ النَّاسَ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، وَمِنْ خَاصَّةِ أَهْلِكَ، وَمَنْ لَكَ فِيهِ هَوىً مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّكَ إِلاَّ تَفْعَلْ تَظْلِمْ، وَمَنْ ظَلَمَ عِبَادَ اللهِ كَانَ اللهُ خَصْمَهُ دُونَ عِبَادِهِ، وَمَنْ خَاصَمَهُ اللهُ أَدْحَضَ حُجَّتَهُ، وَكَانَ لله حَرْباً حَتَّى يَنْزعَ وَيَتُوبَ. وَلَيْسَ شَيْءٌ أَدْعَى إِلَى تَغْيِيرِ نِعْمَةِ اللهِ وَتَعْجِيلِ نِقْمَتِهِ مِنْ إِقَامَة عَلَى ظُلْم، فَإِنَّ اللهَ سَميِعٌ دَعْوَةَ الْمَظْلُومِينَ، وَهُوَ لِلظَّالِمِينَ بِالْمِرْصَادِ⟫

The course most beloved to you should be the one most balanced in truth, most universal in justice, and most apt to win the contentment of the subjects — for the displeasure of the common people overwhelms the favour of the elite, while the displeasure of the elite is bearable so long as the common people are content. None among the subjects is more burdensome to the ruler in seasons of ease, less helpful in seasons of distress, more averse to equity, more importunate in petition, less grateful when given, less ready to accept reasons when refused, and weaker in patience under the calamities of time than the elite. The pillar of the religion, the body of the Muslims, and the array against the enemies, is the common people of the community. Let your inclination, therefore, be towards them and your leaning with them.

⟪ar-quote:كُنْ أَحَبَّ الاْمُورِ إِلَيْكَ أَوْسَطُهَا فِي الْحَقِّ، وَأَعَمُّهَا فِي الْعَدْلِ، وَأَجْمَعُهَا لِرِضَى الرَّعِيَّةِ، فَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْعَامَّةِ يُجْحِفُ بِرِضَى الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْخَاصَّةِ يُغْتَفَرُ مَعَ رِضَى الْعَامَّةِ. وَلَيْسَ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الرَّعِيَّةِ، أَثْقَلَ عَلَى الْوَالِي مَؤُونَةً فِي الرَّخَاءِ، وَأَقَلَّ مَعُونَةً لَهُ فِي الْبَلاَءِ، وَأَكْرَهَ لِلاْنْصَافِ، وَأَسْأَلَ بِالاْلْحَافِ، وَأَقَلَّ شُكْراً عِنْدَ الاْعْطَاءِ، وَأَبْطَأَ عُذْراً عِنْدَ الْمَنْعِ، وَأَضْعَفَ صَبْراً عِنْدَ مُلِمَّاتِ الدَّهْرِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّمَا عَمُودُ الدِّينِ، وَجِمَاعُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، وَالْعُدَّةُ لِلاْعْدَاءِ، الْعَامَّةُ مِنَ الاْمَّةِ، فَلْيَكُنْ صِغْوُكَ لَهُمْ، وَمَيْلُكَ مَعَهُمْ⟫

The man among your subjects most distant from you, and most odious in your sight, should be the one most eager to pry into the faults of the people; for people do have faults, and the ruler is the one most obliged to conceal them. Do not bring to light what has been hidden from you; your duty is only to set right what is manifest, while God will judge what is veiled from you. Cover faults, then, as far as you are able, and God will cover those of yours that you would wish to keep hidden from your subjects. Loose every knot of rancour among the people; sever from yourself the cause of every vendetta. Feign unawareness of whatever is not plain to you. Do not hasten to credit the report of a slanderer, for the slanderer is a deceiver however much he resembles those who counsel sincerely.

⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ أَبْعَدَ رَعِيَّتِكَ مِنْكَ، وَأشْنَأَهُمْ عِنْدَكَ، أَطْلَبُهُمْ لِمَعَائِبِ النَّاسِ، فإنَّ في النَّاسِ عُيُوباً، الْوَالِي أَحَقُّ مَنْ سَتَرَهَا، فَلاَ تَكْشِفَنَّ عَمَّا غَابَ عَنْكَ مِنْهَا، فَإنَّمَا عَلَيْكَ تَطْهِيرُ مَا ظَهَرَ لَكَ، وَاللهُ يَحْكُمُ عَلَى مَا غَابَ عَنْكَ، فَاسْتُرِ الْعَوْرَةَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتَ يَسْتُرِ اللهُ مِنْكَ ما تُحِبُّ سَتْرَهُ مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ. أَطْلِقْ عَنِ النَّاسِ عُقْدَةَ كُلِّ حِقْد، وَاقْطَعْ عَنْكَ سَبَبَ كُلِّ وِتْر، وَتَغَابَ عَنْ كلِّ مَا لاَ يَضِحُ لَكَ، وَلاَ تَعْجَلَنَّ إِلَى تَصْدِيقِ سَاع، فَإِنَّ السَّاعِيَ غَاشٌ،⟫

Do not admit into your council a miser, who would turn you aside from generosity and threaten you with poverty; nor a coward, who would weaken your resolve in your affairs; nor a covetous man, who would dress up rapacity through injustice as something fair. Miserliness, cowardice, and greed are distinct dispositions which a single ill opinion of God draws together.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تُدْخِلَنَّ فِي مَشُورَتِكَ بَخِيلاً يَعْدِلُ بِكَ عَنِ الْفَضْلِ، وَيَعِدُكَ الْفَقْرَ، وَلاَ جَبَاناً يُضعِّفُكَ عَنِ الاْمُورِ، وَلاَ حَرِيصاً يُزَيِّنُ لَكَ الشَّرَهَ بِالْجَوْرِ، فَإِنَّ الْبُخْلَ وَالْجُبْنَ وَالْحِرْصَ غَرَائِزُ شَتَّى يَجْمَعُهَا سُوءُ الظَّنِّ بِاللهِ⟫

The worst of your ministers is he who served as minister to the wicked before you and partook with them in their sins. Such a man shall not be of your inner circle, for these are the helpers of sinners and the brothers of oppressors. You will find good substitutes for them among those who possess like opinion and effectiveness, yet are unburdened by their loads and crimes — men who never aided a wrongdoer in his wrong nor a sinner in his sin. They will impose the least cost upon you and render the best support; they will incline most tenderly towards you and least towards others. Take them, then, as your chosen companions in privacy and in public assembly alike.

⟪ar-quote:شَرُّ وُزَرَائِكَ مَنْ كَانَ لِلاْشْرَارِ قَبْلَكَ وَزِيراً، وَمَنْ شَرِكَهُمْ فِي الاْثَامِ، فَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ لَكَ بِطَانَةً، فَإِنَّهُمْ أَعْوَانُ الاْثَمَةِ، وَإِخْوَانُ الظَّلَمَةِ، وَأَنْتَ وَاجِدٌ مِنْهُمْ خَيْرَ الْخَلَفِ مِمَّنْ لَهُ مِثْلُ آرَائِهِمْ وَنَفَاذِهِمْ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ آصَارِهِمْ وَأَوْزَارِهِمْ وَ آثَامِهِمْ، مِمَّنْ لَمْ يُعَاوِنْ ظَالِماً عَلَى ظُلْمِهِ، وَلاَ آثِماً عَلَى إِثْمِهِ، أُولئِكَ أَخَفُّ عَلَيْكَ مَؤُونَةً، وَأَحْسَنُ لَكَ مَعُونَةً، وَأَحْنَى عَلَيْكَ عَطْفاً، وَأَقَلُّ لِغَيْرِكَ إِلْفاً، فَاتَّخِذْ أُولئِكَ خَاصَّةً لِخَلَوَاتِكَ وَحَفَلاَتِكَ⟫

Then, among them, let the most preferred in your sight be those who speak the bitter truth openly before you and lend you least support in those of your acts which God dislikes in His friends, however much such acts may accord with your wishes. Cleave to people of scrupulousness (waraʿ) and truthfulness, and then train them not to extol you, nor to exult you with falsehood concerning a deed you did not perform — for an excess of praise breeds vainglory and brings one near to arrogance.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ لْيَكُنْ آثَرُهُمْ عِنْدَكَ أَقْوَلَهُمْ بِمُرِّ الْحَقِّ لَكَ، وأَقَلَّهُمْ مُسَاعَدَةً فِيَما يَكُونُ مِنْكَ مِمَّا كَرِهَ اللهُ لاِوْلِيَائِهِ، وَاقِعاً ذلِكَ مِنْ هَوَاكَ حَيْثُ وَقَعَ. وَالْصَقْ بِأَهْلِ الْوَرَعِ وَالصِّدْقِ، ثُمَّ رُضْهُمْ عَلَى أَلاَّ يُطْرُوكَ وَلاَ يُبَجِّحُوكَ بِبَاطِل لَمْ تَفْعَلْهُ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الاْطْرَاءِ تُحْدِثُ الزَّهْوَ، وَتُدْنِي مِنَ الْعِزَّةِ⟫

The virtuous and the vicious must not stand in equal rank before you, for to do so dissuades the virtuous from virtue and habituates the vicious to vice. Confine each to the standing he has assigned himself. Know that nothing is more apt to draw the favourable opinion of a ruler towards his subjects than his beneficence to them, his lightening of their burdens, and his refraining from pressing them to what he has no right to demand. Let your conduct, therefore, follow a course that will gather to you a good opinion of your subjects, for a good opinion will spare you long fatigue. The most deserving of your good opinion is the one whom you have well treated; the most deserving of your suspicion is the one whom you have ill treated.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ الْـمُحْسِنُ وَالْمُسِيءُ عِنْدَكَ بِمَنْزِلَة سَوَاء، فَإِنَّ فِي ذلِكَ تَزْهِيداً لاِهْلِ الاْحْسَانِ فِي الاْحْسَانِ،تَدْرِيباً لاِهْلِ الاْسَاءَةِ عَلَى الاْسَاءَةِ، وَأَلْزِمْ كُلاًّ مِنْهُمْ مَا أَلْزَمَ نَفْسَهُ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ شَيْءٌ بِأَدْعَى إِلَى حُسْنِ ظَنِّ وَال بِرَعِيَّتِهِ مِنْ إحْسَانِهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، وَتَخْفِيفِهِ الْمَؤُونَاتِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِكْرَاهِهِ إِيَّاهُمْ عَلَى مَا لَيْسَ لهُ قِبَلَهُمْ، فَلْيَكُنْ مِنْكَ فِي ذلِكَ أَمْرٌ يَجَتَمِعُ لَكَ بِهِ حُسْنُ الظَّنِّ بِرَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّ حُسْنَ الظَّنِّ يَقْطَعُ عَنْكَ نَصَباً طَوِيلاً، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ حَسُنَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ حَسُنَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ سَاءَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ سَاءَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ⟫

Do not abolish the noble usages (sunan ṣāliḥa) by which the foremost of this community lived, through which concord was gathered and the subjects flourished. Do not initiate any practice that injures any portion of those earlier usages — for the reward of those who established them will run on, and the burden of your abolishing them will fall upon you. Increase your study with the learned (ʿulamāʾ) and your converse with the wise (ḥukamāʾ) for the consolidation of what has set the affairs of your lands in order and for the continuance of what your predecessors had established.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْقُضْ سُنَّةً صَالِحَةً عَمِلَ بِهَا صُدُورُ هذِهِ الاْمَّةِ، وَاجْتَمَعتْ بِهَا الاْلْفَةُ، وَصَلَحَتْ عَلَيْهَا الرَّعِيَّةُ،لاَ تُحْدِثَنَّ سُنَّةً تَضُرُّ بِشَيء مِنْ مَاضِي تِلْكَ السُّنَنِ، فَيَكُونَ الاْجْرُ بِمَنْ سَنَّهَا، وَالْوِزْرُ عَلَيْكَ بِمَا نَقَضْتَ مِنْهَا. وَأَكْثِرْ مُدَارَسَةَ الَعُلَمَاءِ، وَمُنَافَثَةَ الْحُكَمَاءِ، فِي تَثْبِيتِ مَا صَلَحَ عَلَيْهِ أَمْرُ بِلاَدِكَ،⟫

Know that the people are constituted of classes, none of which prospers save through the others, and none of which can dispense with the rest. Among them are the army of God; the secretaries of the common people and of the elite; the judges of equity; the agents of justice and conciliation; the payers of poll-tax (jizya) and land-tax (kharāj) — both the protected non-Muslims (ahl al-dhimma) and the common Muslims; the merchants and artisans; and finally the lowest class, the needy and the destitute. For each of these God has fixed a share and set down within His Book or in the practice (sunna) of His Prophet — God's blessings be upon him and his family — a precept concerning its limits and its due, a covenant preserved with us.[^cite-23]

⟪ar-quote:وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الرَّعِيَّةَ طَبَقَاتٌ لاَ يَصْلُحُ بَعْضُهَا إلاَّ بِبَعْض، وَلاَ غِنَى بِبَعْضِهَا عَنْ بَعْض- فَمِنْهَا جُنُودُ اللهِ،مِنْهَا كُتَّابُ الْعَامَّةِ وَالْخَاصَّةِ، وَمِنْهَا قُضَاةُ الْعَدْلِ، وَمِنهَا عُمَّالُ الاْنْصَافِ وَالرِّفْقِ، وَمِنْهَا أَهْلُ الْجِزْيَةِ وَالْخَراجِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الذِّمَّةِ وَمُسْلِمَةِ النَّاسِ، وَمِنْهَا التُّجَّارُ وَأَهْلُ الصِّنَاعَاتِ، وَمِنهَا الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ ذَوِي الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ، وَكُلٌّ قَدْ سَمَّى اللهُ سَهْمَهُ، وَوَضَعَ عَلَى حَدِّهِ وَفَرِيضَتِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ أَوْ سُنَّةِ نَبِيِّهِ (صلى الله عليه وآله)عَهْداً مِنْهُ عِنْدَنَا مَحْفُوظاً⟫

The army, by God's leave, is the fortress of the subjects, the ornament of rulers, the strength of the religion, and the means of peace. The subjects cannot stand without the army, and the army can be maintained only by the revenues which God draws out for them — by which they gain the strength to wage war on their enemy, on which their own welfare rests, and which suffices their need. Yet these two classes cannot stand except through a third: the judges, the executive officers, and the secretaries, who weld contracts firm, gather the public benefits, and are entrusted with both special and general affairs.

⟪ar-quote:فَالْجُنُودُ، بِإِذْنِ اللهِ، حُصُونُ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَزَيْنُ الْوُلاَةِ، وعِزُّ الدِّينِ، وَسُبُلُ الاْمْنِ، وَلَيْسَ تَقُومُ الرَّعِيَّةُ إِلاَّ بِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِلْجُنُودِ إِلاَّ بِمَا يُخْرِجُ اللهُ لَهُمْ مِنَ الْخَرَاجِ الَّذِي يَقْوَوْنَ بِهِ فِي جِهَادِ عَدُوِهِمْ، وَيَعْتَمِدُونَ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما أصْلَحهُمْ، وَيَكُونُ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حَاجَتِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِهذَيْنِ الصِّنْفَيْنِ إِلاَّ بِالصِّنْفِ الثَّالِثِ مِنَ الْقُضَاةِ وَالْعُمَّالِ وَالْكُتَّابِ، لِمَا يُحْكِمُونَ مِنَ الْمَعَاقِدِ، وَيَجْمَعُونَ مِنْ الْمَنَافِعِ، وَيُؤْتَمَنُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ خَوَاصِّ الاْمُورِ وَعَوَامِّهَا⟫

And none of these classes can stand except through the merchants and the men of industry, who furnish them their necessities, establish the markets, and provide what others cannot accomplish with their own hands. After them comes the lowest class, the people of need and destitution, whose support and provision are a binding duty. With God there is room for every one of them, and every one of them has a right upon the ruler in proportion to what is needed for his well-being. The ruler does not discharge what God has truly bound upon him in this regard save through diligence, by seeking God's help, by setting his soul to cleave to the truth, and by enduring upon it whatever weighs light or weighs heavy.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ قِوَامَ لَهُمْ جَمِيعاً إِلاَّ بِالتُّجَّارِ وَذَوِي الصِّنَاعَاتِ، فِيَما يَجْتَمِعُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ مَرَافِقِهِمْ، وَيُقِيمُونَهُ مِنْ أَسْوَاقِهِمْ، وَيَكْفُونَهُمْ مِنَ التَّرَفُّقِ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ ممّا لاَ يَبْلُغُهُ رِفْقُ غَيْرِهِمْ. ثُمَّ الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ الَّذِينَ يَحِقُّ رِفْدُهُمْ وَمَعُونَتُهُمْ. وَفِي اللهِ لِكُلّ سَعَةٌ، وَلِكُلٍّ عَلَى الْوَالِي حَقٌ بِقَدْرِ مَا يُصْلِحُهُ. وَلَيْسَ يَخْرُجُ الْوَالِي مِنْ حَقِيقَةِ مَا أَلْزَمَهُ اللهُ مِنْ ذلِكَ إِلاَّ بِالاْهْتِمامِ وَالاسْتِعَانَةِ بِاللهِ، وَتَوْطِينِ نَفْسِهِ عَلَى لُزُومِ الْحَقِّ، وَالصَّبْرِ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما خَفَّ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ ثَقُلَ

.⟫

### 1. The Army

Set in command of your forces the man who, in your considered judgement, is the most sincere well-wisher of God, of His Prophet, and of your Imām. **Let him be the chastest of them in heart and the highest of them in forbearance (ḥilm): slow to take fire in anger, ready to accept an excuse, gentle with the weak and firm with the strong; one whom violence will not provoke and weakness will not leave inert.**

⟪ar-quote:فَوَلِّ مِنْ جُنُودِكَ أَنْصَحَهُمْ فِي نَفْسِكَ لله وَلِرَسُولِهِ وَلاِمَامِكَ، وَأَنْقَاهُمْ جَيْباً، وَأَفْضَلَهُمْ حِلْماً مِمَّنْ يُبْطِىءُ عَنِ الْغَضَبِ، وَيَسْتَرِيحُ إِلَى الْعُذْرِ، وَيَرْأَفُ بِالضُّعَفَاءِ، وَيَنْبُو عَلَى الاْقْوِيَاءِ، وَمِمَّنْ لاَ يُثِيرُهُ الْعُنْفُ، وَلاَ يَقْعُدُ بِهِ الضَّعْفُ⟫

Then attach to yourself men of nobility (murūʾa) and of honourable descent, from virtuous houses and of fair antecedents, then men of bravery and valour, of generosity and openhandedness — for they are the gathering-points of nobility and the branches of beneficence. Inquire after their affairs as parents inquire after the affairs of their child. Let nothing you do to strengthen them seem too great in your own eyes, and never count any small kindness extended to them as too trifling to bestow, however slight — for such kindness will move them to render you sincere counsel and to think well of you. Do not neglect attention to their small matters in reliance upon attention to the great, for your small kindness has its place where they will profit by it, while your great kindness has a station they cannot do without.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ الْصَقْ بَذَوِي الْمُرُوءَاتِ وَالاْحْسَابِ، وَأَهْلِ الْبُيُوتَاتِ الصَّالِحَةِ، وَالسَّوَابِقِ الْحَسَنَةِ، ثُمَّ أَهْلِ النَّجْدَةِ وَالشَّجَاعَةِ، وَالسَّخَاءِ وَالسَّماحَةِ، فَإِنَّهُمْ جِمَاعٌ مِنَ الْكَرَمِ، وَشُعَبٌ مِنَ الْعُرْفِ. ثُمَّ تَفَقَّدْ مِنْ أُمُورِهِمْ مَا يَتَفَقَّدُهُ الْوَالِدَانِ مِنْ وَلَدِهِمَا، وَلاَ يَتَفَاقَمَنَّ فِي نَفْسِكَ شَيْءٌ قَوَّيْتَهُمْ بِهِ، وَلاَ تَحْقِرَنَّ لُطْفاً تَعَاهَدْتَهُمْ بِهِ وَإِنْ قَلَّ، فَإِنَّهُ دَاعِيَةٌ لَهُمْ إِلَى بَذْلِ النَّصِيحَةِ لَكَ، وَحُسْنِ الظَّنِّ بِكَ. وَلاَ تَدَعْ تَفَقُّدَ لَطيِفِ أُمُورِهِمُ اتِّكَالاً عَلَى جَسِيمِهَا، فَإِنَّ لِلْيَسِيرِ مِنْ لُطْفِكَ مَوْضِعاً يَنْتَفِعُونَ بِهِ، وَلِلْجَسِيمِ مَوْقِعاً لاَ يَسْتَغْنُونَ عَنْهُ.⟫

Let the chief of your army be, in your sight, the one who shares the costs of their support, who spends from his own substance upon them and upon those of their households whom they have left behind — so that all their cares may converge into a single care for combat against the enemy. Your tenderness to them will turn their hearts towards you. The most pleasing thing for rulers is the establishment of justice in their lands and the manifest love of their subjects; yet that love appears only when the breasts of the people are clean, and their counsel rings true only when they surround the bearers of their affairs in protection, find their continuance no heavy thing, and do not look forward to the cutting short of their tenure. Open out their hopes, then; persist in fair praise of them; keep reckoning the trials borne by those among them who have been tried — for the frequent mention of their fine deeds shakes the brave to action and incites the laggard, if God so wills.

⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ آثَرُ رُؤوسِ جُنْدِكَ عِنْدَكَ مَنْ وَاسَاهُمْ فِي مَعُونَتِهِ، وَأَفْضَلَ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنْ جِدَتِهِ بِمَا يَسَعُهُمْ يَسَعُ مَنْ وَرَاءَهُمْ مِنْ خُلُوفِ أَهْلِيهِمْ حَتَّى يَكُونَ هَمُّهُمْ هَمّاً وَاحِداً فِي جِهَادِ الْعَدُوِّ، فَإِنَّ عَطْفَكَ عَلَيْهِمْ يَعْطِفُ قُلُوبَهُمْ عَلَيْكَ. وَإِنَّ أَفْضَلَ قُرَّةِ عَيْنِ الْوُلاَةِ اسْتِقَامَةُ الْعَدْلِ فِي الْبِلاَدِ، وَظُهُورُ مَوَدَّةِ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَإِنَّهُ لاَ تَظْهَرُ مَوَدَّتُهُمْ إِلاَّ بَسَلاَمَةِ صُدُورِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَصِحُّ نَصِيحَتُهُمْ إِلاّ بِحِيطَتِهِمْ عَلَى وُلاَةِ أُمُورِهِمْ، وَقِلَّةِ اسْتِثْقَالِ دُوَلِهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِبْطَاءِ انْقِطَاعِ مُدَّتِهِمْ. فَافْسَحْ فِي آمَالِهِمْ، وَوَاصِلْ فِي حُسْنِ الثَّنَاءِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَعْدِيدِ مَا أَبْلى ذَوُوالْبَلاَءِ مِنْهُمْ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الذِّكْرِ لِحُسْنِ أَفْعَالِهِمْ تَهُزُّ الشُّجَاعَ، وَتُحَرِّضُ النَّاكِلَ، إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ⟫

Recognize the trial borne by each one of them on its own terms; never attach one man's deed to another, and never measure the reward short of the extent of the deed. Let no man's eminence draw you to magnify a small deed of his into something great, and let no man's lowliness lead you to belittle a great deed of his into something small.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْرِفْ لِكُلِّ امْرِىء مِنْهُمْ مَا أَبْلى، وَلاَ تَضُمَّنَّ بَلاَءَ امْرِىء إِلَى غَيْرِهِ، وَلاَ تُقَصِّرَنَّ بِهِ دُونَ غَايَةِ بَلاَئِهِ، وَلاَ يَدْعُوَنَّكَ شَرَفُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تُعْظِمَ مِنْ بَلاَئِهِ مَا كَانَ صَغِيراً، وَلاَضَعَةُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تَسْتَصْغِرَ مِنْ يَلاَئِهِ مَاكَانَ عَظيِماً⟫

Refer back to God and His Messenger those affairs that perplex you and those matters that appear confused to you, for God — addressing a people whom He, the Sublime, wishes to guide — has said:

> ⟪quran 4:59⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوٓا۟ أَطِيعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا۟ ٱلرَّسُولَ وَأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَمْرِ مِنكُمْ ۖ فَإِن تَنَزَعْتُمْ فِى شَىْءٍۢ فَرُدُّوهُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِ وَٱلرَّسُولِ إِن كُنتُمْ تُؤْمِنُونَ بِٱللَّهِ وَٱلْيَوْمِ ٱلْآخِرِ ۚ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَحْسَنُ تَأْوِيلًا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Obey Allah and obey the Messenger (Muhammad PBUH), and those of you (Muslims) who are in authority.&nbsp;(And) if you differ in anything amongst yourselves, refer it to Allah and His Messenger (PBUH), if you believe in Allah and in the Last Day.&nbsp;That is better and more suitable for final determination.&nbsp;*
> O you who believe! Obey God and obey the Messenger and those in authority among you. And if you dispute among yourselves about anything, refer it to God and His Messenger, if you believe in God and the Last Day. That is better and better in the final issue.
> — **Quran 4:59 (inline widget)**

A further definition of justice (ʿadl) holds that all things are set in their proper stations and ranks in the Hereafter — in the sight of God — as they are also set in this world.

Considered in the governmental and social sphere, this principle yields the truth that justice arises only as the fruit of piety (taqwā) and uprightness. The Imām teaches that the right of the ruler over his subjects has its exact counterpart in the right of the subjects over their ruler. The ruler cannot be righteous ⟪ar:’صالح‘⟫ unless his subjects are righteous, and the subjects cannot be righteous unless the ruler is righteous. When the subjects fulfil the rights of their ruler and the ruler fulfils the rights of his subjects, the truth is honoured, the paths of religion prevail, and the banners of justice are set firmly in place. It is for this reason that so heavy an emphasis is placed upon the piety of the ruler.

When we examine the life of the Amīr al-Muʾminīn, we find it expended, in its entirety, in conformity with these divine principles and this divine disposition. Its full range cannot be set forth in any single account. Yet a single facet of it suffices to make the matter plain: the period following the assassination of ʿUthmān, when his outward caliphate was established. A careful reading of the history reveals that the civil strife provoked by Muʿāwiya's rebellion did not begin at Ṣiffīn but in Medina. When ʿAlī (peace be upon him) assumed the seat of the caliphate, his kinsman ⟪ar:ابن عباس⟫ counselled him to leave the heads of ʿUthmān's government in their posts for the present, removing them only once his own administration was in place. The Imām answered that he had no doubt his counsel was the wisest strategy for outward reconciliation. But, he said, ⟪ar:الادھی یلزمنی من الحق⟫ — the right binds me. Once I have come to know the truth concerning the governors set up by ʿUthmān, how can I keep them in their offices? By God, never shall I keep them in their offices!

He deposed Muʿāwiya, and all the other governors with him, the moment he came to the caliphate. To Ibn ʿAbbās the worldly success of the contrary course was plain enough: Muʿāwiya sought only earthly power and rule, and would have been content with the governance of Syria to the end of his days. Although historians have judged ʿAlī's act a political miscalculation, we ought rather to read his conduct through the lens of his aversion to this world and to its dominion and luxury. Wherever the comfort of the world has been secured at the cost of the principles of the Hereafter, the Imām has rejected such accommodation outright. As he wrote in another of his letters: when people abandon a portion of their religion for the sake of the world, God opens upon them in this world the gates of greater trouble still. It is therefore clear that for ʿAlī to have retained the men of the Uthmanic dispensation — whose corruption and wickedness were notorious — would have been a mere matter of expediency, the surrender of part of his religion for the sake of the world, an accommodation with it. Such a thought was, for him, unthinkable. In this decision, and in countless others of its kind, and most plainly of all in the letter to Mālik al-Ashtar, the same posture of his justice stands before us in open view.

[^cite-21]: See Nahj al-Balāgha, Letter 53 (the ʿAhd to Mālik al-Ashtar).
[^cite-22]: Cf. Qāḍī al-Nuʿmān, Daʿāʾim al-Islām, on the reciprocal rights binding ruler and ruled.
[^cite-23]: Cf. Qāḍī al-Nuʿmān, Daʿāʾim al-Islām, on the ordered classes of the Muslim polity and the share due to each.

<!-- section 11 (id=3594, raw_sort=11): عدل اور ظلم -->
## Justice and Tyranny

Because this letter is addressed to one of Mawlānā ʿAlī's dearest associates, his warning against tyranny must be understood in a specific register. These admonitions are directed not only at those who are already just and wish to govern with equity, but also at those who, while professing the philosophy of justice, remain susceptible to the pull of tyranny. For when the intoxication of rule rises within a man, it can transform even the just sovereign into an oppressor.

The potentiality for evil is latent in every human being. When this latent power is fused with personal resources, and when the ruler is bereft of divine support, then the potential state of evil becomes actual. At the opening of his letter to Mālik al-Ashtar, the Imam declares: "Give priority to the obedience of Allah over everything else, and obey the commandments contained in His Book; for he who follows ⟪ar:’سعد‘⟫ is made fortunate, and he who disregards ⟪ar:’خبیث‘⟫ is undone." This preamble is more than a formal opening — it is not merely a notification but a foundation. Obedience to Allah is not only obligatory; it confers spiritual liberty. Such obedience releases the soul from the tyranny of the soul itself, for the lower self commands evil until the mercy of the Lord intervenes — as the Qur'an records on the tongue of ⟪ar:حضرت یوسف علیہ السلام⟫:[^cite-24]

> ⟪quran 12:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَمَآ أُبَرِّئُ نَفْسِىٓ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلنَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌۢ بِٱلسُّوٓءِ إِلَّا مَا رَحِمَ رَبِّىٓ ۚ إِنَّ رَبِّى غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *"And I free not myself (from the blame). Verily, the (human) self is inclined to evil, except when my Lord bestows His Mercy (upon whom He wills). Verily, my Lord is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful."*
> And I do not say of my own acquittal. Indeed, the soul incites evil, except upon whom my Lord has mercy. Indeed my Lord is Forgiving and Merciful.
> — **Quran 12:53 (inline widget)**

The verse exhibits the precise relationship between divine compassion ⟪ar:رحم⟫ (raḥm, mercy) and the human self. Without the Lord's mercy the soul gravitates toward sin and excess; with that mercy it is freed from the snare of its own appetites and returns, satisfied, to its original nature. Hence the Qur'an addresses the tranquil soul:

> ⟪quran 89:27-29⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎ ‏ٱرْجِعِىٓ إِلَىٰ رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةًۭ مَّرْضِيَّةًۭ ‎ ‏فَٱدْخُلِى فِى عِبَدِى ‎⟫
> *(It will be said to the pious): "O (you) the one in (complete) rest and satisfaction! " Come back to your Lord, Well-pleased (yourself) and well-pleasing unto Him! "Enter you, then, among My honoured slaves,*
> Return, O soul of peace, to your Lord, well-pleased with Him, so be one of My servants.
> — **Quran 89:27-29 (inline widget)**

It is thus understood that *fiṭra* (the innate disposition, primordial nature) is both the origin and the terminus of the self. The soul has been carved into the divine pattern, and its return is likewise toward that primordial state.[^cite-25]

<!-- section 12 (id=3595, raw_sort=12): روحانیت اور اخلاق -->
## Spirituality and Ethics

The Amīr al-Muʾminīn says in his first sermon:

---

⟪ar-quote:وَاصْطَفى سُبْحَانَهُ مِنْ وَلَدَهِ أَنْبيَاءَ أَخَذَ عَلَى الْوَحْيِ مِيثَاقَهُم، وَعَلَى تَبْليغِ الرِّسَالَةِ أَمَانَتَهُمْ، لَمَّا بَدَّلَ أَكْثَرُ خَلْقِهِ عَهْدَ اللهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، فَجَهِلُوا حَقَّهُ، واتَّخَذُوا الاْنْدَادَ مَعَهُ، وَاجْتَالَتْهُمُ الشَّيَاطِينُ عَنْ مَعْرفَتِهِ، وَاقتَطَعَتْهُمْ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ، فَبَعَثَ فِيهمْ رُسُلَهُ، وَوَاتَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ أَنْبِياءَهُ،**لِيَسْتَأْدُوهُمْ مِيثَاقَ فِطْرَتِهِ**، وَيُذَكِّرُوهُمْ مَنْسِيَّ نِعْمَتِهِ، وَيَحْتَجُّوا عَلَيْهِمْ بَالتَّبْلِيغِ، **وَيُثِيرُوا لَهُمْ دَفَائِنَ الْعُقُولِ**، وَيُرُوهُمْ آيَاتِ الْمَقْدِرَةِ⟫

From his (Adam's) progeny Allah chose prophets and took their pledge for his revelation and for carrying His message as their trust. In course of time many people perverted Allah's trust with them and ignored His position and took compeers along with Him. Satan turned them away from knowing Him and kept them aloof from His worship. Then Allah sent His Messengers and series of His prophets towards them to get them to fulfil the pledges of His creation, to recall to them His bounties, to exhort them by preaching, to unveil before them the hidden virtues of wisdom and show them the signs of His Omnipotence

---

The buried treasures alluded to here are that ⟪ar:’علم کلی‘⟫ (ʿilm kullī, universal knowledge) that was deposited within the souls on the day of the primordial covenant. This knowledge — at once nature, life, and inheritance — is their *fiṭra*, because in it lies the possibility of every good thing.[^cite-26] Hence the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to say that the most beloved deed should be ⟪ar:’عمل صالح‘⟫ (ʿamal ṣāliḥ, righteous action), for ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ (al-ḥaqq, the Truth, the Real) is not only the root of every good act but also the essence of every created thing. In one place he praises Allah with these words:

By Thy majesty which fills all things, by Thy names which are the foundation of all things, by Thy knowledge which encompasses all things, by the light of Thy face by which everything is illuminated.

From this vantage, every good character-trait ⟪ar:خُلق حسنۃ⟫ in the world is the reflection of some ⟪ar:’الہی صفت‘⟫ (ilāhī ṣifa, divine attribute), and every divine attribute is one of the names of Allah — which is why the prophetic counsel runs ⟪ar-quote:تخلُقو بأخلاق اللہ⟫ ("Take on the character of Allah"), an act called ⟪ar:’أحسانی‘⟫ (iḥsānī, a manner of beautiful conduct). In ethics and theology, monotheism is so established that, on the one hand, cultivating noble character draws down the divine substance, and on the other, that same "divine substance" is the inner essence of every good created thing. Every good quality therefore points back to its own source and to the expression of its very being: ⟪ar:’اللہُ وحدہ لا شریک لہ‘⟫ (Allāh waḥdahu lā sharīka lah — Allah alone, no partner with Him). Allah declares in the Qurʾān:

> ⟪quran 8:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَلَمْ تَقْتُلُوهُمْ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ قَتَلَهُمْ ۚ وَمَا رَمَيْتَ إِذْ رَمَيْتَ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ رَمَىٰ ۚ وَلِيُبْلِىَ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْهُ بَلَآءً حَسَنًا ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *You killed them not, but Allah killed them. And you (Muhammad PBUH) threw not when you did throw but Allah threw, that He might test the believers by a fair trial from Him. Verily, Allah is All-Hearer, All-Knower.*
> It was not you who killed them, but it was God who killed them. And you did not throw your handful when you threw, but it was God who threw, and that He might bestow His grace on the believers. God is All-hearing, All-knowing.
> — **Quran 8:17 (inline widget)**

This indicates that in order for the ⟪ar:’متقی‘⟫ (muttaqī, the God-conscious) to come into being, it is not enough for a man to negate his own self; he must also cultivate the divine attributes within himself. Knowledge of those attributes humbles him, and turns the soul away from desire toward the divine realities that are the substance of every virtue and ethical excellence.[^cite-27]

Consider now the ⟪ar:’نفس امارۃ‘⟫ (nafs ammāra, the self that commands to evil) and the narrative of Yūsuf. When his innocence was vindicated in the king's court, he declared, "I do not exonerate myself: indeed the soul commands evil, save where my Lord has mercy." The Qurʾānic account of Zulaykhā makes plain that his vindication was not the achievement of his own self, but the bestowal of divine grace. No verse describes the helplessness of man in the trial of false desire more searchingly than: ⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ ٱلنَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌۢ بِٱلسُّوٓءِ إِلَّا مَا رَحِمَ رَبِّىٓ⟫.

The human soul therefore lives between two pillars. The first is the appetite of its own selfhood, which propels it toward evil in this fleeting and deceitful world. The second is its attentive turning toward the grace of God, which restores it to its original station. Man stands in need of divine grace at every instant. The moment that grace is withheld, the soul is bent toward sin. It is for this reason that the Imam opens his letter with this very verse, since he has entrusted Mālik al-Ashtar with a province rich in resources, where the temptations toward evil run high. When a man strives to avoid sin it does not mean that he is self-sufficient or has dispensed with divine grace; on the contrary, it proves that Allah's grace already rests upon him, and that under its influence he both wills to resist sin and strives to do so. The very pursuit of the good is a token of bounty that Allah placed in the soul on the primordial day, and that He continues to summon forth through the seeker's sincere exertion.[^cite-28]

It is worth noting that, although the laws required for the practice of justice are amply spelled out, the means of holding to those laws against the onslaught of desire, power, and greed are rarely articulated. Laws can punish the tyrant, but the *intention* not to be led astray cannot be legislated. For this reason the Imam offers such counsel as: break the soul that rises in the form of strong desire, master your appetites, and restrain yourself from what is unlawful for you.

The aim of living by just precepts is not the surface obedience of the stated law. The aim is the moral disciplining of the self toward those precepts. Justice, in this sense, is not the mere performance of the right act or compliance with statute; it is the recognition of ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫. The horizon of the human being shifts from "doing" to "being" — from action to thought. This does not weaken or render indeterminate the work itself. Rather, action becomes the mirror of divine thought, and through that mirroring it grows in strength and fecundity. ⟪ar:الحق⟫ — constant attentiveness to the self — heightens action and establishes truth and justice in the soul. The rank of the human is the rank of ⟪ar:’تحقیق‘⟫ (taḥqīq, verifying or realising the Truth), which is to "do the truth." Spirituality is realised through spirituality; spirituality is realised through piety.[^cite-29]

<!-- section 13 (id=3596, raw_sort=13): کبر اور غرور سے بچنے کی نصیحت -->
## Counsel against Arrogance and Pride

The Imam warns the holder of authority: do not arm your soul for combat against Allah. What sort of acts amount to fighting against Allah? Upon careful reflection, this passage refers to dispositions in which outward action wears the appearance of evil, while inwardly the very thinking stands opposed to the spirit of action. Take arrogance, against which Mawlānā ʿAlī has cautioned in many places. When a ruler grows "arrogant," he usurps one of the great attributes of Allah, claiming for himself what belongs to Allah alone — for ⟪ar:’المتکبر‘⟫ (al-Mutakabbir, the Supremely Proud) is a name fitted to Him and to no other. To boast before men and parade one's grandeur is to oppose Allah inwardly and to deny His ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫ (aḥadiyya, absolute oneness). Such concealed denial can be read precisely under the figure of waging war against God. Hostility to the Real ⟪ar:الحق⟫ is the hidden substance that a ruler displays toward his subjects in every form of haughtiness, vainglory, and oppression. The ruler's notion of superiority over those "below" him is, in truth, a declaration of revolt against the One "above" him. The oppressor therefore not only invites the just wrath of the Creator by oppressing creatures, but actively contends with the Creator through his own deeds. The root of this worldly evil is ⟪ar:الحق⟫ — a spiritual defect that arises from denial of the Lord's ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫ and His ⟪ar:حقانیت⟫ (ḥaqqāniyya, absolute truth and rightful sovereignty), and from forgetting the Qurʾānic verse:[^cite-30]

> ⟪quran 40:16⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَوْمَ هُم بَرِزُونَۖ لَا يَخْفَىٰ عَلَى ٱللَّهِ مِنْهُمْ شَىْءٌۭۚ لِّمَنِ ٱلْمُلْكُ ٱلْيَوْمَۖ لِلَّهِ ٱلْوَحِدِ ٱلْقَهَّارِ ‎⟫
> *The Day when they will (all) come out, nothing of them will be hidden from Allah. Whose is the kingdom this Day? (Allah Himself will reply to His Question): It is Allah's the One, the Irresistible!*
> day when they will all come forth, nothing of them will be hidden from Allah.
> — **Quran 40:16 (inline widget)**

This ⟪ar:’الیوم‘⟫ ("the Day") does not refer only to the Day of Judgement, but to every day. In his renowned sermon, known as ⟪ar:’القاصیۃ‘⟫ (al-Qāṣiʿa, the sermon of disparagement), the Imam describes the humiliation of the arrogant Iblīs, who was the first to confront Allah on the field of pride, and so became the centre and the source of all arrogance. When Allah commanded him to prostrate before Ādam, he flatly refused, filled with pride, considering himself greater than Ādam: "I am made of fire, and he of clay." By this arrogance Iblīs became not only the first enemy of Allah but the leader ⟪ar:أمام المتعصبین و صلف المستکبرین⟫ (imām al-mutaʿaṣṣibīn wa-ṣalaf al-mustakbirīn — leader of the bigoted and forerunner of the arrogant) of every haughty man who came after him. Beware, then, the sickness sown by his whispers and his stratagems. Wear always the garment of humility; trample self-praise beneath your feet; cast off the chains of pride from your neck; and take refuge in the secure citadel of meekness.[^cite-31]

This shows that *humility* is the surest weapon against the devil, since his entire purpose is to plant arrogance in man. Arrogance is in itself a vice of the worst order, but it is also a deadly poison to every other ⟪ar:خصال محمودۃ⟫ (khiṣāl maḥmūda, praiseworthy qualities). Whatever good keeps company with arrogance is converted into evil. Hence the saying: "A sin that grieves you is better than a good deed that makes you arrogant." The seasons of praise and self-importance are exactly the moments at which Satan finds his clearest opening.[^cite-32]

*Verses referenced in this topic (curated linkage from KAHSKOLE. TopicAyats — 7 of 7 not already cited above):*

> ⟪quran 7:181⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎⟫
> *And of those whom We have created, there is a community who guides (others) with the truth, and establishes justice therewith.*
> And of those whom We have created, there is a community guiding the truth and thereby they do justice.
> — **Quran 7:181 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 7:182⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *Those who reject Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.), We shall gradually seize them with punishment in ways they perceive not.*
> And those who belie Our signs, step by step We will seize them from whence they are unaware.
> — **Quran 7:182 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 9:85⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *And let not their wealth or their children amaze you. Allah's Plan is to punish them with these things in this world, and that their souls shall depart (die) while they are disbelievers.*

> — **Quran 9:85 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 17:81⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَقُلْ جَآءَ ٱلْحَقُّ وَزَهَقَ ٱلْبَطِلُ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلْبَطِلَ كَانَ زَهُوقًۭا ‎⟫
> *And say: "Truth (i.e. Islamic Monotheism or this Quran or Jihad against polytheists) has come and Batil (falsehood, i.e. Satan or polytheism, etc.) has vanished. Surely! Batil is ever bound to vanish."*
> And say, The truth has come, and falsehood has vanished. Falsehood is bound to vanish.
> — **Quran 17:81 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*
> And do not invoke any other god along with Allah; there is no God except Him; all things will perish except His Face; His is the command, and it is to Him that you will be returned.
> — **Quran 28:88 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 55:26⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish.*
> whosoever is on the earth will perish.
> — **Quran 55:26 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 55:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*
> and of your Lord will remain the Countenance of the Most Majesty and the Most Honourable.
> — **Quran 55:27 (TopicAyats)**

<!-- section 14 (id=3601, raw_sort=14): شرک خفی -->
## Hidden Shirk

The outward sense of shirk (associating partners with God) is commonly taken to be the worship of idols. In another sense, however, the worship of idols hidden within the self is equally shirk — idols that lodge in the soul as intentions, attitudes, inclinations, pride, ostentation, boasting, and fabrication. Alluding to this, the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) is reported to have said: "Shirk in my community is more hidden than the creeping of a black ant upon a black stone on a dark night." Hence the warning that even the slightest hypocrisy is shirk. For to act in pursuit of the praise of others, and not for the sake of God, is to set another beside God; and whoever acts for any other than God, God consigns him to the one he served.

It was the deterioration of Iblīs's inner arrogance that drove him to the sin of outward disobedience, sealing his destiny of humiliation. Iblīs was humbled because he had disobeyed, and he disobeyed because he was arrogant — proof that kibr (arrogance) is itself a disgrace, the seed of its own destruction. Do you not see how God humiliated him? To exalt oneself is, in reality, to be lowered; to magnify oneself is, in truth, to belittle oneself.[^cite-33] For this reason the Imam said to Malik al-Ashtar: "Do not say, 'I hold authority; I command and I am obeyed.'" A notion of this kind sows disorder in the heart and ruins religion. From this counsel it is also understood that the soundness of religion's outward form depends upon the soundness of inner intentions and convictions.[^cite-34] When power rises to the head, faith departs the heart; for faith to survive in this world, it must issue from within and appear outwardly as humility — a form of placing things in their proper station, which is the essence of justice.

He then says to Malik al-Ashtar: "If your position should make you arrogant or self-regarding, then look upon the greatness of God above you." Such contemplation will overcome your appetites and restore the intellect by guarding it from the rigidity of the self. The relation between intellect and humility deserves a moment's reflection here. The portion of the intellect that is distracted by arrogance and pretense is precisely the portion by which the reality of God is grasped, and by which the branches issuing from that reality are discerned. In Arabic, arrogance is called ⟪ar:’مَخِلا‘⟫, a term whose root lies in khayāl — fancy, imagining. Kibr, then, is an "imagining," tied deeply to this fleeting and deceptive world. Arrogance is a severe form of conjecture born of a disordered intellect; it appears as an evil and is recognized as immoral. Nor is it merely a matter of thinking oneself great: it is also the belittling of ⟪ar:الحق⟫. Only a ⟪ar:ولی اللہ⟫ can grasp the reality of the following verses and draw from them the humility that uproots ⟪ar:’أنائیت‘⟫ — the I-ness that is the root of every arrogance, ostentation, and pride, and the very nourishment of every oppression:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*
> And do not invoke any other god along with Allah; there is no God except Him; all things will perish except His Face; His is the command, and it is to Him that you will be returned.
> — **Quran 28:88 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 55:26-27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎ ‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish. And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*
> whosoever is on the earth will perish, and there will remain the Countenance of your Lord, the Most Majestic and the Most Majestic.
> — **Quran 55:26-27 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 17:81⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَقُلْ جَآءَ ٱلْحَقُّ وَزَهَقَ ٱلْبَطِلُ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلْبَطِلَ كَانَ زَهُوقًۭا ‎⟫
> *And say: "Truth (i.e. Islamic Monotheism or this Quran or Jihad against polytheists) has come and Batil (falsehood, i.e. Satan or polytheism, etc.) has vanished. Surely! Batil is ever bound to vanish." *
> And say, The truth has come, and falsehood has vanished. Falsehood is bound to vanish.
> — **Quran 17:81 (inline widget)**

With these matters in view, we can savor what the Imam went on to say: "Beware of vying with God in His grandeur, or likening yourself to Him in His might; for God brings low every tyrant and humbles every vainglorious one." Whoever fails to render to God and His creation what is their due will discover on the Day of Resurrection that not only God's creation but God Himself stands against him. Man remains at war with God until he abandons his oppression and turns in repentance. And though he may yet survive in this world, he shall not survive in the world to come.

The longer the oppressor persists, the more wicked his soul becomes, and the more deeply it is steeped in suffering. The Qur'an captures this in the concept of ⟪ar:’استدراج‘⟫ — the gradual, almost imperceptible escalation of chastisement. The following verses not only describe these degrees but draw a sharp line between those who do justice to the truth and those who do violence to it:

> ⟪quran 7:181-182⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎ ‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And of those whom We have created, there is a community who guides (others) with the truth, and establishes justice therewith. Those who reject Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.), We shall gradually seize them with punishment in ways they perceive not.*
> And of those whom We have created there is a community guiding the truth and justifying by it. And those who belie Our signs, We will seize them little by little from where they are unaware.
> — **Quran 7:181-182 (inline widget)**

This chastisement comes not only in the form of poverty, illness, and suffering, but equally in the form of worldly success, glory, and progeny, as God declares:

> ⟪quran 9:85⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *And let not their wealth or their children amaze you. Allah's Plan is to punish them with these things in this world, and that their souls shall depart (die) while they are disbelievers.*
> Do not amaze at their riches or their children. Allah only desires to punish them with these in this world, and that their souls will depart while they are unbelievers.
> — **Quran 9:85 (inline widget)**

The wrongdoer can be a ⟪ar:’مسلمان‘⟫ and at the same time a ⟪ar:’کافر‘⟫: for kufr means concealment, and he has concealed the truth from himself, from his deeds, and from all the good that might have flowed therefrom.

<!-- section 15 (id=3597, raw_sort=15): اخلاقی و روحانی ضمیر -->
## Moral and Spiritual Conscience

Another form of warring against God is to war against one's own conscience. A soul that knows its moral obligations and understands them addresses the self in the accents of an inward voice. That voice of conscience is, in truth, the voice of an awakened soul:

> ⟪quran 91:7-8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَنَفْسٍۢ وَمَا سَوَّىٰهَا ‎ ‏فَأَلْهَمَهَا فُجُورَهَا وَتَقْوَىٰهَا ‎⟫
> *And by Nafs (Adam or a person or a soul, etc.), and Him Who perfected him in proportion; Then He showed him what is wrong for him and what is right for him;*
> and soul, and He who made it right, then He made to him his evil and his good.
> — **Quran 91:7-8 (inline widget)**

The verse teaches that what restrains and rightly guides the ⟪ar:نفس⟫ ⟪ar:أمارۃ بالسوء⟫ (the soul that incites to evil) is the conscience, the inward arena in which the arguments of good and evil are weighed. A morally awakened soul will incline toward goodness; a degraded soul will incline toward wickedness. God Most High has sown in every soul, at the very seat of conscience, what this verse indicates. For this reason every soul not only discerns between good and evil but also instinctively recognizes its own ⟪ar:’عبدیت‘⟫ (servanthood) and the ⟪ar:’الہیت‘⟫ (divinity) of God. The Qur'an commemorates the very moment when God created humankind and drew from it the covenant of His Lordship:

> ⟪quran 7:172⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam, from their loins, their seed (or from Adam's loin his offspring) and made them testify as to themselves (saying): "Am I not your Lord?" They said: "Yes! We testify," lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection: "Verily, we have been unaware of this." *
> And when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam from their loins, their offspring, and made them testify as to themselves, I am not your Lord, they said, Yes, we testify. Lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection, We were not aware of this.
> — **Quran 7:172 (inline widget)**

The wrongdoer, then, is the one who breaks this covenant with God and takes the ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫ — his own commanding soul — for his lord, in the place of God. This is why ʿAlī (peace be upon him) admonished Malik al-Ashtar: "Do not say, 'I command, and am obeyed,' for that is the way of the ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫, whose commands are obeyed by the body, the soul, the imagination, the intellect, the will, the emotions, and the senses." The way to render justice to oneself is ⟪ar:مجاہدۃ النفس⟫ (the struggle against the soul) — to begin by uprooting one's own defects. As the Imam said: "If you wish to reform others, begin with yourself; for to seek the betterment of other souls while evil yet dwells within is the gravest of sins."

Before ⟪ar:مالک اشتر⟫, the Imam had appointed ⟪ar:محمد بن ابی بکر⟫ as governor of Egypt, and he counseled him too, saying: "I have made you the guardian of the people of Egypt; it is incumbent upon you, in essence, to oppose your own self and to protect your religion." This counsel is striking. He entrusted authority to Muḥammad ibn Abī Bakr and laid two obligations upon him: first, the safeguarding of the self from its appetites; second, the safeguarding of his religion. The greater the power and authority, the heavier the responsibility to restrain the self. For if the soul submits to its desires and gratifies them through the powers it commands, a man destroys not only himself but his religion. The outward act of a Muslim's faith depends, for its survival, upon the inner integrity of the soul — yet another instance of placing things in their proper station. Upon attaining power, the soul that breeds arrogance and the lust for dominance — the ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ⟫ — is the one of which the Qur'an speaks thus:

> ⟪quran 96:6-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّآ إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَيَطْغَىٰٓ ‎ ‏أَن رَّآهُ ٱسْتَغْنَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Nay! Verily, man does transgress all bounds (in disbelief and evil deed, etc.). Because he considers himself self-sufficient.*
> indeed, man becomes arrogant when he finds himself rich.
> — **Quran 96:6-7 (inline widget)**

The more a soul is deceived by the illusion of "self-sufficiency" and flees from reliance upon God, the more it comes to imagine itself a god — and this is its gravest injustice. It becomes the very one of whom God says:

> ⟪quran 45:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who takes his own lust (vain desires) as his ilah (god), and Allah knowing (him as such), left him astray, and sealed his hearing and his heart, and put a cover on his sight. Who then will guide him after Allah? Will you not then remember?*
> have you seen him who has become a slave of his own desire, and Allah has led him astray despite his knowledge, and set a seal upon his hearing and his heart, and put a covering on his sight? Who will guide him after Allah? Will you not then understand?
> — **Quran 45:23 (inline widget)**

The more thoroughly a person realizes his own poverty and his neediness before God, the more the grip of the ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫ loosens about his neck. For only the soul that commands itself to evil can command others to evil, and only the soul that humbles itself before God can deal with people in humility, mercy, and justice.

The Imam continues: "Let the dearest of your affairs be those that strike the middle course in truth, the most encompassing in justice, and the most pleasing to the common people; for the displeasure of the commonalty undoes the contentment of the elite."[^cite-35] Note the insistence on the approval of ordinary people. The one who humbles himself in the sight of God will dwell among the common people; the arrogant will only delight in the company of the arrogant. And it is the humble alone who reads aright this verse:

> ⟪quran 35:15⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫
> *O mankind! it is you who stand in need of Allah, but Allah is Rich (Free of all wants and needs), Worthy of all praise.*
> O men, it is you who are in need of Allah, and Allah is All-sufficient, All-laudable.
> — **Quran 35:15 (inline widget)**

The life of the Commander of the Faithful, the Master of the universe, stands as proof in this regard. Once the family of a man named ⟪ar:آثم بن زیاد⟫ — an ascetic of the dervish way — complained that he was needlessly living in destitution. The Imam summoned him and counseled him to look after his kin and not to forsake the gifts God had granted. The man replied: "O ʿAlī, you tell me this, while you yourself are wrapped in coarse cloth and eat dry bread." The Imam said: "Woe to you! I am not like you. God has made it obligatory upon the ⟪ar:ائمۃ الحق⟫ — the Imams of Truth — to live as the poorest of their people, so that they may feel the poverty of the poor, and lest they themselves grow covetous."[^cite-36]

This account demonstrates that the ruler must live his worldly life at the station of the poorest among his subjects. ʿAlī chose for himself the least of what was available — and only because his bond with ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ was so deep that, in its light, every material thing of this world appeared in his eyes despicable, contemptible, and worthless.

[^cite-33]: Cf. Imam ʿAlī's Khuṭbat al-Qāṣiʿa, where Iblīs serves as the archetypal exemplar of how arrogance ruins long obedience.
[^cite-34]: Cf. Qāḍī al-Nuʿmān's Daʿāʾim al-Islām, Kitāb al-Niyya, on the principle that no outward act is valid except by the soundness of inward intention.
[^cite-35]: This passage is drawn from the Imam's celebrated letter to Malik al-Ashtar in Nahj al-Balāgha (Letter 53).
[^cite-36]: Cf. Imam ʿAlī's encounter with ʿĀṣim ibn Ziyād al-Ḥārithī in Nahj al-Balāgha (Sermon 209).

<!-- section 16 (id=3587, raw_sort=16): عدل اور ہمدردی -->
## Justice and Compassion

To feel the suffering of the poor sharpens one's awareness of dependence upon the Lord, and this awareness sustains a life poised between hope and fear at the mercy of God. Within such a life, the innate disposition (fiṭra, the primordial constitution) naturally inclines a person to treat his fellow beings with tenderness. Empathy is in no way opposed to the demands of justice; it is in fact constitutive of it, for it preserves things in their proper places, accords with the very nature of the cosmos, and reflects an exalted attribute of the Real. For this reason God has prefaced every sūra of the Qurʾān with Bismillāh al-Raḥmān al-Raḥīm (In the name of God, the Compassionate, the Merciful), invoking His mercy and protective care at the very threshold of revelation. The same disposition is everywhere visible in the conduct of the Prophet and of Amīr al-Muʾminīn (the Commander of the Faithful, ʿAlī): they bore themselves toward God's creatures with unfailing mercy, and did so not from the prompting of private sentiment but as a fulfilment of God's own command, as He has declared:

> ⟪quran 7:156⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَٱكْتُبْ لَنَا فِى هَذِهِ ٱلدُّنْيَا حَسَنَةًۭ وَفِى ٱلْآخِرَةِ إِنَّا هُدْنَآ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ عَذَابِىٓ أُصِيبُ بِهِۦ مَنْ أَشَآءُ ۖ وَرَحْمَتِى وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَىْءٍۢ ۚ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَٱلَّذِينَ هُم بِـَٔايَتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ ‎⟫
> *And ordain for us good in this world, and in the Hereafter.&nbsp;Certainly we have turned unto You." He said: (As to) My Punishment I afflict therewith whom I will and My Mercy embraces all things.&nbsp;That (Mercy) I shall ordain for those who are the Muttaqun (pious - see V.2:2), and give Zakat; and those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs and revelations, etc.); *
> And ordain for us in this world that which is good, and in the world to come. We turn unto Thee. He said, I afflict with My chastisement whomsoever I will, and My mercy encompasses all things. So I shall ordain it for those who fear Allah and pay the poor-rate and those who believe in Our signs.
> — **Quran 7:156 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *When those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.) come to you, say: "Salamun 'Alaikum" (peace be on you); your Lord has written Mercy for Himself, so that, if any of you does evil in ignorance, and thereafter repents and does righteous good deeds (by obeying Allah), then surely, He is Oft&shy;Forgiving, Most Merciful.*
> And those who believe in Our verses, when they come to you, say, Peace be upon you. Your Lord has made mercy incumbent upon Himself. So whoever among you does evil in ignorance, then repents thereafter and does good, then indeed He is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful.
> — **Quran 6:54 (inline widget)**

Among the sayings of Mawlānā ʿAlī on this same theme is the following: "The act of mercy draws down upon you the mercy of God; you are shown mercy in the measure that you show it to others. I marvel at the man who hopes for mercy from those above him yet withholds it from those beneath him."[^cite-37]

By this logic, the more compassionate a person becomes in the inner reaches of his thought and the outward forms of his conduct, the closer he stands to the Most High. In any society, justice requires that people be treated with kindness wherever circumstance permits. There are, of course, moments in which severity becomes unavoidable. This is why, in his celebrated epistle to Mālik al-Ashtar, ʿAlī instructed his governor to punish without indulgence those officers found guilty of embezzling the public wealth, so that the justice of God might be made manifest.[^cite-38] In another letter, addressed to his cousin whom he had appointed governor of Baṣra, he wrote: "I swear by God in all sincerity that if the report reaches me that you have appropriated the wealth of the Muslims, whether in small measure or great, I shall chastise you with a punishment that diminishes your estate, breaks your back, and humbles your works."

Whenever a petitioner approached ʿAlī seeking favour at the expense of the public trust, he was met with the same severity, even when the petitioner was a close kinsman. It is famously related that his own brother ʿAqīl once requested an additional share from the Bayt al-Māl (public treasury); ʿAlī placed a heated iron near his hand, and when ʿAqīl cried out in pain, he said, "Brother ʿAqīl, if you cannot endure this little flame, how shall I bear the blazing fire of God's Hell on the Day of Resurrection, to which by your request you would invite me?" Likewise, when word reached him that his cousin ʿAbd Allāh ibn ʿAbbās had taken what was not his from the public funds, ʿAlī wrote to him: "Fear God, and restore to the people what is rightfully theirs. If you do not, and God grants me authority over you, I shall strike you with my sword — and no one I have struck with it has failed to enter the Fire. By God, were Ḥasan or Ḥusayn to do the like, they would receive from me no concession greater than yours."

This makes plain that, however elevated a man's station, in the scales of justice all stand equal. Such conduct stood in sharpest contrast to that of the earlier caliphs, who, in ʿAlī's striking phrase, divided the offices of state among their kindred and devoured the wealth of the Muslims "as a camel in springtime devours the tender shoots." God has said in the Qurʾān:

> ⟪quran 4:135⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ كُونُوا۟ قَوَّمِينَ بِٱلْقِسْطِ شُهَدَآءَ لِلَّهِ وَلَوْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِكُمْ أَوِ ٱلْوَلِدَيْنِ وَٱلْأَقْرَبِينَ ۚ إِن يَكُنْ غَنِيًّا أَوْ فَقِيرًۭا فَٱللَّهُ أَوْلَىٰ بِهِمَا ۖ فَلَا تَتَّبِعُوا۟ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ أَن تَعْدِلُوا۟ ۚ وَإِن تَلْوُۥٓا۟ أَوْ تُعْرِضُوا۟ فَإِنَّ ٱللَّهَ كَانَ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Stand out firmly for justice, as witnesses to Allah, even though it be against yourselves, or your parents, or your kin, be he rich or poor, Allah is a Better Protector to both (than you).&nbsp;So follow not the lusts (of your hearts), lest you may avoid justice, and if you distort your witness or refuse to give it,  verily, Allah is Ever Well&shy;Acquainted with what you do.*
> O you who believe! Be just, bear witness to Allah, even if it be against yourselves or against your parents or your relatives, whether it be rich or poor, for Allah is better for them than you. So do not follow your desires in justice, and if you distort or transgress, then surely Allah is Aware of what you do.
> — **Quran 4:135 (inline widget)**

The portion of the letter that follows is especially remarkable, for in it ʿAlī enlarges compassion into a universal frame, bringing the whole of humanity onto a single plane of equality. In this single utterance lies the antidote to every form of prejudice and partisan division. He writes:

⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْعِرْ قَلْبَكَ الرَّحْمَةَ لِلرَّعِيَّةِ، وَالْـمَحَبَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَاللُّطْفَ بِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَكُونَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ سَبُعاً ضَارِياً تَغْتَنِمُ أَكْلَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهُمْ صِنْفَانِ- إِمَّا أَخٌ لَكَ فِي الدِّينِ، وَإمّا نَظِيرٌ لَكَ فِي الْخَلْقِ، يَفْرُطُ مِنْهُمُ الزَّلَلُ، وَتَعْرِضُ لَهُمُ الْعِلَلُ،يُؤْتَى عَلَى أَيْدِيهِمْ فِي الَعَمْدِ وَالْخَطَاَ، فَأَعْطِهِمْ مِنْ عَفْوِكَ وَصَفْحِكَ مِثْلَ الَّذِي تُحِبُّ أَنْ يُعْطِيَكَ اللهُ مِنْ عَفْوِهِ وَصَفْحِهِ، فَإِنَّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ، وَ وَالِي الاْمْرِ عَلَيْكَ فَوْقَكَ، وَاللهُ فَوْقَ مَنْ وَلاَّكَ! وَقَدِ اسْتَكْفَاكَ أَمْرَهُمْ، وَابْتَلاَكَ بِهِمْ⟫

> Habituate your heart to mercy for the subjects and to affection and kindness for them. Do not stand over them like greedy beasts who feel it is enough to devour them, since they are of two kinds, either your brother in religion or one like you in creation. They will commit slips and encounter mistakes. They may act wrongly, wilfully or by neglect. So, extend to them your forgiveness and pardon, in the same way as you would like Allah to extend His forgiveness and pardon to you, because you are over them and your responsible Commander (Imam) is over you while Allah is over him who has appointed you. He (Allah) has sought you to manage their affairs and has tried you through them.

By enjoining mercy toward all of mankind, ʿAlī directs the ruler's gaze toward the mercy of God. Every human being, however exalted as king or governor, remains a servant (ʿabd) of God and stands in total need of His mercy. If a person finds himself in authority over another, he must remember that he himself is in submission before God. This recollection makes him gentle and compassionate with those beneath him, and draws down upon him the mercy of God. ʿAlī thus reminds Mālik al-Ashtar that, though a ruler, he remains a man among other men.

It is related that Mawlānā ʿAlī once came upon a blind mendicant begging in the street, and was told that the man was a Christian. He said, "You have taken his strength while he was able-bodied; now that he has aged and weakened, do you abandon him? From this day forth, let him be maintained from the Bayt al-Māl." This act teaches the principle that, in the matter of justice, Muslim and non-Muslim stand on equal ground. Social justice and religious equality alike take root in mercy, and mercy is thus an indispensable duty upon the Muslim.

To Mālik al-Ashtar ʿAlī wrote also that his governance is no honour bestowed by God but a trial and a testing — words that disclose how ʿAlī himself understood the office of caliph. He once said from the pulpit: "Had God not taken from the learned the covenant that they should not acquiesce in the gluttony of the oppressor nor in the hunger of the oppressed, I would have cast the reins of this caliphate upon its own neck, and you would have seen how this world is, in my sight, of less worth than the substance that flows from a goat's nostril."[^cite-39] Here is heard, faintly, a kindred note to Plato's teaching that the true philosopher is one who governs only for the welfare of the governed: not as an honour to himself but as an inescapable obligation, his entire aim being the establishment of justice, since the founding and restoration of any society can rest only upon this single attribute.
