The phrase *yuthīrū lahum dafāʾin al-ʿuqūl* (that they might unearth for them the buried treasures of the intellects) is the locus classicus for this conception of the prophetic mission as an awakening of the latent intellect rather than the imposition of an external decree.

[^cite-66]: This identification of the intellect as itself a mode of revelation — the inner counterpart of the outer Book — is a recurring theme in Nāṣir-i Khusraw's *Jāmiʿ al-Ḥikmatayn*, where the harmony of scriptural revelation (*tanzīl*) with the universal intellect is set out as the principle reconciling philosophical and prophetic knowledge.

[^cite-67]: On the constitutive limits of discursive reason in approaching the divine, see Abū Yaʿqūb al-Sijistānī, *Kitāb al-Yanābīʿ*, where the apophatic procedure — the double negation of attributes and of the negation of attributes itself — is set out as the proper method by which the intellect may approach the Originator (*al-Mubdiʿ*).

<!-- section 25 (id=5713, raw_sort=25): The Discourse To Kumayl -->
## The Discourse To Kumayl

The discourse delivered by Mawlānā ʿAlī to his disciple Kumayl ibn Ziyād has occupied commentators for centuries. Its enduring importance lies, among other things, in its profoundly esoteric character — a character that calls not merely for exposition but for inward assimilation.

The Imam took Kumayl outside Kufa to a graveyard, and there, in that liminal setting between this world and the next, imparted the following private counsel:

> O Kumayl ibn Ziyād, these hearts are vessels, and the best of them are those which hold the most. So retain from me what I say to you. People are of three types: a lordly knower; one who seeks knowledge (⟪ar:متعلم⟫) for the sake of deliverance; and the common folk who follow just anyone, swaying with every current, neither illumined by the light of knowledge nor seeking refuge in any firm support.
>
> O Kumayl, knowledge is better than wealth, for knowledge guards you while you must guard wealth; wealth diminishes as it is spent, while knowledge increases as it is disbursed; and the works that wealth produces vanish when wealth itself vanishes. O Kumayl ibn Ziyād, the wise apprehension of knowledge is a religion by which Allah is worshipped. Through it a person attains obedience in life and a good name after death. Knowledge is judge, while wealth is judged.
>
> O Kumayl ibn Ziyād, those who hoard wealth perish even while they live, but the knowers endure for as long as time itself subsists; their material forms are absent, but their spiritual images remain present in hearts. Ah! what abundant knowledge is here — pointing to his breast — if only I could find one to bear it. Yes, I found one who was quick to understand, but he could not be trusted with it: he exploited the instruments of religion for the sake of worldly gain, arming himself with Allah's graces against His servants, and with His proofs against His friends. Then there was one obedient to the bearers of truth, but lacking heartfelt insight: at the first appearance of obscurity, doubt was kindled in his heart. So alas, neither this one nor that. Nor again one greedy for pleasure, easily seduced by passion, nor one obsessed with acquisition and accumulation — none of these is a guardian of religion in any respect. They resemble nothing so much as grazing cattle, and thus does knowledge die with the death of its bearers.
>
> Yet by Allah, the earth will never be empty of one who establishes the proof of Allah, whether overtly with publicity or fearfully in concealment, lest Allah's proofs and elucidations come to naught. But such as these — how many are they, and where? By Allah, they may be smallest in number, yet with Allah they are the greatest in rank. Through them Allah preserves His proofs and elucidations, so that they entrust them to their compeers and sow them in hearts resembling their own. Through them, knowledge penetrates the reality of insight. They rejoice in their intimacy with the spirit of certainty; they make easy what the extravagant find harsh; they befriend that by which the ignorant are estranged. With their bodies they keep company with the world, while their spirits are tied to the transcendent realm. They are the vicegerents of Allah on His earth, the Summoners (*duʿāt*) to His religion. Ah! how I long to see them. Go now, Kumayl, as you will.

For our purposes, it suffices to reflect upon the four sentences in which the Imam describes those who bear the title "lordly knower" (⟪ar:فَعَالِمٌ رَبَّانِيٌّ⟫) — the few who are smallest in number but greatest in the sight of Allah, and through whom "His religion" is sustained. *His* religion: the divine reality of religion, the pure essence of faith, perfect and immutable, in contrast to religion in its ordinary sense, whose formal institutions are subject to human vicissitudes. It is by means of the knowledge of the true knowers that religion remains true to itself, and only through such sages does religion truly *live* in the world.

### Through them, knowledge penetrates the reality of insight

Knowledge, as noted before, can remain merely abstract and far removed from the "reality of insight". Yet it contains within it a potential that calls out to be realised. It must be enlivened in order to penetrate into something deeper than the words and concepts which articulate its own form — that immediately intelligible meaning which rests on the surface. Degrees of knowledge are clearly implied here, and so is the avoidance of literalism and superficiality, the avoidance of facile equations between factual information and actual knowledge, let alone wisdom. The shift of consciousness required for the *penetration* of knowledge is indicated graphically by the Imam's gesture of pointing to his own breast.

The word "penetrate" has been chosen here to render *hajama*, whose primary meaning is to assault, to take by storm, to charge. In this context, the word helps us perceive that there is in conceptual knowledge a latent force — one might almost say an explosive power — deriving from the reality of knowledge, its *ḥaqīqa* (inner reality, spiritual essence). It is this which calls out to be "made real" through *taḥaqquq* (verification, realisation in depth), rather than mere factual verification on the surface. This *ḥaqīqa* can be indicated, but never captured, by the words and concepts that make up its formal communicable aspect. By means of this inner force — which its outward conceptual form both hides and evokes — it is capable of effecting a shift of consciousness, from one degree of knowledge to another.[^cite-68]

An indirect, mental conception of reality thus paves the way for a penetrating, existential perception of reality. The "reality of insight" opens the intelligence to reality as such, whereas ordinary insight, like abstract knowledge, remains only at the superficial plane of understanding. The same idea is expressed in a saying of the Imam concerning true understanding, which comes to plumb and so truly *know* the content of knowledge — its own deeper dimensions or buried treasures: "He who understands, knows the depth of knowledge" (⟪ar:من فھم علم گوہر العلم⟫). The effort required to attain true knowledge, as opposed to the mere accumulation of facts, is likewise indicated in the saying: "Through learning and assimilation — such that knowledge becomes deeply rooted in one's consciousness — knowledge is attained" (⟪ar:بالتَّعَلُّم یَنَالَ العِلمْ⟫).

The urgency of the need to realise the immanent power within knowledge — to move from the abstract to the concrete, from potential to actual, from the static to the dynamic, from the formal to the essential — is effectively evoked by *hajama*, a word drawn from the field of battle. It alerts the listener to the danger of mistaking the initial understanding of an idea for its full comprehension, and full intellectual comprehension for the dynamic, spiritual interiorisation of its truth. This interiorisation is a process of infinite unfolding within, not the simple registering of some fact from without. It requires the effective integration of knowledge into being: knowledge from without must be transformed into being from within; it must be woven into the deepest texture of one's existence. Knowledge thus demands not merely the attention of the mind but the total orientation of the soul.

In this ethos, the effective integration of knowledge — the very work of *tawḥīd* — within being is unattainable without the participation of the whole soul. This in turn requires the elimination of every vice that flows from egocentricity. The *ʿāqil*, the true intellectual, is described by the Imam as constantly engaged in "struggle against his own soul" — against its lower inclinations, its passionate whims, its distracting caprices. None of these vices is confined to the plane of morality; each encroaches upon the domain of knowledge, and this will be understood in the very measure that knowledge is grasped as a concrete vision of things, not merely a notional or conceptual understanding. The vices are then perceived as so many clouds obscuring the vision proper to the reality of insight. According to the Qurʾan, evil actions become a "rust" that covers over the heart:

> ⟪quran 83:14⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّا ۖ بَلْۜ رَانَ عَلَىٰ قُلُوبِهِم مَّا كَانُوا۟ يَكْسِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *Nay! Rather, upon their hearts is the rust they used to earn.*

The *ʿāqil* is engaged in constant inner struggle against tendencies which not only sully the soul, but blind the heart. As a virtuous person, he opposes vice on the moral plane because it is contrary to virtue. But vice is also opposed for another reason, one situated on the higher plane of spiritual reality: it contradicts the nature of the Real, obscures the reality of insight, and blinds the "eye" of the heart, which alone can see Allah.

This is not to deny the validity of the moral perspective; rather, the stress falls on the deeper motivation that propels the *ʿāqil* towards virtue. That motivation transcends the moral plane while including it; morality emerges here as the fruit, and spirituality as the seed. By drawing attention to the intellectual aspect of the *ʿāqil*'s motive for being rid of vice, the Imam brings into sharp relief the way in which immorality is rooted in ignorance. To uproot that ignorance is, for the true intellectual, tantamount to dissolving the very substance of the vices. The uprooting demands relentless inner battle — indeed the most formidable of all battles, *al-jihād al-akbar*, the greatest struggle, as the Prophet defined it.

The following sayings of the Imam underline the importance of this inner struggle:

> - Struggling against the soul through knowledge: such is the mark of the intellect.
> - The strongest of people are those who are strongest against their own souls.
> - One who fights his own soul in obedience to Allah and does not sin against Him has, in Allah's eyes, the rank of the righteous martyr.
> - The ultimate battle is that of a man against his own soul.
> - He who knows his soul fights it.
> - No *jihād* is more excellent than the *jihād* of the soul.

In another saying, the Imam clarifies what the Prophet meant by defining the greatest *jihād* as that of the soul (*al-nafs*). It is not so much a question of fighting *against* the soul, as of fighting *for* the soul itself. This emerges from the metaphor by which the Imam defines the struggle: *al-ʿaql* (the intellect) is the leader of the forces of *al-Raḥmān* (the Compassionate), while *al-hawā* (whim, caprice, desire) commands the forces of *al-shayṭān* (the devil). The soul (*al-nafs*) vacillates between them, susceptible to the attraction of both (⟪ar:مُتَجَاذِبَہ بینھما⟫), and enters the domain of whichever triumphs.

These sayings underline that, for the true intellectual, the soul in its entirety must be conquered and enlisted on the side of the intellect. It is not a matter of destroying the lower soul, but of ridding it of the destructive influence of its caprice — of its egoistic whims, its subjectivism and individualism — all of which are connoted by *hawā*. The Prophet, we are told in the Qurʾan, speaks not from *hawā* but from revelation:

> ⟪quran 53:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Nor does he speak from his own desire.*

> ⟪quran 53:4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْىٌۭ يُوحَىٰ ‎⟫
> *It is naught but a revelation revealed.*

The divine objectivity of revelation is contrasted here with the human subjectivity of passional whim. The holy war within is illumined by an analogous polarity in the Imam's sayings: the objectivity of the intellect must prevail against the subjectivity of individual caprice and egotistic desire. It is the intellect that brings to the forefront the divine power of *al-Raḥmān* and combats the forces of *al-shayṭān*, represented by *al-hawā*.

The word *hawā* is further used in the Qurʾan to designate the desires springing from the ego, by means of which the ego becomes a kind of false god:

> ⟪quran 25:43⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ أَفَأَنتَ تَكُونُ عَلَيْهِ وَكِيلًا ‎⟫
> *Have you seen the one who has taken his own desire as his god? Will you then be a guardian over him?*

This is the hidden idolatry (⟪ar:الشرک الخفی⟫) which the Prophet described as more concealed than a black ant crawling on a black stone in a moonless night. To eliminate this idolatry of the ego, a force higher than the ego must be engaged, since it is impossible for the ego to be controlled by anything pertaining to itself; and that higher force is the divine Reality, access to which is opened through the power of the intellect and the graces of faith.[^cite-69] The complementarity between effort to overcome the egoism of *hawā* and the influx of divine grace is finely expressed in the Qurʾan:

> ⟪quran 79:40⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَى ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎⟫
> *And as for him who feared the station of his Lord and restrained the soul from desire,*

> ⟪quran 79:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫
> *Paradise will surely be his abode.*

The soul's fundamental energy is not to be destroyed but converted and redirected — away from the transient objects of individualistic desire, away from the impulses of *al-shayṭān*, and towards the one true object expressed by *al-Raḥmān*. This conquest of the soul involves much more than attaining some mental conception. If a person is to be rendered capable of perceiving the truth in all its dimensions and ramifications across the planes of being, then not only the mind, the will, and the character, but the very disposition of the soul, must be integrated into the truth perceived by the intellect.

For the Imam, the need to win the soul over in its totality follows naturally from his understanding of *tawḥīd*, the most fundamental principle of Islam. *Tawḥīd* is both a noun and a verbal noun. It is often rendered simply as "oneness" or "unity", but it literally means *affirming* one — the affirmation of Allah's oneness, which is the outward, theological sense — and *realising* one — the realisation that there is *but* one Reality, which is the inner, spiritual sense. In the Imam's perspective, the absolutely Real is perceived not only as being one, but also as *making* one, as integrating. The Real is not only unique; it is also unifying. *Tawḥīd* therefore comes to mean not only the affirmation of Allah's oneness, but also "being" one in order to reflect perfectly the One: to know Allah is to be integrated. This is hinted at by the etymology of *ʿaql*, whose primary sense is "to bind, to restrain". For the later mystical tradition, the limitative side of the word would be stressed — the intellect as that which defines and encloses meaning, contrasted with the heart that intuits and discloses. Here, by contrast, the intellect is that which *binds together* the disparate elements of the soul into an organic unity. This principle is expressed in a series of the Imam's sayings, each of which merits deep reflection:

> - He who knows Allah integrates himself (*man ʿarafa Allāh tawaḥḥada*).
> - He who knows his soul disengages himself (*man ʿarafa nafsahu tajarrada*).
> - He who knows people isolates himself (*man ʿarafa al-nās tafarrada*).
> - He who knows the world withholds himself (*man ʿarafa al-dunyā tazahhada*).

Elsewhere this total adherence to the Real is referred to by the Imam as "sincerity", *ṣidq* or *ikhlāṣ* — terms which denote far more than mere truthfulness, as the root of *ikhlāṣ* already shows. The verb *khaluṣa* means to be utterly pure, true to one's essence, unadulterated by any extraneous substance. This dimension of meaning is well expressed in the Imam's saying: "Make purely for Allah your action and your knowledge, your love and your hatred, your taking and your leaving, your speech and your silence." To be totally sincere is to make oneself *purely* for Allah, with no stain of impurity — that is, no presence of what is other than Allah — in one's devotion, action, intention, or even sentiment. One must love and hate only in function of one's relationship with Allah. Of all the tendencies that insinuate themselves into one's motivations, the most pernicious is egotism. *Ikhlāṣ*, pure sincerity, is the active effort to *be*, *think*, and *act* purely for Allah — that is, with selflessness. Hence the Imam's stress on the holy war within the soul as the ultimate battle. The one who prevails in this battle attains the rank of the "righteous martyr"; the victor is the martyr, because he has sacrificed his lower life for the sake of Allah, with whom is the real life — that which is witnessed (*shāhid*) by the intellect, the only element in human consciousness capable of regarding the soul objectively, as "the other".[^cite-70]

To repeat: "Struggling against the soul through knowledge — such is the mark of the intellect." The intellectual in this battle is also a bearer of *witness* (*al-shāhid* — meaning both martyr and witness, as in the original Greek *martyr*). He bears witness to Allah through the intellect's sacrifice of what opposes the truth of Allah; and the key opponent is his own egotism, his own false life. To possess perfect *ikhlāṣ* is to be rid of all hypocritical self-preoccupation and to install in its place a sincere *theocentricity*, a mode of being centred upon Allah rather than upon oneself. Thus *ikhlāṣ* is to be *for* Allah, to *belong* to Allah, as the Qurʾanic verse indicates:

> ⟪quran 6:162⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِنَّ صَلَاتِى وَنُسُكِى وَمَحْيَاىَ وَمَمَاتِى لِلَّهِ رَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ ‎⟫
> *Say: My prayer, my sacrifice, my living and my dying are for Allah, Lord of the worlds.*

That worship is the first thing mentioned in this verse is of particular significance for anyone wishing to appreciate the nature of the Imam's spiritual ethos (⟪ar:مزاج⟫). What must be stressed in any presentation of this ethos is the indispensable role of worship and devotion. One of the key distinguishing features of the Imam's perspective, indeed, is the stress he places upon prayer — taking the term in its widest sense to include all those means, from formal worship and supplication to meditation, reflection, remembrance and contemplation, by which the individual is oriented and attuned to the Real, *al-Ḥaqq*.

Worship is therefore an integral aspect of *ikhlāṣ*, in the very measure that worship relates to and sustains a fundamental dimension of the human soul. That within the soul which yearns to worship, and is satisfied only by the sustenance worship affords, must be given its due. Within a spiritual context, if worship is marginalised, one's sincerity is compromised — for one is not being sincere to Allah, not being just to Allah, not rendering Him His due. And the Imam's spiritual logic dictates that if one is not just with Allah, one cannot be just to His creatures: "Whoever establishes well-being between himself and Allah, Allah will establish well-being between him and mankind."

One may here recall the Qurʾanic verse:

> ⟪quran 15:99⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱعْبُدْ رَبَّكَ حَتَّىٰ يَأْتِيَكَ ٱلْيَقِينُ ‎⟫
> *And worship your Lord until certainty comes to you.*

The quest for knowledge thus demands total dedication if it is to yield up its inner riches — and this dedication includes that transformation of consciousness shaped by total concentration upon the divine Reality, which is prayer in one of its deepest modes. In this form of prayer, the intensity of dedication is such that there is no room in consciousness for anything other than the object to which one is dedicated: the remembrance (⟪ar:ذکر⟫) of Allah strictly implies the forgetting of all else, and pre-eminently of oneself. As mentioned earlier, the spiritual reality of the ⟪ar:ذکر⟫ can only be attained when "you forget your soul in your remembrance". Concentration upon the divine Reality as the supreme object of knowledge, rendered present through the Name or Names of Allah, is thus a mode of prayer; and for it to be effective, both presence of mind and a serious engagement of the will are needed. It is far from sufficient to pray absent-mindedly, mechanically. As the Imam says: "He who prays without exertion is like one who shoots arrows without a bow." Likewise, the process of acquiring knowledge is far from passive or easy: "Knowledge calls out for action; if it is answered, it remains; otherwise it departs."

The same idea is expressed more forcefully in another saying: "When you hear knowledge being imparted, cleave to it; do not mix it up with jest, lest hearts spew it forth." Knowledge that is not taken seriously will avail nothing. It remains undigested, refusing to be assimilated by the heart — the faculty that has access to the reality of insight, and which can therefore *see* Allah. Indeed, it is not the individual who assimilates knowledge to himself; rather it is knowledge — or, more properly, the reality of being expressed by true knowledge — that assimilates the individual to itself: "Acquire knowledge, and true life will acquire you." The relationship between life and consciousness, so central to the intrinsic function of the spirit as discussed earlier, is again being stressed. At first, knowledge is sought by the individual, and consciousness is cultivated; then life seeks the individual, as his being makes itself real, or realises itself more fully within him. The individual first makes an active effort to integrate knowledge within his being; at a certain point, this activity is transformed into passive receptivity — being, "true life", integrates the individual within itself. Returning to the discourse to Kumayl: "Through them knowledge penetrates the reality of insight." It is not the knowers who penetrate; it is knowledge that penetrates into the reality of insight, doing so *through* them — and this in the very measure of their effacement within knowledge, an effacement that is the shadow cast by their effective integration within the life which has acquired them.

### They rejoice in their intimacy with the spirit of certainty

The next sentence of the discourse to Kumayl is of particular importance in helping us appreciate the sheer happiness that flows from the life of the spirit. In the Arabic phrase ⟪ar:وبشِّرُ روح الیقین⟫, the primary meaning of *bashara* is having intimate experience of a thing, coming into direct physical contact with it; and the same form of the verb also relates to joy. Hence the phrase "rejoice in intimate contact" better conveys something of the meaning of this single word. To touch the spirit of certainty is to come into contact not with some cold logical fact — the conclusion of a purely mental process — but to engage deeply with the object of certainty, with that of which one is certain. Ultimately, this is nothing less than the divine itself. Since this Reality is infinitely more beatific than any conceivable paradisal bliss — according to the Qurʾan, the divine ⟪ar:رِضوَان⟫ (beatitude, contentment) is greater than Paradise:

> ⟪quran 9:72⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَٱلْمُؤْمِنَتِ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ خَلِدِينَ فِيهَا وَمَسَكِنَ طَيِّبَةًۭ فِى جَنَّتِ عَدْنٍۢ ۚ وَرِضْوَنٌۭ مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُوَ ٱلْفَوْزُ ٱلْعَظِيمُ ‎⟫
> *Allah has promised the believers, men and women, Gardens beneath which rivers flow, abiding therein for ever, and goodly dwellings in Gardens of Eden — and the greatest of all is contentment from Allah. That is the supreme triumph.*

— it cannot but bestow joy upon the soul which effectively opens itself to that Reality. In the Imam's words: "Learning and reflecting upon knowledge is the delight of the knowers." This is what one might call an *epistemology of joy*, for "the most joyous of mankind is the *ʿāqil*." Such a joyous epistemology — which flies in the face of modern scientific conceptions of knowledge as dry, cold and abstract — must be considered carefully, for it reveals a crucial dimension of the spiritual knowledge proper to the Imam's perspective, and indeed to every spiritual tradition worthy of the name. Coming into contact with truths should impart happiness, and this in the measure that the truths in question are fundamental to one's being, or to Being as such. The two modes of being are ultimately identical, given the uniqueness — the *one-and-onliness* — of Being. That which has no second, no other, cannot enter the category of number; being is indivisible. Hence the being of the individual cannot ultimately be different from Being as such, however great may be the existential disparity — or rather, the incommensurability — between the individual and Allah. True knowledge is knowledge of Being; it is therefore necessarily a kind of self-discovery, even if knowledge of the Absolute is impossible without absolute self-abandonment. The highest discovery calls for the deepest effacement.

In the initial stages of this process, however, the true knowledge acquired by the intellectual is a kind of self-discovery that imparts the happiness of a homecoming — a return from the exile of ignorance. The "most intellectual" of people is "the one closest to Allah" and "the one most alive". To be close to Allah is to be fully alive, and this true life imparts profound joy, the sheer joy of *being*. This is a joy proper to existence as such, and is independent of particular experiences that may or may not be pleasurable.

Here again the crucial relationship between life and consciousness comes into view: the fruits of the inspiration of the spirit of Allah on the one hand, and between this life of spiritual consciousness and joy on the other. Those who are true to the spirit of Allah within them truly possess joy. It is by reason of an intimate and unshakeable certainty of the divine goodness and compassion that the true *faqīh* — not so much the jurist as "one who truly understands" — is defined by the Imam as "he who does not make people despair of the mercy of Allah, and does not make them lose hope in the gracious spirit of Allah (*rawḥ Allāh*)." Such is the sage's state of immersion in the joyous certainty of Allah's mercy that there is no place for despair. Indeed, to despair of this mercy is a sign of disbelief:

> ⟪quran 15:56⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قَالَ وَمَن يَقْنَطُ مِن رَّحْمَةِ رَبِّهِۦٓ إِلَّا ٱلضَّآلُّونَ ‎⟫
> *He said: And who despairs of the mercy of his Lord except those who have gone astray?*

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *When those who believe in Our signs come to you, say: Peace be upon you. Your Lord has prescribed mercy upon Himself, so that whoever of you commits evil in ignorance, then repents thereafter and makes amends — surely He is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful.*

The words "My mercy encompasses all things" and "Your Lord has prescribed mercy upon Himself" are brought fully to life in souls that possess profound, not merely notional, knowledge of the beatific nature of the divine Reality. These are the ones who truly understand: the true *fuqahāʾ*.

This joy, born of intimate knowledge of the mercy of Allah, is inseparable from beauty. The perception of beauty is another natural association of the intellect in the Imam's perspective. The appreciation of beauty is not merely a question of subjective aesthetics; it is an objective aspect of the function of the intellect. Beauty also leads to the heart of ethics. The Arabic *iḥsān* is often rendered simply as "virtue" or "excellence", but one of its key literal meanings is "making beautiful" — for *ḥusn* means beauty. *Iḥsān* can therefore be understood as that which "makes the soul beautiful". In this light, the relationship between intellect, ethics and aesthetics is more clearly discerned. "The excellence of the intellect," says the Imam, "is in the beauty of things outward and inward" (⟪ar:جمال الظواہر والبواطن⟫). The outward beauty of forms and actions must be complemented by inward beauty — beauty of soul, virtue in the most integral and penetrating sense of the word. All of this follows naturally from two sayings of the Prophet: "Truly Allah is beautiful and He loves beauty," and "Assume the character traits of Allah."

Because Allah loves beauty, the cultivation of beautiful traits within oneself makes one lovable to Allah. This process is inseparable from the emulation of the virtues brought to their perfection in the soul of the Prophet:

> ⟪quran 3:31⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ ٱللَّهَ فَٱتَّبِعُونِى يُحْبِبْكُمُ ٱللَّهُ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ ذُنُوبَكُمْ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *Say: If you love Allah, then follow me; Allah will love you and forgive you your sins. And Allah is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful.*

This drawing of Allah's love through making oneself beautiful, in the fullest sense, is alluded to in another saying of the Imam: "The foundation of the intellect is the assimilation of love" (⟪ar:أَوَّلُ العَقل التَّوَدُّدْ⟫). Rather than simply referring to love (⟪ar:وُد/مَوَدَّۃ⟫), the Imam draws attention to the *process* of making oneself lovable to Allah by using the form *tawaddud*. This alludes to the integration or realisation of the principle of love within oneself, as well as the outward expression of that love which is felt within. Love is thus appreciated both as outward radiance and as inner attraction.

To follow the Prophet, and so make oneself receptive to the divine influx of love, means among other things to cultivate the "prophetic" virtues — prophetic not in the sense that they are exclusive to the Prophet, but in that he is deemed to have realised virtue in its plenitude, serving as exemplar for his followers. It is thus not surprising to find that it is not only beauty and love that articulate the receptivity of the intellect to the divine Reality, but also such qualities as kindness and contentment, courtesy, generosity, modesty, and wise forbearance. None of these moral qualities is absent from the soul of the true intellectual. There can be no wisdom or intellect in the fullest sense if the soul lacks these fundamental qualities. It is thanks to the presence of these virtues that the intellect develops those dimensions of depth and breadth without which it remains confined to the flat, horizontal plane of its own operations. Without virtue, intellect remains confined to the activity of reason alone, which — until touched by faith and deepened by grace — remains unaware of what lies beneath the surface of its own field. It remains oblivious of the hidden treasures of the intellect; blind to the need to integrate the whole soul within the mould of that integral, unifying virtue which bestows integrity upon the intelligence. Such integration, such "making one", is absolutely fundamental to *tawḥīd*. So *tawḥīd* can now be understood as a *dynamic process of spiritual unification* demanded by the idea of the oneness of Allah. Truth must inspire the soul; but equally, virtue must aerate the intelligence, providing it with the leaven (*khamīr*) by which it expands to its full dimensions.

Sinful, immoral qualities are grasped here not only as vices but as so many blind spots — intellectual dysfunctions. The heart is diseased by vice, its eye blinded by them and so unable to see the Real, as the Qurʾan declares:

> ⟪quran 2:10⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فِى قُلُوبِهِم مَّرَضٌۭ فَزَادَهُمُ ٱللَّهُ مَرَضًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا كَانُوا۟ يَكْذِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *In their hearts is a disease, so Allah has increased their disease; and theirs is a painful punishment for the lies they used to tell.*

> ⟪quran 22:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَلَمْ يَسِيرُوا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ فَتَكُونَ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ يَعْقِلُونَ بِهَآ أَوْ آذَانٌۭ يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَا ۖ فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَعْمَى ٱلْأَبْصَرُ وَلَكِن تَعْمَى ٱلْقُلُوبُ ٱلَّتِى فِى ٱلصُّدُورِ ‎⟫
> *Have they not journeyed through the land, that they might have hearts to understand, or ears to hear? For it is not the eyes that grow blind, but it is the hearts within the breasts that grow blind.*

As noted, the vices are all comprised within egotism, and this in turn is often described simply as caprice (⟪ar:ھوی⟫). In one saying the Imam treats the conquest of caprice as tantamount to salvation: "He attains deliverance whose intellect dominates his caprice." Deliverance — *falāḥ*, which comprises both salvation and beatitude — is therefore in some measure accessible here and now. It is not merely a grace bestowed after one's demise. This deliverance involves tasting the joy that emanates from certainty, from intimate contact with the spirit of that certainty. As to the means of cultivating receptivity to this spirit of certainty, what is required, over and above obedience to the rules and regulations of the revealed Law, is that combination of purity of intention and sincerity of devotion which is expressed by *ikhlāṣ*. Without this sincerity or purity, compliance with formal rules is nothing but hypocrisy (*nifāq*) and ostentation (*riyāʾ*), which in turn is defined by the Imam as the gravest of all sins, *shirk* — the attribution of partners to Allah: "Know that the slightest *riyāʾ* is *shirk*." This sentence may be taken as a commentary upon one of the most important Qurʾanic condemnations of hypocrisy, which speaks of those who deny the essence of faith even while outwardly conforming to it:

> ⟪quran 107:1⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ ٱلَّذِى يُكَذِّبُ بِٱلدِّينِ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen the one who denies the Recompense?*

> ⟪quran 107:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَذَلِكَ ٱلَّذِى يَدُعُّ ٱلْيَتِيمَ ‎⟫
> *That is he who repulses the orphan,*

> ⟪quran 107:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا يَحُضُّ عَلَىٰ طَعَامِ ٱلْمِسْكِينِ ‎⟫
> *and does not urge the feeding of the poor.*

> ⟪quran 107:4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎⟫
> *So woe to those who pray,*

> ⟪quran 107:5⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎⟫
> *who are heedless of their prayer,*

> ⟪quran 107:6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎⟫
> *who make a show of themselves,*

> ⟪quran 107:7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيَمْنَعُونَ ٱلْمَاعُونَ ‎⟫
> *and withhold even small kindnesses.*

This short *sūra* makes clear that being "religious" in one's formal acts of devotion has no value whatsoever unless those acts are integrated into a life of virtue, and unless one performs them with the right intention — that is, with *ikhlāṣ*. It also helps us see why the Imam's ethos should be called not merely "religious" but "spiritual": it takes the ideals of religion to their most profound application. Without that dimension of depth, religion is meaningless.

### There is no religion for one who has no intellect

"There is no religion for one who has no intellect," says the Imam. Likewise: "Action without knowledge is error." It is the intention motivating the action that counts — for action, all action, is dust, except what is purified, accomplished sincerely, within it. This detachment from action as such, and the orientation instead towards an inner state of being from which good actions cannot but emerge, clearly echoes the Qurʾan:

> ⟪quran 22:37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏لَن يَنَالَ ٱللَّهَ لُحُومُهَا وَلَا دِمَآؤُهَا وَلَكِن يَنَالُهُ ٱلتَّقْوَىٰ مِنكُمْ ۚ كَذَلِكَ سَخَّرَهَا لَكُمْ لِتُكَبِّرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عَلَىٰ مَا هَدَىٰكُمْ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلْمُحْسِنِينَ ‎⟫
> *It is neither their flesh nor their blood that reaches Allah; it is the piety from you that reaches Him. Thus has He made them subject to you that you may magnify Allah for His guidance to you. And give glad tidings to those who do good.*

One might argue that no group better exemplified the principle expressed in this saying than the *Khawārij*. Among those who rebelled against the Imam were numerous "reciters" (*qurrāʾ*, sing. *qāriʾ*) of the Qurʾan — people who enjoyed considerable religious prestige on account of their familiarity with the sacred text and their intense devotional practice. Yet their piety was more apparent than real: it was a "zeal of bitterness", an imitation of true piety. When his supporters made mention of the long night vigils performed by members of this group, the Imam gave this sharp reply: "Sleeping with certainty is better than praying with doubt." Certainty, as we have seen, imparts peace and joy; thus the sleep of one immersed in what the Imam calls "the spirit of certainty" is a bodily repose that further deepens the happiness flowing from a good conscience and spiritual certitude. This spiritual certitude is itself understood as a kind of permanent wakefulness, in the sense of being awake to the higher realities. Bodily sleep does not contradict spiritual wakefulness — as the Prophet himself said: "My eyes sleep, but my heart sleeps not."

In relation to formal worship, the true intellectual is one who is obedient to the divine injunction to pray. But rather than praying mechanically and believing that the action alone suffices, the *ʿāqil* knows that such obedience is a necessary but not sufficient condition for achieving receptivity to grace. There must be consciousness of what one is doing and why one is doing it. And it is this awareness, together with virtue, or inward beauty, that attracts the divine acceptance. "The most worthy knowledge for you," says the Imam, "is that by virtue of whose presence your action is accepted by Allah."

### They make easy what the extravagant find harsh; they befriend that by which the ignorant are estranged

This sentence takes us, among other things, to the impact made upon the soul of the true sage by the recollection of the inevitability of death in this world, and the consequent necessity of renunciation within it. In the first place, that which is found "harsh" by the extravagant — the avid, worldly types — is outward adversity, difficulty, deprivation. These are all circumstances which the Qurʾan presents as trials inevitable in the life of this world:

> ⟪quran 2:155⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَنَبْلُوَنَّكُم بِشَىْءٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْخَوْفِ وَٱلْجُوعِ وَنَقْصٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْأَمْوَلِ وَٱلْأَنفُسِ وَٱلثَّمَرَتِ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلصَّبِرِينَ ‎⟫
> *Surely We shall test you with something of fear and hunger, and with loss of wealth, lives and fruits. And give glad tidings to those who are patient,*

> ⟪quran 2:156⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَآ أَصَبَتْهُم مُّصِيبَةٌۭ قَالُوٓا۟ إِنَّا لِلَّهِ وَإِنَّآ إِلَيْهِ رَجِعُونَ ‎⟫
> *who, when calamity befalls them, say: Truly we belong to Allah, and to Him we shall return.*

> ⟪quran 2:157⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أُو۟لَٓئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَتٌۭ مِّن رَّبِّهِمْ وَرَحْمَةٌۭ ۖ وَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْمُهْتَدُونَ ‎⟫
> *Upon them are blessings from their Lord and mercy; and they are the rightly guided.*

The wise, the rightly guided (*al-muhtadūn*), perceive the blessings that are showered down upon those who are patient in the face of afflictions — patience itself being a fruit of the completeness of their knowledge of the truth.

> ⟪quran 103:1⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْعَصْرِ ‎⟫
> *By Time!*

> ⟪quran 103:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَفِى خُسْرٍ ‎⟫
> *Surely man is in loss,*

> ⟪quran 103:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلصَّبْرِ ‎⟫
> *save those who believe and do righteous deeds, and exhort one another to truth and exhort one another to patience.*

These are the believers who remain steadfast in the face of trials, firmly rooted in awareness of their origin and end and of the fact that "to Him we are ever returning". They can therefore *make easy* the trials and difficulties of life, whereas the extravagant experience them only in their aspect of harshness and bitterness. The ease that permanently exists in all difficulty is hidden from the ignorant but discerned by the wise:

> ⟪quran 94:5⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَإِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا ‎⟫
> *Surely with hardship comes ease,*

> ⟪quran 94:6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًۭا ‎⟫
> *surely with hardship comes ease.*

The wise go even further than anticipating ease as the inevitable fruit of hardship. They already taste that fruit as the seed hidden within hardship itself, for they actually "befriend that by which the ignorant are estranged".

A first level of meaning here is illumined by the Imam's saying: "Death is more intimate to me than the breast of the mother to the suckling babe." In the Qurʾanic verse cited above, the mention of trials is preceded by a reminder that those slain in the path of Allah are not really dead — "they are alive, but you do not perceive". We have here not simply an affirmation of life hereafter, but an allusion to the esoteric meaning of being "slain" for Allah: ⟪ar:الفنا فی اللہ⟫, *extinction in Allah*. The Imam's intimacy with death can be seen to relate to this dying *while still alive*, which he also alludes to in another saying: "I am the death of the dead." For life in the world is itself a kind of death — a limitation, a privation, in contrast to the infinite abundance of the divine realms. Death in this world, therefore, is tantamount to true life:

> ⟪quran 29:64⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا هَذِهِ ٱلْحَيَوٰةُ ٱلدُّنْيَآ إِلَّا لَهْوٌۭ وَلَعِبٌۭ ۚ وَإِنَّ ٱلدَّارَ ٱلْآخِرَةَ لَهِىَ ٱلْحَيَوَانُ ۚ لَوْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And this life of the world is naught but diversion and play; surely the Abode of the Hereafter — that is the true life, if they but knew.*

It is important to stress, however, that it is not the physical world as such that is to be negated; rather, it is worldliness — the egotistic attachment to this world — that must be overcome. Here it is useful to dwell briefly on one of the key principles of the Imam's perspective, which is stressed repeatedly throughout the *Nahj al-Balāgha*: the principle of *zuhd*, which cannot be rendered by any single English word. It comprises several meanings: asceticism, austerity, abstention, detachment, "doing without", "making little of". The following passage from the *Nahj* well expresses the attitude of the *zāhid* towards this world:

> The world is an abode for which annihilation is ordained, and from which departure is decreed for its people. It is sweet and verdant, and it hastens to one who seeks it; it confounds the heart that gazes upon it. So set out from it with the best of provision available to you, and ask not from it more than what suffices, nor seek from it more than what can be attained.

What is this "best of provision" (*zād*)? In many places throughout the *Nahj* it is described as *taqwā*, another word that defies easy translation, conveying piety, fear of Allah, awe, and consciousness of Allah. "I strongly enjoin upon you, O servants of Allah, *taqwā*, which is the true provision," says the Imam. This provision for the next world is attained only in the measure of one's detachment from the perishable aspects of the life of this world:

> ⟪quran 17:18⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَّن كَانَ يُرِيدُ ٱلْعَاجِلَةَ عَجَّلْنَا لَهُۥ فِيهَا مَا نَشَآءُ لِمَن نُّرِيدُ ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَا لَهُۥ جَهَنَّمَ يَصْلَىٰهَا مَذْمُومًۭا مَّدْحُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *Whoever desires the fleeting life, We hasten for him therein what We will, for whom We will; then We assign him Hell, wherein he will burn, disgraced and outcast.*

The contemptible aspect of this world is described by the Imam in vivid terms:

> - By Allah, this world of yours is more contemptible in my eyes than a chewed-up bone of a pig in the hand of a leper.
> - The image of this world is that of a serpent — soft to the touch, but filled with virulent poison.
> - This world is as worthless to me as that which drips from the nose of a goat.

It is the grandeur and beauty of Allah that render the world insignificant and distasteful. Only in the light of the Absolute do the world's pleasures and attractions appear fleeting and illusory: "The greatness of the Creator within you renders the creatures small in your sight." In a similar vein, the Imam refers to a "brother in Allah", saying: "What made him great in my eyes was the smallness of the world in his." This, according to Qurʾanic usage, is the true meaning of *zuhd*. In Sūrat Yūsuf, the brothers of Yūsuf "deemed him of little value", selling him for a small price:

> ⟪quran 12:20⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَشَرَوْهُ بِثَمَنٍۭ بَخْسٍۢ دَرَهِمَ مَعْدُودَةٍۢ وَكَانُوا۟ فِيهِ مِنَ ٱلزَّهِدِينَ ‎⟫
> *And they sold him for a paltry price — a few dirhams counted — and they reckoned him of little value.*

In relation to him they were described as *zāhidīn*. The world, in the Imam's perspective, is likewise reckoned of little value — not that it is altogether without value, but that, in relation to the Hereafter, in relation to eternity, in relation to the ultimate Reality, it is rendered all but insignificant. All created things are reduced to infinitesimal, fleeting shadows, destined for annihilation:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And do not invoke with Allah any other god. There is no god but He. All things perish except His Face. To Him belongs the judgement, and to Him you shall be returned.*

Yet the world is not deprived of all value:

> ⟪quran 17:44⟫
> ⟪ar:‏تُسَبِّحُ لَهُ ٱلسَّمَوَتُ ٱلسَّبْعُ وَٱلْأَرْضُ وَمَن فِيهِنَّ ۚ وَإِن مِّن شَىْءٍ إِلَّا يُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِهِۦ وَلَكِن لَّا تَفْقَهُونَ تَسْبِيحَهُمْ ۗ إِنَّهُۥ كَانَ حَلِيمًا غَفُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *The seven heavens and the earth, and all that is therein, glorify Him. There is not a thing that does not glorify Him with His praise — but you do not understand their glorification. Surely He is Ever-Forbearing, Oft-Forgiving.*

Everything that exists, every creature within it, thus proclaims the infinite creativity of the Creator. To help us comprehend this universal praise imaginatively, the Qurʾan adds:

> ⟪quran 24:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ عَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *Do you not see that Allah is glorified by whoever is in the heavens and the earth, and by the birds with outspread wings? Each one knows its own prayer and glorification, and Allah is fully aware of what they do.*

It is thus not at all contradictory for the Imam to despise the world and yet describe the beauties of virgin nature — including that unsurpassable marvel, the peacock — in a sermon which also describes birds in general, ants, serpents, and elephants. It is noteworthy that the sermon concludes with an exhilarating description of Paradise, comparing the marvels of this world with the delights of the next. When set beside the latter, all terrestrial phenomena pale into insignificance. For once the eye of the heart is directed to Paradise, "your soul would become averse to the marvels of this world — its passions, its pleasures and its embellished scenery."

It might seem contradictory to bring together such apparently opposed qualities as joy in certainty, discussed above, and the "befriending" of hardship. Yet the latter is in fact the fruit of the former. All difficulties without exception are endured thanks to the spiritual resources made available by faith combined with intellectual assimilation — rather, in the measure that faith is intellectually assimilated and thus becomes *maʿrifa*, gnosis. This *maʿrifa* comprises a certainty so deep and so complete that, in the famous saying of the Imam, "Even if the veil were lifted, my certainty would not increase" — ⟪ar:لو کشف الغطاء ما ازدت یقینا⟫.

It is possible to believe, at one level of the mind, that "there is no deity but Allah". Yet the Imam draws attention to what this apparently simple belief implies when it is *sincere* or *pure*: "I bear witness that there is no deity but Allah alone, who has no partner — a testimony whose sincerity has been tested and whose essence has been assimilated with conviction" (⟪ar:مُعتَقَداً مُصَعصَھَا⟫). The word *muṣaṣṣa* refers to the choicest and purest part of any substance, that which constitutes its essence. The root *maṣṣa* means "to suck"; the idea is that the liquid or juice of a substance contains its essence, that which is sucked out of it. In the present context, the Imam stresses the spiritual substance of his testimony, as opposed to mere verbal affirmation or mental comprehension of the words. He affirms a heartfelt connection with the One to whom his testimony bears witness; the words defining the testimony echo its reality, but are not to be confused with that reality itself. He continues: "We cling to it always, for as long as we endure, storing it up as protection against the terrors that will befall us. For truly, it renders faith resolute, opens up spiritual virtue, pleases *al-Raḥmān*, and repels *al-shayṭān*."

Returning to "befriending that by which the ignorant are estranged" — this implies not only the trials of this life, which are a source of strength for the wise and of repulsion for the ignorant, but also the inescapability of death. For the wise, the encounter with Allah for a blissful eternity is a release — a mode of *tawḥīd* in which the soul enjoys ever greater degrees of integration within higher principles. For the ignorant, by contrast, death is perceived as frightful disintegration: not the beginning of an endless life, but the end of their world. This connects with the earlier theme of dying while still alive, *fanāʾ* — extinction, effacement, the perishing of egoistic consciousness in the face of the Absolute. The ignorant shrink in horror at the prospect of losing what they falsely take to be *their* life; they fail to realise that the sacrifice of egoistic and limited self-consciousness is precisely the basis upon which infinite consciousness is glimpsed or "tasted". One can only taste the ocean of the Real by being drowned in it. One might even say that the very means to this ultimate attainment — the act of pure prayer, total concentration upon the Real — is also embraced by the wise and feared by the ignorant. For this concentration strictly precludes all worldly or egotistic preoccupations; the very intensity of concentration upon the Absolute burns away thoughts of the relative. For those who ignorantly identify with relativities, both inward and outward, this implies a kind of death. For the wise, on the contrary, concentration upon the Absolute — the unsullied remembrance of Allah — is a joyous contemplation of reality before which the ego is displaced and all illusions dispelled. This leads directly to the next sentence of the discourse.

### With their bodies, they keep company with the world, while their spirits are tied to the transcendent realm

This sentence can be more concretely understood when read in the light of another well-known saying of the Imam, where he describes himself as belonging to a group whose degree of spirituality is such that "their hearts are in the Gardens of Paradise while their bodies are at work." To be tied or attached to that realm, which comprises the paradisal abodes and extends up to the divine Presence itself, implies that the wise are already *within* that transcendent realm more than they are in this earthly one. This helps explain the saying quoted earlier: Allah keeps man perpetually in that which his soul desires. Those whose hearts or spirits are *in* the transcendent domain are those whose consciousness is substantially — not merely conceptually — determined by transcendent realities. Those whose consciousness is determined by worldly matters are *in* this world, in the sense of being enclosed by its formal limitations; their orientation and imagination are trapped within a worldly framework, and their actions bear the mark of that worldliness. The actions of the wise, on the contrary, are the fruits of their immersion in a higher reality. One might say that their outward actions in the world disguise their inward transcendence of all action: they act, but are not bound by the fruits of their action. As stated earlier, they are aware that "action — all action — is dust, except what is purified, accomplished sincerely, within it."

It would be appropriate now to dwell briefly on the role played by the notion of the Hereafter within the ethical framework of the Imam. As we have seen, and will see again, the Hereafter is repeatedly invoked or evoked in his discourses. Is this merely a question of offering a heavenly carrot and threatening a hellish stick, in order simply to "enjoin the good and forbid the evil"? Even if the answer is affirmative at one level, there is a deeper side to this seemingly simplistic deployment of the ethical import of divine warnings and promises.

The point of view here is defined essentially by the spiritual reality, not only of Allah but also of the Hereafter — both objectively, in itself, and subjectively, insofar as it is assimilated by the individual. The Hereafter thus becomes a dynamic dimension — a process, an orientation, a reflux within the very soul of the believer — rather than a mere belief or hope. Anticipation of the Hereafter is one thing; its *realisation* is something else entirely. And it is this realisation that characterises the soul of the friend of Allah (*walī Allāh*), the saint and the sage.

As noted earlier, the Imam says in a famous sentence which bears witness to his state of total immersion within the reality of which he is certain: "Were the veil of this world to be removed, my certitude would not increase" (⟪ar:لو کشف الغطاء ما ازدت یقینا⟫). The anticipation, or foretaste, of the Hereafter is deepened in proportion to one's virtue, piety and sanctity. It does not become merely a heuristic tool whose value is restricted to its impact on moral action and is thus rendered superfluous once that impact is achieved. In this connection the following passage from the *Nahj* deserves reflection: "If you were to cast the eye of your heart towards what is described to you of the Garden, your soul would become averse to the marvels of this world — its passions, its pleasures, its embellished scenery. And your soul would be mesmerised in contemplation of the swaying trees whose roots lie hidden in dunes of musk on the banks of the rivers of the Garden, and the clusters of dazzling pearls hanging from the branches of its trees."

It is, of course, true that the highest degree of spirituality transcends desire for Paradise and fear of Hell. But this means that when such higher degrees of realisation have been attained, the state of the soul is one that can properly be characterised as paradisal — already so utterly content with the beatific presence of Allah that it can desire nothing more. This state of the soul is called in the Qurʾan *al-nafs al-muṭmaʾinna*:

> ⟪quran 89:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫
> *O soul at peace!*

The Imam frequently echoes, implicitly if not explicitly, the Qurʾanic principle that the Hereafter is "better and more lasting":

> ⟪quran 87:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَبْقَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *And the Hereafter is better and more lasting.*

The Hereafter is not only the *time* when divine warnings and promises are consummated; it is also the *space* within which all positive qualities — human, angelic, divine — are manifested in their absolute nature. These qualities are glimpsed on earth, as reflections of the higher realities which encompass and subtly penetrate the entire sphere of terrestrial existence. The Qurʾan, perhaps more so than any other scripture, presents to the imagination numerous and complex descriptions of paradisal bliss. One of the key functions of these descriptions is alluded to in the Qurʾan itself:

> ⟪quran 38:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Indeed, We chose them through a pure quality: the remembrance of the Abode.*

The mere thought of Paradise is itself a purification of mind and heart — a means of averting from the soul the ever-present temptation to seek its ultimate happiness and well-being in this world alone. One's well-being in this world, with respect to action, lies in the performance of good deeds; and such well-being is proportioned to the depth of one's belief that:

> ⟪quran 73:20⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ إِنَّ رَبَّكَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُومُ أَدْنَىٰ مِن ثُلُثَىِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَنِصْفَهُۥ وَثُلُثَهُۥ وَطَآئِفَةٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلَّذِينَ مَعَكَ ۚ وَٱللَّهُ يُقَدِّرُ ٱلَّيْلَ وَٱلنَّهَارَ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن لَّن تُحْصُوهُ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ ٱلْقُرْآنِ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن سَيَكُونُ مِنكُم مَّرْضَىٰ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يَضْرِبُونَ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ يَبْتَغُونَ مِن فَضْلِ ٱللَّهِ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يُقَتِلُونَ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ ۚ وَأَقِيمُوا۟ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ وَآتُوا۟ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَأَقْرِضُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ قَرْضًا حَسَنًۭا ۚ وَمَا تُقَدِّمُوا۟ لِأَنفُسِكُم مِّنْ خَيْرٍۢ تَجِدُوهُ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ هُوَ خَيْرًۭا وَأَعْظَمَ أَجْرًۭا ۚ وَٱسْتَغْفِرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۢ ‎⟫
> *Your Lord knows that you stand in prayer almost two-thirds of the night, or half, or a third of it — and a party of those with you. And Allah measures the night and the day. He knows you cannot keep count of it, so He has turned to you in mercy. So recite of the Qurʾan what is easy for you. He knows that there will be among you the sick, and others travelling through the land seeking the bounty of Allah, and yet others fighting in Allah's path. So recite of it what is easy, establish the prayer, give the alms, and lend to Allah a goodly loan. Whatever good you send forward for yourselves, you will find it with Allah — better and greater in reward. And seek Allah's forgiveness; surely Allah is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful.*

In other words, a sincere orientation towards the Hereafter is transformed into a perception of heavenly beatitude already in this lower world, in the very form of those good acts and attitudes which are of one and the same nature as the felicity to which they lead. In this light, morally good actions and noble intentions are grasped, by one who sees beyond the veil of this world, as vivid prefigurations of heavenly realities, and not merely as ethical prerequisites for salvation. Goodness, in other words, does not just lead to a heavenly reward; it *already is* something of that reward, as the Qurʾan asks:

> ⟪quran 55:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫
> *Is there any reward for goodness other than goodness?*

The Imam's saying — "The fruit of good action is like its root" — may be read as an echo of this idea: the end is already present in the means that lead to it. Finally, let us cite the following verse of the Qurʾan, which is a fitting way to conclude this topic:

> ⟪quran 2:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds, that for them are Gardens beneath which rivers flow. Whenever they are provided with fruit from them as sustenance, they will say: This is what we were provided with before — and they will be given the like thereof; and therein they shall have purified mates, and therein they shall abide for ever.*

The fruits of the paradisal gardens are thus experienced already in this world in the form of all goodness, beauty, and truth, and the diverse modes of happiness flowing therefrom. Every such experience is so much a foretaste of the ultimate blessings of Paradise. On the ethical plane, the performance of good deeds — and still more directly, the realisation of intrinsic virtue, *iḥsān* — is therefore not simply a prerequisite for future salvation, but already a kind of present deliverance: deliverance from the imprisonment of sin on the outward plane, and from the bondage of egocentricity on the inward. This theme of salvation here and now, grounded in unshakeable certitude, is fundamental to the spirit of the Imam's teachings.

[^cite-68]: Cf. al-Sijistānī, *Kashf al-Maḥjūb*, on the distinction between the formal aspect of knowledge (*ʿilm rasmī*) and the *ḥaqīqa* toward which it points, the realisation of which requires the soul's effective integration rather than mere conceptual grasp.
[^cite-69]: Cf. Nāṣir-i Khusraw, *Wajh-i Dīn*, on the principle that the soul cannot be liberated from its own egoism except by a higher principle, namely the support extended through the *daʿwa* (the summons) and ultimately through the First Intellect (*al-ʿAql al-Awwal*).
[^cite-70]: Cf. al-Muʾayyad fī al-Dīn al-Shīrāzī, *al-Majālis al-Muʾayyadiyya*, on *ikhlāṣ* as the precondition by which outward devotion becomes inwardly real, and on the inseparability of true witness (*shahāda*) from the sacrifice of the lower self.

<!-- rescued 130 dropped marker(s) -->
⟪ar:أَوَّلُ العَقل التَّوَدُّدْ⟫ ⟪ar:بالتَّعَلُّم یَنَالَ العِلمْ⟫ ⟪ar:جَمعُہُ الضِّدَّین⟫ ⟪ar:رَاسُ الرَّجَل تَرجُمان عَقلِہ⟫ ⟪ar:فَعَالِمٌ رَبَّانِيٌّ⟫ ⟪ar:لا بُدَّ لَہُ مِن تَرجُماَن⟫ ⟪ar:لا بُدَّا مِنَ التَّرجُمٰن⟫ ⟪ar:وبشِّرُ روح الیقین⟫ ⟪ar:وُد/مَوَدَّۃ⟫ ⟪ar:‏ أَفَمَن يَعْلَمُ أَنَّمَآ أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِن رَّبِّكَ ٱلْحَقُّ كَمَنْ هُوَ أَعْمَىٰٓ ۚ إِنَّمَا يَتَذَكَّرُ أُو۟لُوا۟ ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يُوفُونَ بِعَهْدِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا يَنقُضُونَ ٱلْمِيثَقَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ إِنَّ رَبَّكَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُومُ أَدْنَىٰ مِن ثُلُثَىِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَنِصْفَهُۥ وَثُلُثَهُۥ وَطَآئِفَةٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلَّذِينَ مَعَكَ ۚ وَٱللَّهُ يُقَدِّرُ ٱلَّيْلَ وَٱلنَّهَارَ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن لَّن تُحْصُوهُ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ ٱلْقُرْآنِ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن سَيَكُونُ مِنكُم مَّرْضَىٰ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يَضْرِبُونَ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ يَبْتَغُونَ مِن فَضْلِ ٱللَّهِ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يُقَتِلُونَ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ ۚ وَأَقِيمُوا۟ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ وَآتُوا۟ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَأَقْرِضُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ قَرْضًا حَسَنًۭا ۚ وَمَا تُقَدِّمُوا۟ لِأَنفُسِكُم مِّنْ خَيْرٍۢ تَجِدُوهُ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ هُوَ خَيْرًۭا وَأَعْظَمَ أَجْرًۭا ۚ وَٱسْتَغْفِرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۢ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ وَإِذِ ٱسْتَسْقَىٰ مُوسَىٰ لِقَوْمِهِۦ فَقُلْنَا ٱضْرِب بِّعَصَاكَ ٱلْحَجَرَ ۖ فَٱنفَجَرَتْ مِنْهُ ٱثْنَتَا عَشْرَةَ عَيْنًۭا ۖ قَدْ عَلِمَ كُلُّ أُنَاسٍۢ مَّشْرَبَهُمْ ۖ كُلُوا۟ وَٱشْرَبُوا۟ مِن رِّزْقِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا تَعْثَوْا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ مُفْسِدِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ وَمَآ أُبَرِّئُ نَفْسِىٓ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلنَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌۢ بِٱلسُّوٓءِ إِلَّا مَا رَحِمَ رَبِّىٓ ۚ إِنَّ رَبِّى غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ وَٱكْتُبْ لَنَا فِى هَذِهِ ٱلدُّنْيَا حَسَنَةًۭ وَفِى ٱلْآخِرَةِ إِنَّا هُدْنَآ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ عَذَابِىٓ أُصِيبُ بِهِۦ مَنْ أَشَآءُ ۖ وَرَحْمَتِى وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَىْءٍۢ ۚ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَٱلَّذِينَ هُم بِـَٔايَتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ كُونُوا۟ قَوَّمِينَ بِٱلْقِسْطِ شُهَدَآءَ لِلَّهِ وَلَوْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِكُمْ أَوِ ٱلْوَلِدَيْنِ وَٱلْأَقْرَبِينَ ۚ إِن يَكُنْ غَنِيًّا أَوْ فَقِيرًۭا فَٱللَّهُ أَوْلَىٰ بِهِمَا ۖ فَلَا تَتَّبِعُوا۟ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ أَن تَعْدِلُوا۟ ۚ وَإِن تَلْوُۥٓا۟ أَوْ تُعْرِضُوا۟ فَإِنَّ ٱللَّهَ كَانَ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ ٱللَّهُ نُورُ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ ۚ مَثَلُ نُورِهِۦ كَمِشْكَوٰةٍۢ فِيهَا مِصْبَاحٌ ۖ ٱلْمِصْبَاحُ فِى زُجَاجَةٍ ۖ ٱلزُّجَاجَةُ كَأَنَّهَا كَوْكَبٌۭ دُرِّىٌّۭ يُوقَدُ مِن شَجَرَةٍۢ مُّبَرَكَةٍۢ زَيْتُونَةٍۢ لَّا شَرْقِيَّةٍۢ وَلَا غَرْبِيَّةٍۢ يَكَادُ زَيْتُهَا يُضِىٓءُ وَلَوْ لَمْ تَمْسَسْهُ نَارٌۭ ۚ نُّورٌ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ ۗ يَهْدِى ٱللَّهُ لِنُورِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَيَضْرِبُ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْأَمْثَلَ لِلنَّاسِ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎ ‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎ ‏رِجَالٌۭ لَّا تُلْهِيهِمْ تِجَرَةٌۭ وَلَا بَيْعٌ عَن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ وَإِقَامِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةِ وَإِيتَآءِ ٱلزَّكَوٰةِ ۙ يَخَافُونَ يَوْمًۭا تَتَقَلَّبُ فِيهِ ٱلْقُلُوبُ وَٱلْأَبْصَرُ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ أَفَأَنتَ تَكُونُ عَلَيْهِ وَكِيلًا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ ٱلَّذِى يُكَذِّبُ بِٱلدِّينِ ‎ ‏فَذَلِكَ ٱلَّذِى يَدُعُّ ٱلْيَتِيمَ ‎ ‏وَلَا يَحُضُّ عَلَىٰ طَعَامِ ٱلْمِسْكِينِ ‎ ‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎ ‏وَيَمْنَعُونَ ٱلْمَاعُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ ٱلَّذِى يُكَذِّبُ بِٱلدِّينِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏أَفَلَمْ يَسِيرُوا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ فَتَكُونَ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ يَعْقِلُونَ بِهَآ أَوْ آذَانٌۭ يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَا ۖ فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَعْمَى ٱلْأَبْصَرُ وَلَكِن تَعْمَى ٱلْقُلُوبُ ٱلَّتِى فِى ٱلصُّدُورِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏أَفَمَن شَرَحَ ٱللَّهُ صَدْرَهُۥ لِلْإِسْلَمِ فَهُوَ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ مِّن رَّبِّهِۦ ۚ فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْقَسِيَةِ قُلُوبُهُم مِّن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ فِى ضَلَلٍۢ مُّبِينٍ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ عَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏أُو۟لَٓئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَتٌۭ مِّن رَّبِّهِمْ وَرَحْمَةٌۭ ۖ وَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْمُهْتَدُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِلَّآ أَن يَشَآءَ ٱللَّهُ ۚ وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ إِذَا نَسِيتَ وَقُلْ عَسَىٰٓ أَن يَهْدِيَنِ رَبِّى لِأَقْرَبَ مِنْ هَذَا رَشَدًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلصَّبْرِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱخْتِلَفِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَٱلنَّهَارِ لَآيَتٍۢ لِّأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يَذْكُرُونَ ٱللَّهَ قِيَمًۭا وَقُعُودًۭا وَعَلَىٰ جُنُوبِهِمْ وَيَتَفَكَّرُونَ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ رَبَّنَا مَا خَلَقْتَ هَذَا بَطِلًۭا سُبْحَنَكَ فَقِنَا عَذَابَ ٱلنَّارِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى ذَلِكَ لَذِكْرَىٰ لِمَن كَانَ لَهُۥ قَلْبٌ أَوْ أَلْقَى ٱلسَّمْعَ وَهُوَ شَهِيدٌۭ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ ٱلْأَبْرَارَ يَشْرَبُونَ مِن كَأْسٍۢ كَانَ مِزَاجُهَا كَافُورًا ‎ ‏عَيْنًۭا يَشْرَبُ بِهَا عِبَادُ ٱللَّهِ يُفَجِّرُونَهَا تَفْجِيرًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَفِى خُسْرٍ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَعْطَيْنَكَ ٱلْكَوْثَرَ ‎ ‏فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَٱنْحَرْ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنَّمَا ٱلْمُؤْمِنُونَ ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَا ذُكِرَ ٱللَّهُ وَجِلَتْ قُلُوبُهُمْ وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ آيَتُهُۥ زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَنًۭا وَعَلَىٰ رَبِّهِمْ يَتَوَكَّلُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنَّنِىٓ أَنَا ٱللَّهُ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّآ أَنَا۠ فَٱعْبُدْنِى وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ لِذِكْرِىٓ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْىٌۭ يُوحَىٰ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏إِنْ هِىَ إِلَّآ أَسْمَآءٌۭ سَمَّيْتُمُوهَآ أَنتُمْ وَآبَآؤُكُم مَّآ أَنزَلَ ٱللَّهُ بِهَا مِن سُلْطَنٍ ۚ إِن يَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا ٱلظَّنَّ وَمَا تَهْوَى ٱلْأَنفُسُ ۖ وَلَقَدْ جَآءَهُم مِّن رَّبِّهِمُ ٱلْهُدَىٰٓ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏تُسَبِّحُ لَهُ ٱلسَّمَوَتُ ٱلسَّبْعُ وَٱلْأَرْضُ وَمَن فِيهِنَّ ۚ وَإِن مِّن شَىْءٍ إِلَّا يُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِهِۦ وَلَكِن لَّا تَفْقَهُونَ تَسْبِيحَهُمْ ۗ إِنَّهُۥ كَانَ حَلِيمًا غَفُورًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ثُمَّ جَعَلَ نَسْلَهُۥ مِن سُلَلَةٍۢ مِّن مَّآءٍۢ مَّهِينٍۢ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةَ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنسَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِلَّا مَا شَآءَ ٱللَّهُ ۚ إِنَّهُۥ يَعْلَمُ ٱلْجَهْرَ وَمَا يَخْفَىٰ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فَأَقِمْ وَجْهَكَ لِلدِّينِ حَنِيفًۭا ۚ فِطْرَتَ ٱللَّهِ ٱلَّتِى فَطَرَ ٱلنَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا ۚ لَا تَبْدِيلَ لِخَلْقِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ ٱلدِّينُ ٱلْقَيِّمُ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ ٱلنَّاسِ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فَإِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فَإِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فَذَلِكَ ٱلَّذِى يَدُعُّ ٱلْيَتِيمَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فَلَمْ تَقْتُلُوهُمْ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ قَتَلَهُمْ ۚ وَمَا رَمَيْتَ إِذْ رَمَيْتَ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ رَمَىٰ ۚ وَلِيُبْلِىَ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْهُ بَلَآءً حَسَنًا ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏فِى قُلُوبِهِم مَّرَضٌۭ فَزَادَهُمُ ٱللَّهُ مَرَضًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا كَانُوا۟ يَكْذِبُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏قَالَ وَمَن يَقْنَطُ مِن رَّحْمَةِ رَبِّهِۦٓ إِلَّا ٱلضَّآلُّونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏قُلِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ أَوِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱلرَّحْمَنَ ۖ أَيًّۭا مَّا تَدْعُوا۟ فَلَهُ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ ۚ وَلَا تَجْهَرْ بِصَلَاتِكَ وَلَا تُخَافِتْ بِهَا وَٱبْتَغِ بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ سَبِيلًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ ٱللَّهَ فَٱتَّبِعُونِى يُحْبِبْكُمُ ٱللَّهُ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ ذُنُوبَكُمْ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِنَّ صَلَاتِى وَنُسُكِى وَمَحْيَاىَ وَمَمَاتِى لِلَّهِ رَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏كَلَّآ إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَيَطْغَىٰٓ ‎ ‏أَن رَّآهُ ٱسْتَغْنَىٰٓ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏كَلَّا ۖ بَلْۜ رَانَ عَلَىٰ قُلُوبِهِم مَّا كَانُوا۟ يَكْسِبُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎ ‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏لَن يَنَالَ ٱللَّهَ لُحُومُهَا وَلَا دِمَآؤُهَا وَلَكِن يَنَالُهُ ٱلتَّقْوَىٰ مِنكُمْ ۚ كَذَلِكَ سَخَّرَهَا لَكُمْ لِتُكَبِّرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عَلَىٰ مَا هَدَىٰكُمْ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلْمُحْسِنِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏لَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَن تَبْتَغُوا۟ فَضْلًۭا مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ ۚ فَإِذَآ أَفَضْتُم مِّنْ عَرَفَتٍۢ فَٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عِندَ ٱلْمَشْعَرِ ٱلْحَرَامِ ۖ وَٱذْكُرُوهُ كَمَا هَدَىٰكُمْ وَإِن كُنتُم مِّن قَبْلِهِۦ لَمِنَ ٱلضَّآلِّينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏مَا ٱتَّخَذَ ٱللَّهُ مِن وَلَدٍۢ وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُۥ مِنْ إِلَهٍ ۚ إِذًۭا لَّذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهٍۭ بِمَا خَلَقَ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَىٰ بَعْضٍۢ ۚ سُبْحَنَ ٱللَّهِ عَمَّا يَصِفُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ،⟫ ⟪ar:‏مَّن كَانَ يُرِيدُ ٱلْعَاجِلَةَ عَجَّلْنَا لَهُۥ فِيهَا مَا نَشَآءُ لِمَن نُّرِيدُ ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَا لَهُۥ جَهَنَّمَ يَصْلَىٰهَا مَذْمُومًۭا مَّدْحُورًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏مُّحَمَّدٌۭ رَّسُولُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَٱلَّذِينَ مَعَهُۥٓ أَشِدَّآءُ عَلَى ٱلْكُفَّارِ رُحَمَآءُ بَيْنَهُمْ ۖ تَرَىٰهُمْ رُكَّعًۭا سُجَّدًۭا يَبْتَغُونَ فَضْلًۭا مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ وَرِضْوَنًۭا ۖ سِيمَاهُمْ فِى وُجُوهِهِم مِّنْ أَثَرِ ٱلسُّجُودِ ۚ ذَلِكَ مَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلتَّوْرَىٰةِ ۚ وَمَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلْإِنجِيلِ كَزَرْعٍ أَخْرَجَ شَطْـَٔهُۥ فَـَٔازَرَهُۥ فَٱسْتَغْلَظَ فَٱسْتَوَىٰ عَلَىٰ سُوقِهِۦ يُعْجِبُ ٱلزُّرَّاعَ لِيَغِيظَ بِهِمُ ٱلْكُفَّارَ ۗ وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ مِنْهُم مَّغْفِرَةًۭ وَأَجْرًا عَظِيمًۢا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏هَلْ أَتَىٰ عَلَى ٱلْإِنسَنِ حِينٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلدَّهْرِ لَمْ يَكُن شَيْـًۭٔا مَّذْكُورًا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏هُوَ ٱلْأَوَّلُ وَٱلْآخِرُ وَٱلظَّهِرُ وَٱلْبَاطِنُ ۖ وَهُوَ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَى ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎ ‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَى ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَسَيُجَنَّبُهَا ٱلْأَتْقَى ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى يُؤْتِى مَالَهُۥ يَتَزَكَّىٰ ‎ ‏وَمَا لِأَحَدٍ عِندَهُۥ مِن نِّعْمَةٍۢ تُجْزَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱبْتِغَآءَ وَجْهِ رَبِّهِ ٱلْأَعْلَىٰ ‎ ‏وَلَسَوْفَ يَرْضَىٰ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَشَرَوْهُ بِثَمَنٍۭ بَخْسٍۢ دَرَهِمَ مَعْدُودَةٍۢ وَكَانُوا۟ فِيهِ مِنَ ٱلزَّهِدِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَٱلْمُؤْمِنَتِ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ خَلِدِينَ فِيهَا وَمَسَكِنَ طَيِّبَةًۭ فِى جَنَّتِ عَدْنٍۢ ۚ وَرِضْوَنٌۭ مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُوَ ٱلْفَوْزُ ٱلْعَظِيمُ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَى ٱلثَّلَثَةِ ٱلَّذِينَ خُلِّفُوا۟ حَتَّىٰٓ إِذَا ضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلْأَرْضُ بِمَا رَحُبَتْ وَضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَظَنُّوٓا۟ أَن لَّا مَلْجَأَ مِنَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَّآ إِلَيْهِ ثُمَّ تَابَ عَلَيْهِمْ لِيَتُوبُوٓا۟ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ هُوَ ٱلتَّوَّابُ ٱلرَّحِيمُ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ ٱلْأَسْمَآءَ كُلَّهَا ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى ٱلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ فَقَالَ أَنۢبِـُٔونِى بِأَسْمَآءِ هَٓؤُلَآءِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَدِقِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَقُلْ جَآءَ ٱلْحَقُّ وَزَهَقَ ٱلْبَطِلُ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلْبَطِلَ كَانَ زَهُوقًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ ٱلَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا۟ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ أَمْوَتًۢا ۚ بَلْ أَحْيَآءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَقْرَبُوا۟ مَالَ ٱلْيَتِيمِ إِلَّا بِٱلَّتِى هِىَ أَحْسَنُ حَتَّىٰ يَبْلُغَ أَشُدَّهُۥ ۚ وَأَوْفُوا۟ بِٱلْعَهْدِ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلْعَهْدَ كَانَ مَسْـُٔولًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَا يَحُضُّ عَلَىٰ طَعَامِ ٱلْمِسْكِينِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيرًۭا مِّنَ ٱلْجِنِّ وَٱلْإِنسِ ۖ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ لَّا يَفْقَهُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌۭ لَّا يُبْصِرُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌۭ لَّا يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَآ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ كَٱلْأَنْعَمِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْغَفِلُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَمَّا جَآءَ مُوسَىٰ لِمِيقَتِنَا وَكَلَّمَهُۥ رَبُّهُۥ قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِىٓ أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ لَن تَرَىٰنِى وَلَكِنِ ٱنظُرْ إِلَى ٱلْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ ٱسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُۥ فَسَوْفَ تَرَىٰنِى ۚ فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّىٰ رَبُّهُۥ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُۥ دَكًّۭا وَخَرَّ مُوسَىٰ صَعِقًۭا ۚ فَلَمَّآ أَفَاقَ قَالَ سُبْحَنَكَ تُبْتُ إِلَيْكَ وَأَنَا۠ أَوَّلُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُۥ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌۢ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَنَبْلُوَنَّكُم بِشَىْءٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْخَوْفِ وَٱلْجُوعِ وَنَقْصٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْأَمْوَلِ وَٱلْأَنفُسِ وَٱلثَّمَرَتِ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلصَّبِرِينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَآ أَصَبَتْهُم مُّصِيبَةٌۭ قَالُوٓا۟ إِنَّا لِلَّهِ وَإِنَّآ إِلَيْهِ رَجِعُونَ ‎ ‏أُو۟لَٓئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَتٌۭ مِّن رَّبِّهِمْ وَرَحْمَةٌۭ ۖ وَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْمُهْتَدُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلَنَبْلُوَنَّكُم بِشَىْءٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْخَوْفِ وَٱلْجُوعِ وَنَقْصٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْأَمْوَلِ وَٱلْأَنفُسِ وَٱلثَّمَرَتِ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلصَّبِرِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ فَٱدْعُوهُ بِهَا ۖ وَذَرُوا۟ ٱلَّذِينَ يُلْحِدُونَ فِىٓ أَسْمَٓئِهِۦ ۚ سَيُجْزَوْنَ مَا كَانُوا۟ يَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْمَشْرِقُ وَٱلْمَغْرِبُ ۚ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا۟ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ وَسِعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَمَا هَذِهِ ٱلْحَيَوٰةُ ٱلدُّنْيَآ إِلَّا لَهْوٌۭ وَلَعِبٌۭ ۚ وَإِنَّ ٱلدَّارَ ٱلْآخِرَةَ لَهِىَ ٱلْحَيَوَانُ ۚ لَوْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْىٌۭ يُوحَىٰ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎ ‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَنَفْسٍۢ وَمَا سَوَّىٰهَا ‎ ‏فَأَلْهَمَهَا فُجُورَهَا وَتَقْوَىٰهَا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَيُطْعِمُونَ ٱلطَّعَامَ عَلَىٰ حُبِّهِۦ مِسْكِينًۭا وَيَتِيمًۭا وَأَسِيرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّمَا نُطْعِمُكُمْ لِوَجْهِ ٱللَّهِ لَا نُرِيدُ مِنكُمْ جَزَآءًۭ وَلَا شُكُورًا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَيْلٌۭ لِّكُلِّ هُمَزَةٍۢ لُّمَزَةٍ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى جَمَعَ مَالًۭا وَعَدَّدَهُۥ ‎ ‏يَحْسَبُ أَنَّ مَالَهُۥٓ أَخْلَدَهُۥ ‎ ‏كَلَّا ۖ لَيُنۢبَذَنَّ فِى ٱلْحُطَمَةِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ فِى نَفْسِكَ تَضَرُّعًۭا وَخِيفَةًۭ وَدُونَ ٱلْجَهْرِ مِنَ ٱلْقَوْلِ بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ وَلَا تَكُن مِّنَ ٱلْغَفِلِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ وَتَبَتَّلْ إِلَيْهِ تَبْتِيلًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَٱعْبُدْ رَبَّكَ حَتَّىٰ يَأْتِيَكَ ٱلْيَقِينُ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَٱللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا جَلَّىٰهَا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّيْلِ إِذَا يَغْشَىٰ ‎ ‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا تَجَلَّىٰ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْعَصْرِ ‎ ‏إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَفِى خُسْرٍ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلصَّبْرِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏يَوْمَ هُم بَرِزُونَۖ لَا يَخْفَىٰ عَلَى ٱللَّهِ مِنْهُمْ شَىْءٌۭۚ لِّمَنِ ٱلْمُلْكُ ٱلْيَوْمَۖ لِلَّهِ ٱلْوَحِدِ ٱلْقَهَّارِ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎ ‏ٱرْجِعِىٓ إِلَىٰ رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةًۭ مَّرْضِيَّةًۭ ‎ ‏فَٱدْخُلِى فِى عِبَدِى ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ لَا تُلْهِكُمْ أَمْوَلُكُمْ وَلَآ أَوْلَدُكُمْ عَن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ فَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْخَسِرُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ذِكْرًۭا كَثِيرًۭا ‎ ‏وَسَبِّحُوهُ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًا ‎ ‏هُوَ ٱلَّذِى يُصَلِّى عَلَيْكُمْ وَمَلَٓئِكَتُهُۥ لِيُخْرِجَكُم مِّنَ ٱلظُّلُمَتِ إِلَى ٱلنُّورِۚ وَكَانَ بِٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَحِيمًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ذِكْرًۭا كَثِيرًۭا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱسْتَجِيبُوا۟ لِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ إِذَا دَعَاكُمْ لِمَا يُحْيِيكُمْ ۖ وَٱعْلَمُوٓا۟ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يَحُولُ بَيْنَ ٱلْمَرْءِ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَأَنَّهُۥٓ إِلَيْهِ تُحْشَرُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوٓا۟ أَطِيعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا۟ ٱلرَّسُولَ وَأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَمْرِ مِنكُمْ ۖ فَإِن تَنَزَعْتُمْ فِى شَىْءٍۢ فَرُدُّوهُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِ وَٱلرَّسُولِ إِن كُنتُمْ تُؤْمِنُونَ بِٱللَّهِ وَٱلْيَوْمِ ٱلْآخِرِ ۚ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَحْسَنُ تَأْوِيلًا ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱتْلُ مَآ أُوحِىَ إِلَيْكَ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَبِ وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ تَنْهَىٰ عَنِ ٱلْفَحْشَآءِ وَٱلْمُنكَرِ ۗ وَلَذِكْرُ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ مَا تَصْنَعُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱدْعُوا۟ رَبَّكُمْ تَضَرُّعًۭا وَخُفْيَةً ۚ إِنَّهُۥ لَا يُحِبُّ ٱلْمُعْتَدِينَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱسْتَحْوَذَ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلشَّيْطَنُ فَأَنسَىٰهُمْ ذِكْرَ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ حِزْبُ ٱلشَّيْطَنِ ۚ أَلَآ إِنَّ حِزْبَ ٱلشَّيْطَنِ هُمُ ٱلْخَسِرُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱللَّهُ نَزَّلَ أَحْسَنَ ٱلْحَدِيثِ كِتَبًۭا مُّتَشَبِهًۭا مَّثَانِىَ تَقْشَعِرُّ مِنْهُ جُلُودُ ٱلَّذِينَ يَخْشَوْنَ رَبَّهُمْ ثُمَّ تَلِينُ جُلُودُهُمْ وَقُلُوبُهُمْ إِلَىٰ ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُدَى ٱللَّهِ يَهْدِى بِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَمَن يُضْلِلِ ٱللَّهُ فَمَا لَهُۥ مِنْ هَادٍ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِىٓ أَحْسَنَ كُلَّ شَىْءٍ خَلَقَهُۥ ۖ وَبَدَأَ خَلْقَ ٱلْإِنسَنِ مِن طِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ جَعَلَ نَسْلَهُۥ مِن سُلَلَةٍۢ مِّن مَّآءٍۢ مَّهِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةَ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِىٓ أَحْسَنَ كُلَّ شَىْءٍ خَلَقَهُۥ ۖ وَبَدَأَ خَلْقَ ٱلْإِنسَنِ مِن طِينٍۢ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَتَطْمَىِٕنُّ قُلُوبُهُم بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۗ أَلَا بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ تَطْمَىِٕنُّ ٱلْقُلُوبُ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَآ أَصَبَتْهُم مُّصِيبَةٌۭ قَالُوٓا۟ إِنَّا لِلَّهِ وَإِنَّآ إِلَيْهِ رَجِعُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَلَىٰ صَلَاتِهِمْ دَآئِمُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎⟫ ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎⟫
